Waqf — Endowment
intermediate
8 min
The Nature of Waqf: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Ownership Transfer
Defines waqf and presents intra-Hanafi dispute on ownership.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on waqf ownership transfer and explain why the Sahibayn's view became mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Waqf is valid by consensus; the dispute is whether ownership transfers to Allah or remains, with practical consequences on revocability.

This passage from Ashraf al-Bidaya (commentary on al-Hidayah) defines waqf and presents the well-known intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The school ultimately favors the Sahibayn's binding view, but understanding Abu Hanifa's original position is essential for grasping the legal evolution of waqf in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
State each imam's view on whether the waqif's ownership ceases. Abu Hanifa: ownership remains, waqf is revocable. Abu Yusuf: ownership ceases immediately by utterance. Muhammad: ownership ceases only upon delivery to trustee.
2
Examine Abu Hanifa's dalil
List his proofs: hadith 'La habsa 'an fara'id Allah', report of Shuraih that the Prophet sold a habs, and analogy to ariyah (loan).
3
Examine the Sahibayn's dalil
List their proofs: hadith of Umar (the Prophet said 'Give charity from its principle, it is not sold, inherited, or gifted') and qiyas to mosque, which is made purely for Allah.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Explain how Abu Hanifa rebuts the Sahibayn's evidence: the Umar hadith is about sadaqah, not waqf; the Prophet's instruction was irshad, not hukm; waqf is distinguishable from mosque because human rights remain.
5
Determine the tarjih
Explain why later scholars (Ibn al-Humam, al-Marghinani) preferred the Sahibayn's view: the Umar hadith is stronger in transmission and the qiyas to mosque is more appropriate for ensuring perpetual reward. State the mufta bihi.

Source Text

كتاب الوقف
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ہفتم عَلَى وَجْةٍ تَعُودُ مَنَفَعَتُهُ إِلَى الْعِبَادِ فَيَلْزَمُ وَلَا تُبَاعُ وَلَا يُرْهَنُ وَلَا يُورَثُ وَاللَّفْظُ يَنتَظِمُهُما والترجيح بالدليل لَهُمَا قَوْل النَّبِي لِعُمَرَ حِينَ أَرَادَ انَ يَتَصَدَّقَ بِأَرْضِ لَهُ تُدْعَى ثَمْغَ تَصَدَّقُ بِأَصْلِهَا لَايْبَاعُ وَلَا يُورَثُ وَلَا يُوهَبُ ولأنَّ الحاجةَ ماسَّةٌ إلى أن الوَقْفَ يَلْزَمُ لِيَصِلَ ثَوَابُهُ إِلَيْهِ عَلَى الدَّوَامِ وَقَدْ أَمْكَنَ دَفْعُ حَاجَتِهِ بِإِسْقَاطِ الْمِلْكِ وَجَعْلِهِ لِلهِ تَعَالَى إِذْ لَهُ نَظِيرُ فِى الشَّرْعِ وَهُوَ الْمَسْجِدُ فَيُجْعَلُ كَذَالِكَ وَلِأَبِي حَنِيفَة قَوْلُهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلام لَا حَبْسَ عَنْ فَرَائِضِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى وَعَنْ شُرَيْحٍ جَاءَ مُحَمَّدٌ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَام يَبيعُ الحَبْسَ وَلِأَنَّ الْمَلكَ بَاقٍ فِيهِ بِدَلِيْل أَنَّهُ يَجُوزُ الانْتِفَاعُ بِه زِرَاعَةً وَسُكْنَى وَغَيْرَ ذَالِكَ وَالْمُلْكُ فِيهِ لِلْوَاقِفِ أَلَا تَرَى أَنَّ لَهُ وَلَايَةُ التَصرُّف فِيْهِ بِصَرْفِ غَلَّاتِه إِلى مَصَارِفِهَا وَنَصْبِ الْقَوَّامِ فِيهَا إِلَّا أَنَّهُ يَتَصَدَّقُ بِمَنَافِعِهِ فَصَارَ شَيْئًا الْعَارِيَةِ وَلِأَنَّهُ يُحْتَاجُ إِلَى التَّصَدُّقِ بِالْغَلَّةِ دَائِمَّا وَلَا تَصَدُّقَ عَنْهُ إِلَّا بِالْبَقَاءِ عَلى مِلْكِهِ وَلِأَنَّهُ لَا يُمْكِنُ أَنْ تُزَالَ مِلْكُهُ لَا إلَى مَالِك لِأَنَّهُ غَيْرُ مَشْرُوع مَعَ بَقَائِهِ كَالسَّائِبَةِ بخلاف الإعتاق لأنه إتلافُ وَبِخِلَافِ الْمَسْجِدِ لِأَنَّهُ جُعِلَ خَالِصًا لِلَّهِ تَعَالَى وَلِهٰذَا لَا يَجُوزُ الإِنْتِفَاعُ بِهِ وَهُهُمَا لَمْ يَنقَطِعْ حَقَّ الْعَبْدِ عَنْهُ فَلَمْ يَصِرْ خَالِصًا لِلَّهِ تَعَالَى قَالَ فِى الْكِتَابِ لَا يَزُولُ مِلكُ الْوَاقِفِ إِلَّا أَنْ يَحْكُم بِهِ الْحَاكِمُ أَو يُعْلِقَهُ بِمَوْتِهِ وَهُذَا فِي حُكْمِ الْحَاكِمِ صَحِيحُ لِأَنَّهُ قَضَاءٌ فِي مُجْتَهَدٍ فِيهِ أَمَّا فِى تَعْلِيقِهِ بِالْمَوْتِ فَالصَّحِيحُ أَنَّهُ لَا يَزُولُ مِلْكُهُ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ تَصَدَّقَ بِمَنَافِعِهِ مُؤَبَّدًا فَيَصِيرُ بِمَنْزِلَةِ الوَصِيَّةِ بِالمَنَافِعِ مُؤَبَّدًا فَيَلْزَمُ وَالْمُرَادُ بِالْحَاكِمِ المَوْلَى فَأَمَّا الْحَكَمِ فَفِيهِ اِخْتِلَافُ الْمَسَائِحِ وَلَوْ وَقَفَ فِي مَرَضِ مَوْتِهِ قَالَ الطَّحَاوِتُ هُوَ بِمَنْزِلَةِ الوَصِيَّةِ بَعْدَ المَوتِ وَالصَّحِيحُ أَنَّهُ لَا يَلْزَمُه عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَعِنْدَهُمَا يَلْزَمُهُ إلّا أنه يعتبر من الثُّلُثِ وَالْوَقْفُ فِى الصّحَةِ مِنْ جَمِيعِ الْمَالِ وَإِذَا كَانَ الْمِلْكُ يَزُولُ عِنْدَهُمَا يَزُولُ بِالْقَوْلِ عِنْدَأَبِى يُوسُفَ وَهُوَ قَولُ الشَّافِعِي بِمَنْزِلَةِ الْإِعْتَاقِ  لِأَنَّهُ إِسْقَاطُ المِلْكِ وَعِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ لَا بُدَّ مِنَ التَّسْلِيمِ إِلَى الْمُتَوَلَّى لِأَنَّهُ حَقَّ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى وَإِنَّمَا يَثْبُتُ حَقُّهُ فِى ضِمْنِ التَّسْلِيمِ إِلَى الْعَبْدِ لِاَنَّ التَّمْلِيكَ مِنَ اللهِ تَعَالَى وَهُوَ مَالِكُ الْأشْيَاء لَا يَتَحَقَّقُ مَقْصُودًا وَقَدْ يَكُونُ تَبْعًا لِغَيْرِهِ فَيَأْخُذُ حُكْمَهُ فَيُنْزَلُ مَنْزِلَةُ الزَّكَوةِ وَالصَّدَقَةِ
و لگانا
و در
ور
ترجمہ ابوحنیفہ رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ وقف کرنے سے واقف کی اس کے مال موقوف پر سے حق ملکیت ختم نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ البتہ اگر کوئی حاکم اس کے ختم ہونے کے بارے میں حکم دے دے یا خود وقف کرنے والا اپنی موت پر اسے معلق کر دے اور یوں کہہ دے کہ جب میں مرجاؤں میں نے اپنا گھر یازمین اس کام کے لئے وقف کر دی ہے۔ اور ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے کہا ہے کہ وقف کرتے ہی اس کی ملکیت اس پر سے ختم ہو جائے گی۔ یعنی اس نے جیسے ہی کہا کہ میں نے اسے وقف کیا وہ گھر اس کی ملکیت سے نکل گیا ۔ اور امام محمد رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے کہا کہ واقف کی ملکیت ختم نہیں ہوئی مگر اس وقت جبکہ وہ کسی دوسرے کو متولی مقرر کر کے اس کے حوالہ کر دے۔ قال الوقف لغة الخ مصنف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ لغت میں وقف کے معنی ہیں جبس کرنا یعنی روک لینا چنا نچہ محاورہ میں بولا جاتا ہے وقفت الدابة ، میں نے اپنا گھوڑا روک لیا۔ اور اوقفتھا بھی اسی معنی میں بولتے ہیں۔ اور شرع میں جس کے معنی امام ابو حنیفہ رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک یہ ہیں کہ مال مین کو وقف کرنے والا اپنے پاس روکے اور اس کے منافع کو صدقہ کر دے جیسے کہ عاریت ہوتی ہے۔ پھر کہا گیا ہے کہ منافع تو معدوم ہوتے ہیں اور کسی معدوم چیز کو صدقہ کرنا صحیح نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے امام اعظم رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک وقف بالکل جائز نہیں ہونا چاہئے ۔ اصل میں یہی الفاظ مذکور ہیں ۔ یعنی امام ابو حنیفہ رحمتہ اللہ علیہ اسے جائز نہیں کہتے تھے ۔ لیکن قول اصح یہ ہے کہ امام

۲۴۵
كتاب الوقف
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد هفتم ابوحنیفہ رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک بھی وقف جائز ہے لیکن بمنزلہ عاریت کے لازم نہیں ہے۔ صاحبین رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک وقف کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ مال عین کو اللہ تعالیٰ کی ملک پر روکنا۔ پس وقف کرنے والے کی ملکیت کا بندہ سے ختم ہو کر اللہ تعالیٰ کی طرف اس طرح منتقل ہو جانا کہ اس کے منافع بندوں ہی کو حاصل ہوں۔ جس سے وقف لازم ہو جائے گا اس کے بعد وہ چیز فروخت نہیں کی جاسکے گی۔ اور نہ ہیبہ ہو سکے گی اور نہ وہ میراث بن سکے گی۔ پس لفظ وقف دونوں قول کو شامل ہے۔ یعنی وقف صحیح ہو جائے گا۔ خواہ ملک ختم ہو یا نہ ہو اور امام صاحب یا صاحبین میں سے ہر ایک کے قول کی ترجیح دلیل سے ہوتی ہے۔ چنانچہ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب حضرت عمر نے اپنے حصہ خیبر کو جس کا نام شمع ( نا کے فتحہ اور میم کے سکون کے ساتھ ) تھا صدقہ کرنا چاہا تو رسول اللہ نے فرمایا کہ اس کی اصل کو صدقہ کر دو تا کہ وہ آئندہ کبھی نہ بیچی جا سکے گی اور نہ میراث بنے گی اور نہ ہیہ ہو سکے گی 2 صحاح ستہ نے اس کی روایت کی ہے)۔ اور اس دلیل سے بھی کہ واقف کو کبھی اس بات کی ضرورت در پیش ہو جاتی ہے کہ اس کا وقف لازم ہو جائے تاکہ قیامت تک کے لئے اسے اس وقف کا ثواب ملتا رہے اور صدقہ جاریہ ہو جائے۔ اور اس ضرورت کے پورے ہونے کی صورت اسی طرح ممکن ہوگی کہ چیز اس کی ملکیت سے باہر کر کے اللہ
تعالیٰ کی ملکیت میں دے دی جائے۔ کیونکہ شریعت میں اس کی نظیر موجود ہے اور وہ مسجد ہے۔ اس طرح وقف بھی کر دیا جائے۔ ابو حنیفہ رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ رسول اللہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ کے فرائض میں سے کوئی چیز ھیں نہیں ہے۔ یعنی ہر چیز میراث کی طرح فرائض الہی میں تقسیم ہو جائے گی۔ اس کی روایت دار قطنی و ابن ابی شیبہ اور طبرانی نے ضعیف اسناد کے ساتھ کی ہے) اور شریح رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے کہا ہے کہ رسول اللہ نے آکر جس کو فروخت کیا ہے ؟ اس کی روایت ابن ابی شیبہ بیتی اور طحاوی نے اسناد صحیح کے ساتھ کی ہے اور اس دلیل سے بھی کہ وقف کرنے والے کی ملکیت وقف میں باقی رہتی ہے۔ جس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ واقف کو موقوفہ زمین سے نفع اٹھانا مثلا زمین میں کھیتی کر کے یا گھر میں رہ کر اور دوسرے طریقوں سے جائز ہے۔ اور وقف کرنے والے کی ملکیت اس میں باقی ہے۔ اسی لئے ہم یہ دیکھتے ہیں کہ اسے وقف میں تصرف کرنے کا پوراحق ہے۔ اور اس کی آمدنی اور پیداوار کو جہاں تصرف کرنا چاہئے کرتا ہے۔ اس وقف کی دیکھ بھال کے لئے متولی اور قیم مقرر کرتا ہے۔ البتہ اس کی پیداوار اور منافع کو صدقہ کر دیتا ہے۔ لہذا یہ وقف عاریت کے مشابہ ہو گیا اور اس دلیل سے کہ وقف کرنے والے کو ہمیشہ اس کی آمدنی کو وقف کرنے کی ضرورت ہے کیونکہ اس کی طرف سے صدقہ اسی صورت میں ہو سکتا ہے جبکہ وہ وقف اس کی ملکیت میں باقی ہو۔ اور اس دلیل سے بھی کہ یہ بات ممکن نہیں ہے کہ موقوف سے واقف کی ملکیت اس طرح ختم کر دی جائے کہ دوسرا اس کا کوئی مالک باقی نہ رہے کیونکہ ایسی صورت شریعت میں ثابت نہیں ہے۔ حالانکہ وہ چیز خود باقی رہتی ہے۔ جیسے جانور سانڈ وغیرہ کو آزاد چھوڑ نا ممنوع ہے۔
بخلاف الاعتاق یعنی غلامی کو ختم کرنیکے خلاف ۔ کیونکہ اس میں مملوکیت کی صفت کو دور کرنا ہوتا ہے۔ اور بخلاف مسجد کے کیونکہ وہ خالصہ اللہ تعالیٰ کے نام کی کر دی جاتی ہے۔ اس لئے مسجد سے نفع اٹھانا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور وقف کی صورت میں بندہ کا حق وقف سے ختم نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ اسی لئے وقف خالصہ اللہ تعالیٰ کے نام کا نہیں ہوتا ہے )۔ پھر ترجیح میں علماء نے کلام کیا ہے۔ ابن الہام رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے کہا ہے کہ حضرت عمر کے وقف میں رسول اللہ نے حکم دے دیا تھا۔ اس لئے وہ وقف لازم ہو گیا)۔
( میں مترجم کہتا ہوں کہ نہیں حکم نہیں فرمایا تھا بلکہ صرف ارشاد فرمایا تھا۔ شیخ الاسلام رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے مبسوط کی شرح میں کہا ہے کہ امام ابو حنیفہ رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کی نقلی دلیل میں کوئی حجت نہیں ہے کیونکہ جب واقف نے وقف کر دیا تو فرائض الہی یعنی میراث کا اس سے کوئی تعلق
Book of Waqf. Ashraf al-Bidaya, Urdu commentary of al-Hidayah, volume 7. [Definition of waqf: keeping the property in a way that its benefit returns to the people, so it becomes binding, and it is not sold, not pawned, not inherited. The word [waqf] encompasses both [opinions]. And preference is by evidence for them [the two disciples]. The statement of the Prophet to Umar when he wanted to give charity from a land of his called Thamgh: 'Give charity from its principle, it is not sold, not inherited, not gifted.' And because the need is pressing that the waqf be binding so that its reward reaches him continuously, and it is possible to fulfill his need by removing ownership and making it for Allah Almighty, since there is an analogy in the law, which is the mosque, so it is made likewise. And for Abu Hanifa: his statement, peace be upon him, 'No habs (waqf) regarding the divinely ordained shares of Allah Almighty' and from Shuraih: 'Muhammad, peace be upon him, came selling the habs.' And because ownership remains in it by evidence that it is permissible to benefit from it by cultivation, residence, and other than that, and ownership in it is for the waqif. Do you not see that he has the authority of disposition in it by spending its revenues to their destinations and appointing a caretaker over it? However, he gives charity from its benefits, so it becomes like a loan (ariyah). And because there is a constant need to give charity from the yield, and charity from him is only possible by remaining in his ownership. And because it is not possible that his ownership be removed, not to any owner, because it is not legislated while [the property] remains, like the sa'ibah (released animal). Contrary to emancipation (itlaq) because it is destruction. And contrary to the mosque because it is made purely for Allah Almighty, and therefore it is not permissible to benefit from it. And in [waqf], the right of the servant is not cut off from it, so it does not become purely for Allah Almighty. He said in the book: The ownership of the waqif does not cease unless a judge rules so, or he ties it to his death. And this with the ruling of a judge is valid because it is a judgment in [a matter of] ijtihad. As for tying it to death, the correct view is that his ownership does not cease, but he gives charity from its benefits perpetually, so it becomes like a will of benefits perpetually, so it is binding. And what is meant by 'al-hakim' is the ruler (al-mawla). As for the arbitrator (al-hakam), there is a difference of [؟] in the issues. And if he makes a waqf in his death-sickness, al-Tahawi said it is like a will after death. And the correct view is that it is not binding upon him according to Abu Hanifa, and according to them [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] it is binding upon him, but it is considered from the third. And waqf during health is from all of the wealth. And when ownership ceases according to them, it ceases by the statement according to Abu Yusuf, and it is the statement of al-Shafi'i, like emancipation because it is removal of ownership. And according to Muhammad, there must be delivery (taslim) to the trustee (mutawalli) because it is a right of Allah Almighty, and indeed his right is established within the delivery to the servant, because making something property (tamlik) from Allah Almighty—and He is the Owner of all things—cannot be realized as a primary objective, but it may be secondary to something else, so it takes its ruling, so it is treated like zakat and sadaqah. [Then Urdu translation and commentary follows, repeating and explaining the above positions, proofs, and disagreements in detail.]
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the nature of waqf (endowment). The commentary (Ashraf al-Bidaya) explains that linguistically waqf means 'to detain' (habs). Legally, there is disagreement. According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), waqf means detaining the property (al-'ayn) under the ownership of Allah such that the waqif's ownership ceases, the property cannot be sold, pawned, or inherited, and its benefits go to the people. This makes waqf binding (lazim). Their primary proof is the hadith of Umar: the Prophet instructed him to give charity from the land's original property so it would never be sold, inherited, or gifted. They also argue by qiyas to a mosque, which is made purely for Allah, so waqf should be similarly transferred to Allah's ownership to ensure continuity of reward. Abu Hanifa, however, holds that the waqif's ownership does not cease, likening waqf to ariyah (loan). The property remains in his ownership, but its benefits are given as sadaqah. He cites the hadith 'La habsa 'an fara'id Allah' (no detention regarding the obligatory shares of Allah) and the report of Shuraih that the Prophet sold a habs. He also argues that because the waqif can still benefit from the property (e.g., cultivate, reside), ownership persists. He distinguishes waqf from a mosque and from emancipation. The text then details the intra-Hanafi differences: Abu Hanifa says ownership does not cease unless a judge rules or it is tied to death (then like a will). Abu Yusuf says ownership ceases immediately by utterance, like emancipation. Muhammad says it ceases only upon delivery to a trustee. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is disputed; later scholars like Ibn al-Humam support the Sahibayn's view based on the strength of the hadith of Umar. The Urdu commentary elaborates each proof and indicates that despite Abu Hanifa's earlier view, the correct position (qawl asahh) is that waqf is valid and binding in the school, with the Sahibayn's definition prevailing for fatwa.

Key Terms
وقف (waqf): Linguistically: to detain (habs). Legally: detaining a property such that its ownership is either transferred to Allah (Sahibayn) or remains with the waqif but benefits are given as sadaqah (Abu Hanifa).
حابس (habs): A synonym for waqf; used in early sources. Literally: detaining. The Prophet's hadith uses 'habs'.
عاریة (ariyah): A loan of a benefit without ownership transfer. Abu Hanifa likens waqf to ariyah because the waqif retains ownership but lends the benefits.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school, what happens to the waqif's ownership upon making a valid waqf?
A) Ownership remains with the waqif permanently.
B) Ownership is transferred to Allah (i.e., the waqif ceases to own it).
C) Ownership passes to the beneficiaries.
D) Ownership is destroyed and the property becomes ownerless.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's operative position is that waqf transfers ownership to Allah, making it binding and perpetual.

The Binding Nature of Waqf: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on waqf binding

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the binding nature of waqf and identify the mufta bihi position with its evidence.

Core Idea
Though Abu Hanifa held waqf revocable, the mufta bihi position makes it binding.

This passage presents the ikhtilaf between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, on whether waqf is binding. Understanding this dispute reveals how the Hanafi school evolved and how later authorities weighed evidence to settle the issue.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
Identify the core disagreement: Abu Hanifa holds waqf is valid but revocable (like ariyah); Sahibayn hold it is binding and irrevocable, with ownership transferring to Allah.
2
Examine the Sahibayn's evidence
Analyze the hadith of Umar's waqf where the Prophet said 'Make its original property a sadaqah so it may never be sold, inherited, or gifted.' Also consider their analogy with a mosque and the need for bindingness to secure ongoing reward.
This hadith is recorded in the six authentic collections.
3
Examine Abu Hanifa's evidence
Look at Abu Hanifa's dalils: the weak hadith 'There is no withholding from Allah's obligations', the hadith of Shurayh about selling, and rational arguments based on the waqf-maker retaining benefit and control, similar to ariyah.
The hadith of Shurayh is considered sound, but its application is contested.
4
Analyze the rebuttals and counter-arguments
Study the commentator's responses: the hadith of Umar is a permission not a command; the hadith of Shurayh only abrogates pagan practices; the analogy with mosque is imperfect because waqf benefits are for people, not exclusively for Allah.
Shaykh al-Islam argues that Abu Hanifa's transmitted evidence is weak because waqf has no connection with inheritance.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its authority
Conclude that later scholars (Ibn al-Humam, Shaykh al-Islam, and mashayikh) prefer the Sahibayn's view. The fatwa is upon waqf being binding. Recognize the authority weight: Zahir al-Riwayah records Sahibayn's view as the relied-upon position.
This shows that ikhtilaf within the school is resolved by tarjih based on evidence and widespread practice.

( میں مترجم کہتا ہوں کہ نہیں حکم نہیں فرمایا تھا بلکہ صرف ارشاد فرمایا تھا۔ شیخ الاسلام رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے مبسوط کی شرح میں کہا ہے کہ امام ابو حنیفہ رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کی نقلی دلیل میں کوئی حجت نہیں ہے کیونکہ جب واقف نے وقف کر دیا تو فرائض الہی یعنی میراث کا اس سے کوئی تعلق نہیں رہا اس لئے فرائض الہی سے کوئی جبس نہیں ہوا۔ جیسے مال منقولہ و وصیت و ہبہ وصدقہ میں کوئی جس نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ شیخ الاسلام نے طویل کلام کرنے کے بعد فرمایا ہے کہ اس مقام میں حق بات یہی ہے کہ صاحبین و عالمہ علماء کے قول کمر ترجیح ہے۔ یعنی وقف لازم ہو جاتا ہے۔ کیونکہ اس بحث میں بہت سی حدیثیں وارد ہوئی ہیں۔ اور صحابہ وتابعین اور ان کے بعد عام امت کا بھی اس پر عمل چلا آتا ہے۔ اور حدیث شریح کے صرف یہی معنی ہیں کہ کفار جو اپنے زمانہ میں عام وبحیرہ وغیرہ کو بتوں کے نام کر دیتے اسے رسول اللہ نے منسوخ کر دیا۔ اسی لئے بعض مشائخ رحمتہ اللہ علیہم نے کہا ہے کہ صاحبین رحمتہ اللہ علیہا کے قول پر ہی فتوی ہے۔ میں مترجم کہتا ہوں کہ یہی قول مختار اور اوفق ہے۔ واللہ تعالی اعلم ۔
Book of Waqf. According to Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him), waqf is permissible but like ariyah (loan) it is not binding. According to the Sahibayn (may Allah have mercy on them), the meaning of waqf is to detain the 'ayn (corpus) of property in the ownership of Allah Most High, so that the ownership of the waqf-maker is severed from it and transferred to Allah in such a way that its benefits accrue to the servants. As a result, the waqf becomes binding. After that, the property cannot be sold, nor given as a gift, nor inherited. So the word waqf encompasses both statements: the waqf is valid whether ownership is severed or not. And the preference of the statement of Imam (Abu Hanifa) or the Sahibayn is determined by evidence. The evidence of the Sahibayn is: When Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) wanted to give in charity his share of Khaybar which was called Sham' (with fathah on the noon and sukun on the meem), the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Make its original property a sadaqah so that it may never be sold, nor inherited, nor given as a gift.' (Related by the six authentic collections). And also by the evidence that the waqf-maker sometimes faces the need that his waqf be binding so that he may continue to receive its reward until the Day of Resurrection and it becomes an ongoing charity. And the fulfillment of this need is only possible if the property is removed from his ownership and given into the ownership of Allah, because there is a precedent for this in the Shari'ah, and that is the mosque. So waqf should also be made binding. The evidence of Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) is: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'There is no withholding of anything from the obligatory shares of Allah.' That is, everything will be distributed like inheritance according to divine shares. (This was related by Dar Qutni, Ibn Abi Shaybah, and Tabarani with a weak chain.) And Shurayh (may Allah have mercy on him) said: 'What did the Messenger of Allah sell that He bought?' (This was related by Ibn Abi Shaybah, Bayhaqi, and Tahawi with a sound chain.) And also by the evidence that the ownership of the waqf-maker remains in the waqf. The proof of this is that it is permissible for the waqf-maker to derive benefit from the waqf land, such as cultivating it, living in the house, and other ways. And his ownership remains in it. For this reason, we see that he has full right to dispose of the waqf. He spends its income and produce wherever he wishes. He appoints a mutawalli and a nazir for its care. However, he gives away its produce and benefits as sadaqah. Hence, this waqf resembles ariyah (loan). And also by the evidence that the waqf-maker always needs to dedicate its income to the waqf because his sadaqah can only occur if the waqf remains in his ownership. And also by the evidence that it is not possible that the ownership of the waqf-maker be severed from the waqf property in such a way that no other owner remains, because such a situation is not established in the Shari'ah, although the property itself remains. For example, releasing an animal like a bull is prohibited. Contrary to itq (manumission), because in that, the attribute of being owned is removed. And contrary to the mosque, because it is made exclusively for the name of Allah. Hence, deriving benefit from a mosque is not permissible. And in the case of waqf, the right of the servant is not terminated from the waqf; therefore, waqf is not exclusively for the name of Allah). Then scholars spoke about preference. Ibn al-Humam (may Allah have mercy on him) said: 'In the waqf of Umar, the Messenger of Allah gave a command; therefore, that waqf became binding.' (I, the translator, say: No, he did not command; rather, he only indicated.) Shaykh al-Islam (may Allah have mercy on him) said in the commentary of al-Mabsut: 'There is no proof in the transmission-based evidence of Imam Abu Hanifa, because when the waqf-maker makes a waqf, it has no connection with the obligatory shares of Allah (inheritance), so no withholding occurs. As there is no withholding in movable property, will, gift, or sadaqah.' After a lengthy discussion, Shaykh al-Islam said: 'The truth in this place is that the statement of the Sahibayn and the majority of scholars is preferable, i.e., waqf becomes binding. Because many hadiths have been transmitted on this issue, and the Companions, Successors, and the general ummah after them have continuously acted upon it. And the hadith of Shurayh only means that the Prophet (peace be upon him) abrogated what the disbelievers used to do in their time, such as designating 'Am and Bahirah etc. for idols.' For this reason, some mashayikh (may Allah have mercy on them) said that the fatwa is on the statement of the Sahibayn. I (the translator) say that this is the preferred and most suitable statement. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the legal nature of waqf. The core issue is whether waqf is binding (lazim) and irrevocable, or revocable like a loan (ariyah). Imam Abu Hanifa holds that waqf is valid but not binding; the waqf-maker retains ownership and can revoke it. His evidence includes a weak hadith about no withholding from divine shares, a hadith of Shurayh about selling, and rational arguments: the waqf-maker derives benefit, appoints trustees, and the perpetual transfer of ownership to Allah is not established in Shari'ah (unlike manumission where ownership is removed, or a mosque which is exclusive for Allah). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that waqf is binding; ownership transfers to Allah, making the property inalienable. Their evidence includes the famous hadith of Umar's waqf where the Prophet said 'make its original property a sadaqah so it may never be sold, inherited, or gifted' (recorded in Sahih collections), and the analogy with a mosque. Later Hanafi authorities like Shaykh al-Islam and Ibn al-Humam prefer the Sahibayn's view, and the fatwa is upon it. The translator affirms this preference. This passage thus shows the evolution of the Hanafi position: the mufta bihi view is that waqf is binding.

Key Terms
وقف (waqf): Detaining a property in such a way that its corpus is preserved and its benefits are dedicated to charitable purposes in perpetuity.
عاریت (ariyah): A loan of a usufruct (permission to use something without consuming it); it is revocable at will.
لازم (lazim): Binding or irrevocable; once the contract is made, it cannot be revoked unilaterally.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, is waqf binding or revocable?
A) Binding (lazim)
B) Revocable (jayz)
C) Forbidden
D) Only binding if a judge rules so

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi Hanafi position is that waqf is binding (lazim) and irrevocable, contrary to Imam Abu Hanifa's original view.

Waqf — Endowment
intermediate

How a Judge's Ruling Makes Waqf Binding
Ruling on when a judge's ruling makes waqf binding

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on what makes waqf binding and explain why ta'liq upon death does not terminate ownership but creates a binding will.

Core Idea
Only a judge's ruling makes waqf binding; suspending it on death becomes a will, not a binding waqf.

Imam Abu Hanifa held that waqf is not binding by mere declaration; ownership remains with the waqf-maker. However, a judge's ruling in an ijtihadi matter can make it binding. What about suspending waqf upon one's own death? This lesson unpacks the distinction and the scholarly reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling from al-Quduri
The base text states that ownership ends from waqf only if a judge rules or if the waqf-maker suspends it upon death. Note that this is the statement being commented on.
2
Recognize the two scenarios
Separate the judge's ruling scenario from the ta'liq (suspension) scenario. The commentator affirms the first but clarifies the second.
3
Understand the judge's ruling scenario
A judge's ruling in an ijtihadi matter (like waqf) is binding. This is because the judge's authority settles disputes and makes the hukm effective.
The term 'hakim' means a sultan or a qadi appointed by him; a self-appointed judge's ruling is debated but the most correct view is it is binding.
4
Analyze the ta'liq scenario
Suspending waqf upon death does not terminate ownership under Abu Hanifa. However, if the benefits are dedicated perpetually as sadaqah, it becomes a will (wasiyyah) regarding those benefits, which is binding from one-third of the estate.
This is a qiyas (analogy) to a will, ensuring the perpetual dedication is enforced but not as waqf.
5
Note the intra-madhhab difference on the judge's authority
Some mashayikh do not accept a non-sultan appointed judge's ruling, but the preferred view (as in al-Khulasa) is that any legitimate judge's ruling is binding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ قَالَ فِى الكتب ..... الخ مصنف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ کتاب یعنی قدوری میں جو یہ فرمایا ہے کہ وقف سے مالک کی ملکیت ختم نہ ہوگی مگر جبکہ کوئی حاکم حکم دے دے یا یہ کہ خود واقف اپنی موت پر اسے متعلق کر دئے تو یہ کلام حاکم کے حکم کی صورت میں تو صحیح ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کا حکم ایک اجتہادی مسئلہ میں واقع ہوگا۔ مگر موت پر معلق کرنے کی صورت میں مشائخ رحمتہ اللہ علیہم نے اختلاف کیا ہے اور صحیح یہ ہے کہ امام ابوحنیفہ رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک اس طرح معلق کرنے سے ملکیت ختم نہیں ہوگی ۔ لیکن اس نے وقف کے منافع کو ہمیشہ کے لئے صدقہ کیا ہے تو ایسا ہو گیا کہ گویا منافع کے بارے میں ہمیشہ کے لئے کسی کے واسطے وصیت کر دی جو لا زم ہو جائے گی ۔ معلوم ہونا چاہئے کہ یہاں حاکم سے مراد وہ حاکم ہے جو سلطان ہو یا سلطان کی طرف سے قاضی مقرر کیا گیا ہو ۔ اور اگر کسی شخص کو لوگوں نے اپنے طور پر حاکم مقرر کر لیا ہو تو اس کے حکم دینے میں مشائخ رحمتہ اللہ علیہم کا اختلاف ہے ۔ یعنی اس کے فیصلہ سے بعض مشائخ رحمتہ اللہ علیہم کے نزدیک حکم لازم نہ ہوگا۔ (اور اصح قول یہ ہے کہ حکم لازم ہو جائے گا۔ جیسا کہ خلاصہ میں ہے )
He said: He said in the books... etc. The author (may Allah have mercy on him) stated: In the book (al-Quduri) it is said that the owner's ownership will not be terminated from waqf unless a judge gives a ruling, or unless the waqf-maker himself suspends it upon his death. This statement is correct in the case of a judge's ruling, because his ruling occurs in an ijtihadi matter. However, regarding suspension upon death, the mashayikh have differed. The correct view is that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, ownership is not terminated by such suspension. But if he has dedicated the benefits of the waqf perpetually as sadaqah, then it becomes as if he has made a perpetual will regarding the benefits, which will become binding. It should be known that here 'judge' means one who is a sultan or a qadi appointed by the sultan. If someone is appointed as a judge by the people on their own, there is disagreement among the mashayikh regarding his ruling – some say his ruling will not be binding. (And the most correct view is that his ruling will be binding, as stated in al-Khulasa.)
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific ruling: how can waqf become binding according to Imam Abu Hanifa, who generally holds it is not binding? The matn of al-Quduri states that ownership only terminates from waqf if a judge rules so, or if the waqf-maker suspends it upon his death. The commentator (the author of Ashraf al-Hidaya) clarifies that the first part is correct: a judge's ruling can make the waqf binding because the judge's ruling in an ijtihadi matter is binding. However, the second part (suspension upon death) is disputed. The correct view according to Imam Abu Hanifa is that suspending waqf upon death does not terminate ownership; the waqf remains non-binding. Nevertheless, if the waqf-maker has perpetually dedicated the benefits as sadaqah, it becomes analogous to a will (wasiyyah) regarding those benefits, which would be binding from one-third of his estate. The passage also defines the term 'hakim' (judge): it must be the sultan or an appointed qadi. If someone is appointed by the people without authority, there is scholarly disagreement on the binding nature of his ruling, but the most correct view is that it is binding.

Key Terms
حاکم (hakim): A ruler or judge with authority to adjudicate; here specifically the sultan or a qadi appointed by him.
معلق (mu'allaq): Suspended; a legal condition that makes the waqf effective only upon a future event like death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following makes waqf binding under Imam Abu Hanifa?
A) The waqf-maker's declaration alone
B) A judge's ruling
C) Suspension upon death
D) Appointment of a trustee

Key Takeaway
A judge's ruling can make waqf binding; suspending waqf on death does not but creates a binding will for the benefits.

Waqf During Death Illness: Binding, One-Third, and the Utterance vs Delivery Dispute
Ruling on waqf during death illness with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on waqf during death illness, distinguish between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and explain the practical difference between Abu Yusuf's and Muhammad's views on delivery.

Core Idea
Waqf in death illness is binding only from one-third, and the fatwa follows Abu Yusuf: mere utterance suffices.

This lesson explores a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute about the validity and binding nature of waqf made during a fatal illness (marad al-mawt). While Abu Hanifa held such a waqf non-binding, the Sahibayn considered it binding but limited to one-third of the estate. Within the Sahibayn, a further split arises: Abu Yusuf requires only utterance, while Muhammad insists on delivery to a mutawalli. Understanding this dispute clarifies the practical effects of a deathbed endowment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
The passage addresses waqf made during marad al-mawt. The key question is whether it is binding and if so, to what extent.
Marad al-mawt actions are analogous to wills (wasiyyah).
2
State the Abu Hanifa position
Imam Abu Hanifa held that waqf in death illness is not binding at all.
3
State the Sahibayn position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) agreed that it is binding, but only from one-third of the estate.
This aligns with the rule for wills.
4
Distinguish within the Sahibayn
Abu Yusuf held that mere utterance terminates ownership (like manumission). Muhammad required delivery to a mutawalli because Allah's ownership cannot be directly intended.
Imam Shafi'i and most scholars agreed with Abu Yusuf.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The fatwa, according to al-Munyat, is on Abu Yusuf's view: binding from one-third by mere utterance.
The mashayikh of Bukhara preferred Muhammad's view, but it is not the operative position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْوَقَفَ فِي مَرَض مَوت .... الخ اور اگر کسی نے اپنے مرض الموت میں وقف کیا ہو تو طحاوی رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ یہ وصیت بعد الموت کے حکم میں ہے۔ اور صحیح یہ ہے کہ امام ابوحنیفہ رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک یہ لازم نہ ہوگا۔ لیکن صاحبین رحمتہ اللہ علیہا کے نزدیک لازمی ہوگا۔ مگر اس کا اعتبار صرف ایک تہائی مال سے ہوگا۔ اور جو وقف صحت کی حالت میں ہو تو اس کا اعتبار پورے مال سے ہوگا اور اب جبکہ صاحبین رحمتہ اللہ علیہما کے نزدیک ملکیت ختم ہو جاتی ہے تو ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک صرف قول سے ہی ختم ہو جائے گی ۔ امام شافعی رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کا یہی قول ہے ( ۔ بلکہ اکثر علماء کا یہی قول ہے۔ اور محققین کے نزدیک یہی وجہ ہے۔ اور منیہ میں ہے کہ اسی پر فتوئی ہے)۔ کیونکہ یہ اعتناق کے حکم میں ہے کیونکہ یہ بھی ملکیت ساقط کرنے کا نام ہے۔ اور امام محمد رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک صرف کہنے سے نہیں بلکہ اسے متولی کے سپرد کرنا بھی ضروری ہے۔ کیونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ جو سارے جہاں کا مالک ہے اس کو خاص ارادہ کر کے مالک نہیں بنایا جا سکتا ہے۔ بلکہ کبھی تبعا ہوا کرتا ہے۔ تو اس کا وہی حکم ہو جاتا ہے۔ یعنی جب اس کے کسی بندہ کو دیا تو اس کے ضمن میں اللہ تعالی کی ملکیہ میں دینا ثابت ہو گیا۔ پس صدقہ اور زکوۃ کے حکم میں ہو گیا۔ اسی قول کو مشائخ بخارا نے قبول کیا ہے۔
And if someone made a waqf during a death illness... etc. If someone made a waqf during his death illness, Imam Tahawi (may Allah have mercy on him) said that it is like a will after death. The correct view is that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, it will not be binding. But according to the Sahibayn, it will be binding, but it will be considered only from one-third of the estate. A waqf made in health is considered from the entire estate. Now, since according to the Sahibayn ownership is terminated, according to Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him), it will be terminated by mere utterance. Imam Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) held this view, in fact most scholars hold this, and the researchers consider it the correct basis. In al-Munyat, it is stated that the fatwa is upon this. Because this is in the same ruling as manumission, since it also removes ownership. According to Imam Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him), it is not by mere utterance; rather, it is necessary to hand it over to a trustee (mutawalli). Because Allah, who is the owner of the entire world, cannot be made owner by specific intention; rather, it sometimes occurs incidentally. So the same ruling applies: when given to a servant, indirectly giving to Allah's ownership is established. Thus it falls under the ruling of sadaqah and zakat. The mashayikh of Bukhara accepted this view.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage deals with the validity and binding nature of waqf made during marad al-mawt (death illness). Imam Tahawi held it is like a will (wasiyyah). The correct Hanafi position: According to Abu Hanifa, such a waqf is not binding at all. According to the Sahibayn, it is binding but limited to one-third of the estate (like a will). Since in the Sahibayn's view ownership is terminated, there is further difference: Abu Yusuf holds that mere utterance terminates it (similar to manumission and the view of many scholars including Shafi'i), and the fatwa in al-Munyat is on this. Imam Muhammad holds that mere utterance is not enough; delivery to a mutawalli is required, because ownership to Allah cannot be directly intended but occurs indirectly when given to a servant. The mashayikh of Bukhara preferred Muhammad's view. Hence, there is an intra-Hanafi split: Abu Yusuf requires only utterance, Muhammad requires delivery.

Key Terms
مرض الموت (marad al-mawt): A fatal illness that leads to death, where the person's actions are considered under the rules of bequest (wasiyyah).
متولی (mutawalli): The person appointed to manage the waqf property.
اعتناق (itiq): Manumission (freeing a slave); used analogically by Abu Yusuf to argue that utterance alone removes ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position, how does waqf in death illness become binding?
A) Only by a judge's ruling
B) Not binding at all
C) Binding from one-third by mere utterance
D) Binding from one-third only after delivery to mutawalli

Key Takeaway
Waqf in marad al-mawt is binding from one-third of the estate by mere utterance (Abu Yusuf's view), in contrast to Abu Hanifa's non-binding opinion and Muhammad's delivery requirement.

Ownership of Waqf Property After Valid Waqf
Ruling with talil on ownership after waqf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ownership of waqf property after a valid waqf and explain the talil (legal reasoning) that prevents ownership from transferring to the beneficiary.

Core Idea
Waqf property leaves the waqif's ownership but never enters the beneficiary's ownership.

This passage addresses a fundamental question in waqf law: who owns the property after a valid waqf? The Hanafi school is unanimous that the beneficiary does not become the owner, even though they differ on where ultimate ownership resides. The reasoning (talil) provided is that if the beneficiary became owner, the waqf would not be suspended on their existence—i.e., the property would be transferable and inheritable, contradicting the perpetuity of waqf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
What happens to ownership when waqf is valid? The text states: 'It leaves the ownership of the waqf-maker and does not enter the ownership of the beneficiary.'
Focus on the two negatives: exit from waqif's ownership, no entry into beneficiary's ownership.
2
Locate the talil
The reason (talil) is given: 'Because if it entered the ownership of the beneficiary, it would not be suspended [on the beneficiary's existence].' This shows that ownership would break the perpetual nature of waqf.
The text is cut off after 'bal' but the meaning is clear.
3
Understand the intra-madhhab difference
Abu Hanifa holds the property remains in the waqif's ownership (suspended), while Sahibayn hold it becomes Allah's ownership. Both agree the beneficiary does not become owner.
This intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf does not affect the practical ruling that beneficiary is not owner.
4
Note the cross-madhhab dispute
Other schools (e.g., Hanbali) hold that the beneficiaries become collective owners. This contrasts with the Hanafi position.
The practical consequence: in Hanafi law, the corpus is inalienable; in Hanbali, beneficiaries may dispose of it under conditions.
5
Apply the ruling
In a modern scenario, a waqf property cannot be sold or inherited by beneficiaries. They only have usufruct rights.
This protects the perpetuity of charitable endowments.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَإِذَا صَحَ الْوَقْفُ عَلَى اخْتِلَافِهِمْ وَفِي بَعْضِ النُّسُحَ وَإِذَا اسْتُحِقَ مَكَانَ قَولِ، وَ إِذَاصَحَ خَرَجَ مِنْ مِلْكِ الْوَاقِفِ وَلَمْ يَدْخُلُ فِى مِلْكِ الموقوفِ عَلَيْهِ لِأَنَّهُ لَوْ دَخَلَ فِي مِلكِ الْمَوْقُوفِ عَلَيْهِ لَا يَتَوَقَّفُ عَلَيْهِ بَلْ
He said: When the waqf is valid according to their disagreement, and in some copies it says 'when it is proved' instead of 'statement'. And when it is valid, it leaves the ownership of the waqf-maker and does not enter the ownership of the beneficiary (mawquf 'alayh). Because if it entered the ownership of the beneficiary, it would not be suspended [on the beneficiary's existence] but rather...
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling on the ownership status of waqf property after a valid waqf, regardless of the disagreement on binding nature. The text states that the property exits the ownership of the waqf-maker (al-waqif) and does not enter the ownership of the beneficiary (al-mawquf 'alayh). The reason given is that if it entered the beneficiary's ownership, the waqf would not be suspended (yatawaqqaf) on the beneficiary's existence; in other words, the beneficiary does not become owner because ownership would imply that the property could be transferred or inherited by them, which contradicts the perpetuity of waqf. The phrase is cut off but the meaning is clear: waqf property is not owned by any human; it remains in the ownership of Allah (as per the Sahibayn's view) or in a suspended state (as per Abu Hanifa). This ruling is consistent across both views: the beneficiary does not become owner.

Key Terms
موقوف علیہ (mawquf 'alayh): The person or entity designated to receive the benefits of the waqf.
واقف (waqif): The person who creates the waqf.
وقف (waqf): An Islamic endowment where property is dedicated for charitable or religious purposes in perpetuity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Remains in full ownership of the waqf-maker.
B) Enters ownership of the beneficiary.
C) Leaves the waqf-maker's ownership and does not enter the beneficiary's.
D) Belongs to the state.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a valid waqf transfers ownership from the waqf-maker to Allah (or suspends it), and the beneficiary never becomes owner of the corpus.

Preference for Sahibayn's View on Binding Waqf
Tarjih for binding nature of waqf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi intra-madhhab dispute on whether waqf is binding, explain the tarjih for the Sahibayn's view, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
The mufta bihi view in Hanafi fiqh is that waqf is binding (lazim) once declared.

This passage resolves a famous intra-Hanafi dispute: Is waqf irrevocable or revocable? The author presents Shaykh al-Islam's tarjih for the Sahibayn's view that waqf is binding, supported by hadiths and the practice of the early community. Understanding this tarjih is crucial because the operative ruling (mufta bihi) is the binding view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
Recognize that Imam Abu Hanifa held waqf as revocable (ja'iz), while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) held it as binding (lazim).
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
2
Locate the tarjih
Find where the author expresses preference for the Sahibayn's view, after citing Shaykh al-Islam's lengthy discussion.
Tarjih is the process of preferring one evidence over another.
3
Examine the evidence
Note the references: numerous hadiths, the practice of the Companions and Successors, and the interpretation of Shuraih's hadith as referring to pre-Islamic practices, not Islamic waqf.
The hadith of Shuraih is reinterpreted to remove apparent contradiction.
4
Note the fatwa position
Some mashayikh have explicitly stated that the fatwa is on the view of the Sahibayn.
Fatwa = the operative ruling given to questioners.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
The translator endorses this as the chosen (mukhtar) and most appropriate view.
Mufta bihi = the relied-upon position in the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نہیں رہا اس لئے فرائض الہی سے کوئی جبس نہیں ہوا۔ جیسے مال منقولہ و وصیت و ہبہ وصدقہ میں کوئی جس نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ شیخ الاسلام نے طویل کلام کرنے کے بعد فرمایا ہے کہ اس مقام میں حق بات یہی ہے کہ صاحبین و عالمہ علماء کے قول کمر ترجیح ہے۔ یعنی وقف لازم ہو جاتا ہے۔ کیونکہ اس بحث میں بہت سی حدیثیں وارد ہوئی ہیں۔ اور صحابہ وتابعین اور ان کے بعد عام امت کا بھی اس پر عمل چلا آتا ہے۔ اور حدیث شریح کے صرف یہی معنی ہیں کہ کفار جو اپنے زمانہ میں عام وبحیرہ وغیرہ کو بتوں کے نام کر دیتے اسے رسول اللہ نے منسوخ کر دیا۔ اسی لئے بعض مشائخ رحمتہ اللہ علیہم نے کہا ہے کہ صاحبین رحمتہ اللہ علیہا کے قول پر ہی فتوی ہے۔ میں مترجم کہتا ہوں کہ یہی قول مختار اور اوفق ہے۔ واللہ تعالی اعلم ۔
Therefore, there is no deficiency from divine obligations. Like in movable property, bequest, gift, and charity there is no deficiency. Shaykh al-Islam, after a lengthy discussion, said that in this place the correct view is that the view of the Sahibayn and the great scholars is preponderant. That is, waqf becomes binding. Because in this discussion many hadiths have been reported, and the Companions, Successors, and the general ummah after them have acted upon it. And the hadith of Shuraih only means that the disbelievers used to dedicate things like 'Aam and Bahirah to idols in their time, and the Messenger of Allah abrogated that. Therefore, some mashayikh have said that the fatwa is on the view of the Sahibayn. The translator says that this view is chosen and more appropriate. And Allah the Almighty knows best.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage is a tarjih (preference) within the Hanafi school regarding the binding nature of waqf. The author, after explaining the dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa (who held that waqf is revocable) and the Sahibayn (who held it is binding), affirms that the Sahibayn's view is preferred (mufta bihi). The reasoning given is: (1) numerous hadiths support the binding nature of waqf, (2) the practice of the Companions, Successors, and the ummah has been consistent, and (3) the hadith of Shuraih (which might suggest revocability) is interpreted as referring to pre-Islamic practices of dedicating animals to idols, not to Islamic waqf. Thus, the fatwa is based on the Sahibayn. The commentator (the translator) endorses this as the chosen (mukhtar) and most appropriate view.

Key Terms
وقف لازم (waqf lazim): An endowment that is irrevocable and binding once declared.
ترجیح (tarjih): The process of preferring one legal opinion or evidence over another due to its greater strength.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the tarjih (preference) in this passage, whose view on the binding nature of waqf is relied upon?
A) Imam Abu Hanifa
B) Imam al-Shafi'i
C) The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad)
D) Imam Malik

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi view in the Hanafi school is that waqf is binding (lazim) upon declaration, based on the tarjih of the Sahibayn.

Waqf and the Judge's Decree: When Does Ownership Transfer?
Sharh of Quduri's statement on conditions for waqf binding

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions that make a waqf binding according to Quduri, and explain the Hanafi positions on each condition.

Core Idea
A waqf leaves ownership only by a judge's decree or deathbed suspension; otherwise, ownership remains with the owner.

This passage is a commentary on Quduri's Mukhtasar, explaining the condition for a waqf to exit the owner's property. The commentator clarifies that a judge's decree is valid because it is an ijtihadi ruling, while suspension upon death involves a dispute. Additionally, the definition of a judge is restricted to official appointees.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
Quduri states that waqf does not leave ownership without a judge's decree or death condition. This is the baseline ruling.
2
Analyze the judge's decree condition
The commentator confirms this is correct because a judge's decree is binding in ijtihadi matters. Note that 'judge' here means a legitimate ruler or appointed judge.
3
Examine the deathbed suspension
There is a dispute. The correct view according to Abu Hanifa is that ownership does not transfer, but if the profits are designated as perpetual charity, it becomes a binding bequest.
4
Define the term 'judge'
The commentator restricts 'judge' to a sultan or a judge appointed by the sultan. If people appoint an arbiter, there is disagreement; the soundest view is that his ruling is binding.
5
Synthesize the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that a judge's decree makes the waqf binding, and for deathbed suspension, it is treated as a bequest. The definition of judge is limited to official authorities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ قَالَ فِى الكتب ..... الخ مصنف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ کتاب یعنی قدوری میں جو یہ فرمایا ہے کہ وقف سے مالک کی ملکیت ختم نہ ہوگی مگر جبکہ کوئی حاکم حکم دے دے یا یہ کہ خود واقف اپنی موت پر اسے متعلق کر دئے تو یہ کلام حاکم کے حکم کی صورت میں تو صحیح ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کا حکم ایک اجتہادی مسئلہ میں واقع ہوگا۔ مگر موت پر معلق کرنے کی صورت میں مشائخ رحمتہ اللہ علیہم نے اختلاف کیا ہے اور صحیح یہ ہے کہ امام ابوحنیفہ رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک اس طرح معلق کرنے سے ملکیت ختم نہیں ہوگی ۔ لیکن اس نے وقف کے منافع کو ہمیشہ کے لئے صدقہ کیا ہے تو ایسا ہو گیا کہ گویا منافع کے بارے میں ہمیشہ کے لئے کسی کے واسطے وصیت کر دی جو لا زم ہو جائے گی ۔ معلوم ہونا چہئے کہ یہاں حاکم سے مراد وہ حاکم ہے جو سلطان ہو یا سلطان کی طرف سے قاضی مقرر کیا گیا ہو ۔ اور اگر کسی شخص کو لوگوں نے اپنے طور پر حاکم مقرر کر لیا ہو تو اس کے حکم دینے میں مشائخ رحمتہ اللہ علیہم کا اختلاف ہے ۔ یعنی اس کے فیصلہ سے بعض مشائخ رحمتہ اللہ علیہم کے نزدیک حکم لازم نہ ہوگا۔ (اور اصح قول یہ ہے کہ حکم لازم ہو جائے گا۔ جیسا کہ خلاصہ میں ہے )
He said: He said in the books... etc. The author said: In the Kitab, i.e., Quduri's work, it is stated that waqf does not remove ownership from the owner unless a judge rules or the waqf is suspended upon his death. This statement is correct in the case of a judge's ruling, because his ruling occurs in an ijtihadi matter. However, regarding suspension upon death, the mashayikh have differed, and the correct view is that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, such suspension does not remove ownership. But if he has dedicated the profits of the waqf perpetually as charity, then it is as if he made a perpetual bequest of the profits to someone, which becomes binding. It should be known that by 'judge' here is meant a sultan or a judge appointed by the sultan. If people appoint someone as a judge on their own, then the mashayikh differed concerning his ruling. That is, according to some mashayikh, his decision would not be binding. (The most correct view is that it would be binding, as mentioned in al-Khulasa.)
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on a statement from Quduri's Mukhtasar. Quduri states that a waqf does not exit the owner's property unless either a judge (hakim) issues a decree, or the waqf is suspended upon the owner's death (like a deathbed waqf). The commentator explains: (1) Regarding the judge's decree, it is acceptable because it is an ijtihadi ruling and a judge's decision is binding. (2) Regarding suspension upon death, there is a dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that such suspension does not remove ownership; however, if the waqf is of the profits perpetually, it is like a bequest, which is binding. (3) The term 'hakim' here means a legitimate ruler or a judge appointed by the ruler. If people appoint an arbitrator without authority, there is disagreement; the soundest view is that his ruling is still binding. This passage shows the layered nature of Hanafi jurisprudence: a matn statement is clarified by the commentator, including internal disagreements and the preferred view.

Key Terms
حاکم (hakim): A legitimate ruler (sultan) or a judge appointed by the sultan, whose decree is binding in ijtihadi matters.
وقف (waqf): An endowment; permanent dedication of property for charitable or pious purposes, with ownership transferred away from the owner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, under what condition does a waqf leave the owner's property according to Quduri's statement?
A) If the waqf is of movables
B) If a judge rules or if the waqf is suspended upon death
C) If the waqf is of real estate
D) If the waqf is accepted by the beneficiaries

Key Takeaway
A waqf becomes binding only with a judge's decree or deathbed suspension; the term 'judge' is restricted to official appointees.

Ruling on Waqf During Death Illness
Ruling on waqf made during marad al-mawt and its effect on ownership and the one-third limit.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on waqf during death illness and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad regarding bindingness and delivery.

Core Idea
A waqf made during death illness is valid but binding only up to one-third of the estate, like a bequest.

This lesson examines the ruling of waqf (endowment) made during marad al-mawt (death illness). The Hanafi school has an internal dispute: while all agree it is limited to the bequestable third, they differ on whether it is binding and whether delivery is required. We will explore these positions and the reasoning behind them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
Recognize that the act is a waqf made during death illness (marad al-mawt). Determine that such acts are treated like bequests for inheritance purposes.
2
State the general Hanafi principle
Understand that acts during death illness are limited to one-third of the estate unless heirs consent. This applies to waqf as well.
3
Present the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Note the disagreement: Abu Hanifa holds it is not binding; the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold it is binding but only from one-third.
4
Distinguish between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad
Within the Sahibayn, Abu Yusuf says mere declaration suffices, while Muhammad requires delivery to a trustee. Understand the reasoning behind each.
5
Identify the mufta bihi and its application
The relied-upon position for fatwa is binding per Sahibayn, with mere declaration according to Abu Yusuf (as stated in al-Munya). Note that the scholars of Bukhara accepted Muhammad's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْوَقَفَ فِي مَرَض مَوت .... الخ اور اگر کسی نے اپنے مرض الموت میں وقف کیا ہو تو طحاوی رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ یہ وصیت بعد الموت کے حکم میں ہے۔ اور صحیح یہ ہے کہ امام ابوحنیفہ رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک یہ لازم نہ ہوگا۔ لیکن صاحبین رحمتہ اللہ علیہا کے نزدیک لازمی ہوگا۔ مگر اس کا اعتبار صرف ایک تہائی مال سے ہوگا۔ اور جو وقف صحت کی حالت میں ہو تو اس کا اعتبار پورے مال سے ہوگا اور اب جبکہ صاحبین رحمتہ اللہ علیہما کے نزدیک ملکیت ختم ہو جاتی ہے تو ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک صرف قول سے ہی ختم ہو جائے گی ۔ امام شافعی رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کا یہی قول ہے ( ۔ بلکہ اکثر علماء کا یہی قول ہے۔ اور محققین کے نزدیک یہی وجہ ہے۔ اور منیہ میں ہے کہ اسی پر فتوئی ہے)۔ کیونکہ یہ اعتناق کے حکم میں ہے کیونکہ یہ بھی ملکیت ساقط کرنے کا نام ہے۔ اور امام محمد رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک صرف کہنے سے نہیں بلکہ اسے متولی کے سپرد کرنا بھی ضروری ہے۔ کیونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ جو سارے جہاں کا مالک ہے اس کو خاص ارادہ کر کے مالک نہیں بنایا جا سکتا ہے۔ بلکہ کبھی تبعا ہوا کرتا ہے۔ تو اس کا وہی حکم ہو جاتا ہے۔ یعنی جب اس کے کسی بندہ کو دیا تو اس کے ضمن میں اللہ تعالی کی ملکیہ میں دینا ثابت ہو گیا۔ پس صدقہ اور زکوۃ کے حکم میں ہو گیا۔ اسی قول کو مشائخ بخارا نے قبول کیا ہے۔
And if he made a waqf during death illness... etc. And if someone made a waqf during his death illness, then al-Tahawi said: It is in the ruling of a bequest after death. And the correct view is that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, it will not be binding. But according to the Sahibayn, it will be binding, but it will be considered only from one-third of the property. And a waqf made during health is considered from the entire property. And now, since according to the Sahibayn ownership ends, according to Abu Yusuf, it ends by mere declaration. This is also the view of Imam al-Shafi‘i. Rather, it is the view of most scholars, and the investigators consider it the correct reasoning. And in al-Munya, it is said that fatwa is upon it. Because it is in the ruling of a contract (i‘tiqad), as it is a removal of ownership. And according to Imam Muhammad, it is not by mere declaration; rather, it is necessary to hand it over to a trustee. Because Allah, the Owner of all worlds, cannot be made owner by specific intention; rather, it occurs sometimes as a consequence. So it takes the same ruling. That is, when he gives to one of His servants, then it becomes established that he gave it to Allah's ownership in the process. So it falls under the ruling of charity and zakat. This is the view accepted by the mashayikh of Bukhara.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage discusses waqf made during marad al-mawt (death illness). The commentator presents: (1) al-Tahawi's view that it is like a bequest (wasaya). (2) The correct view: According to Abu Hanifa, it is not binding (the owner can revoke). According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, it is binding but only to the extent of one-third of the property (like a bequest). They differ on the method: Abu Yusuf says mere declaration suffices; Muhammad says delivery to a trustee is required. The viewpoint of Abu Yusuf is likened to Imam al-Shafi‘i and most scholars, and fatwa is given accordingly. The reasoning is that waqf is a contract of removing ownership (izalat al-milk), similar to a gift or sale. Imam Muhammad's view requires delivery because Allah cannot be directly made the owner of a specific property; rather, once given to a human beneficiary, it is then considered dedicated to Allah in meaning. This view was accepted by the scholars of Bukhara. The practical consequence: in death illness, waqf is limited to the bequestable third.

Key Terms
مرض الموت (marad al-mawt): A terminal illness that leads to death, during which acts are treated as bequests if they exceed one-third of the estate.
وقف (waqf): An endowment of property for charitable or religious purposes, where the ownership is transferred to Allah and the benefits are dedicated to beneficiaries.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, what is the limit on a waqf made during death illness?
A) No limit; it affects the entire estate
B) Only one-third of the estate
C) Only one-half of the estate
D) It is completely invalid

Key Takeaway
Waqf during death illness is valid but limited to one-third of the estate, with the mufta bihi being binding by mere declaration per Abu Yusuf.

Ownership of Endowed Property: Between Wakif and Beneficiary
Ruling that endowed property exits wakif's ownership but does not enter beneficiary's ownership

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the ownership of endowed property after a valid waqf and explain the difference between the position of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Endowed property leaves the wakif's ownership but does not become the beneficiary's property; ownership is suspended.

This passage from Quduri and its commentary in al-Hidayah addresses a fundamental question in waqf law: who owns the property once it is endowed? The answer hinges on which Hanafi authority you follow. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying waqf rulings in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Claim
Read Quduri's statement: the property exits the wakif's ownership and does not enter the beneficiary's ownership. Write down the exact ruling.
This is the core ruling from the matn.
2
Examine the Proofs
Find the two reasons Quduri gives: (1) if the beneficiary owned it, he could sell it, contradicting waqf perpetuity; (2) ownership cannot be restricted by the original owner's condition.
These proofs support the ruling.
3
Recognize the Intra-Madhhab Difference
The commentator from al-Hidayah clarifies that Quduri's statement reflects the Sahibayn's view (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the substance remains the wakif's property.
This distinction is crucial for understanding later Hanafi practice.
4
Apply the Ruling
Consider a scenario: a man endows his house as a mosque. According to the Sahibayn, can the mosque committee sell the house? Answer and explain why.
The committee, as beneficiaries, does not own the property.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَإِذَا صَحَ الْوَقْفُ عَلَى اخْتِلَافِهِمْ وَفِي بَعْضِ النُّسُحَ وَإِذَا اسْتُحِقَ مَكَانَ قَولِ، وَ إِذَاصَحَ خَرَجَ مِنْ مِلْكِ الْوَاقِفِ وَلَمْ يَدْخُلُ فِى مِلْكِ الموقوفِ عَلَيْهِ لِأَنَّهُ لَوْ دَخَلَ فِي مِلكِ الْمَوْقُوفِ عَلَيْهِ لَا يَتَوَقَّفُ عَلَيْهِ بَلْ يَنْفُذُبَيْعُهُ كَسَائِرِ أَمْلاكِهِ وَلَأنَّهُ لَوْ مَلَكَهُ لَمَّا انْتَقَلَ عَنْهُ بِشَرُطِ الْمَالِكِ الْاَوَّلِ كَسَائِرِ أَمْلاكِهِ قَالَ وَقَوْلُهُ خَرَجَ . عَنْ مِلْك الوَاقِفِ يَجب أن يَكُونَ قَوْلُهُمَا عَلَى الْوَجُهِ الَّذِي سَبَقَ ذِكْرُهُ ترجمہ اور قدوری رحمۃ اللہ علیہ نے کہا ہے کہ جب فقہاء کے اختلاف کے موافق وقف صحیح ہو گیا تو وہ موقوف وقف کرنے والے کی ملکیت سے نکل گیا ساتھ ہی جن لوگوں پر وہ وقف ہے ان کی ملک میں داخل بھی نہیں ہوا۔ کیونکہ اگر اس شخص ( موقوف علیہ ) کی ملک میں داخل ہو جاتا تو اس پر وہ وقف نہ رہتا بلکہ اگر وہ اسے فروخت کرنا چاہتا تو فروخت صحیح ہو جاتی جیسے کہ اس کی دوسری ذاتی ملکیت کی چیزیں (زمین، مکان وغیرہ میں اس کا فروخت کرنا صحیح ہو جاتا ہے ) اور اس دلیل سے بھی کہ اگر موقوف علیہ اس کا مالک ہو جاتا تو پہلے مالک کی شرط کے موافق دوسروں کی طرف وہ منتقل نہیں ہوسکتا ہے۔ جیسے اس کی دوسری املاک کا حال ہے اور مصنف ہدایہ رحمۃ اللہ علیہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ قدوری رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کا یہ کہنا کہ وقف کرنے والے کی ملکیت سے نکل گیا تو اوپر بیان کئے ہوئے اختلاف کے مطابق یہ قول صاحبین رحمۃ اللہ علیہا کے قول کے مطابق ہونا چاہئے ۔ ( کیونکہ امام اعظم رحمۃ اللہ علیہ کے قول کے مطابق حکم یہ ہے کہ وقف کی اصل جائیداد مالک کی ملک پر باقی تو ر ہے لیکن اس کے منافع دوسروں کو حاصل ہوتے رہیں۔ جیسا کہ اوپر ذکر کیا جاچکا ہے)۔ تشریح واذا صح الوقف الخ قدورى رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کی ایک روایت کے مطابق ایسا ہی ہے۔ لیکن دوسرے نسخہ کے مطابق یہی عبارت بجائے صبح کے یوں ہے واذا استحق الخ۔ ترجمہ سے مطلب واضح ہے۔
He said: And when the waqf becomes valid according to their differences... and in some copies: 'and when it is established' in place of 'his statement: and when it is valid'. It exits from the ownership of the wakif and does not enter into the ownership of the mawquf ‘alayh, because if it entered into the ownership of the mawquf ‘alayh, it would not remain a waqf on him, but rather his sale of it would be valid like any of his other properties. And also because if he owned it, it would not transfer from him by the condition of the first owner, like any other of his properties. He said: And his statement 'exited from the ownership of the wakif' must be according to their statement in the manner mentioned earlier. Translation: And Quduri said: When the waqf becomes valid according to the disagreement of the jurists, the endowed property leaves the ownership of the wakif and does not enter into the ownership of the beneficiaries. Because if it entered the beneficiary's ownership, it would not remain a waqf; rather, if he wanted to sell it, the sale would be valid, like any of his other properties (land, house, etc., his selling would be valid). And also because if the beneficiary became the owner, it could not be transferred from him by the condition of the first owner, like his other properties. And the author of al-Hidayah said: Quduri's statement that it leaves the wakif's ownership must be in accordance with the disagreement mentioned earlier, that this statement is according to the Sahibayn's view. (Because according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the substance of the waqf remains in the owner's ownership, but its profits go to others, as mentioned earlier). Explanation: 'Wa idha sahha al-waqf...' is the same according to one narration of Quduri. But according to another copy, instead of 'sahha', the wording is 'istuḥiqqa' (established). The translation makes the meaning clear.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage is a definitional ruling regarding the ownership of waqf property after a valid endowment. The matn from Quduri states that the property leaves the wakif's ownership but does not become owned by the beneficiaries (mawquf ‘alayh). Two proofs are given: (1) If the beneficiary owned it, he could sell it, which contradicts the perpetuity of waqf. (2) Ownership would be absolute and could not be restricted by the original owner's condition. The commentator (the author of al-Hidayah) clarifies that Quduri's statement 'exits from the wakif's ownership' applies only according to the Sahibayn's view (that waqf removes ownership). According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the property remains in the wakif's ownership but its profits are dedicated. Thus the ruling is nuanced: the status of ownership depends on which Hanafi position is adopted. The Urdu translation and explanation further clarify this.

Key Terms
موقوف (mawquf): The property that is endowed; it leaves the wakif's ownership but does not become the property of the beneficiaries.
موقوف عليه (mawquf ‘alayh): The beneficiary of a waqf; they do not own the property but are entitled to its benefits.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (the relied-upon position), what is the ownership status of an endowed property after a valid waqf?
A) It remains the property of the wakif.
B) It becomes the property of the beneficiary.
C) It leaves the wakif's ownership but does not enter the beneficiary's ownership.
D) It becomes joint property of the wakif and beneficiaries.

Key Takeaway
Endowed property is removed from the wakif's ownership and does not vest in the beneficiaries; it is considered owned by Allah in trust, according to the Sahibayn's view adopted in the Hanafi school.

Waqf of Undivided Property (Musha‘) – Abu Yusuf vs. Muhammad
Intra-Hanafi dispute on musha‘ waqf with proofs and exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on waqf of musha‘, explain the role of qabd, and apply the rulings to indivisible property, mosques, and partial istihqaq.

Core Idea
Validity of waqf of undivided property depends on whether qabd is a condition: Abu Yusuf says no; Muhammad says yes.

Waqf of shared property (musha‘) is a classic intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The core difference lies in whether possession (qabd) is a condition for waqf. This lesson unpacks their arguments, exceptions for indivisible property, and the unique treatment of mosques and cemeteries.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
What exactly is being contested? It is the validity of waqf of undivided property that is capable of division (e.g., half a house).
The dispute does not apply to property that cannot be divided (e.g., a narrow lane).
2
State Abu Yusuf's position and proof
Abu Yusuf says ja’iz (valid). He argues that division is merely a completion of possession, and since possession is not a condition for waqf, its completion is also not required.
His key phrase: 'al-qismatu min tamam al-qabd'.
3
State Muhammad's position and proof
Muhammad says la yajuz (invalid) for divisible property. He treats possession as a condition, so whatever completes it (division) becomes mandatory for validity.
His key phrase: 'asl al-qabd 'indahu shart'.
4
Examine the exceptions
For indivisible property, Muhammad allows waqf (by analogy to gift/charity). For mosques and cemeteries, even Abu Yusuf prohibits musha‘ because partnership prevents exclusive dedication and alternate use (muhaya‘a) is repugnant.
Example of repugnant muhaya‘a: using land for burial one year and farming the next.
5
Analyse partial istihqaq (post-waqf claim)
Muhammad says if a part of the waqf property is later claimed and taken, the waqf becomes void in the remainder because the undividedness existed from the start. But if the taken part is specific and distinguishable, it does not void the rest.
This is compared to gift (hiba) rules.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَوَقْفُ الْمُشَاعِ جَائِزٌ عِندَ أَبِى يُوسُفَ لِأَنَّ الْقِسْمَةَ مِنْ تَمَامِ الْقَبْضِ وَالْقَبْضُ عِنْدَهُ لَيْسَ بِشَرْطٍ فَكَذَا تَيَمَّتُهُ وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ لا يَجُوزُلانَّ أَصْلَ الْقَبْضِ عِندَهُ شَرُطْ فَكَذَا مَايُتِمُّ بِهِ وَهذَا فِيمَا يَحْتَمِلُ الْقِسْمَةَ فَأَمَّا فِيمَا لَا يَحْتَمِلُ الْقِسْمَةَ فَيَجُوزُ مَعَ الشَّيُوعِ عِندَ مُحَمَّدٍ ايْضًا لِأَنَّهُ يَعْتَبِرُهُ بِالْهِبَةِ وَالصَّدَقَةِ الْمُنَفِّدَةِ إِلَّا فِي الْمَسْجِدِ وَ الْمَقْبَرَةِ فَإِنَّهُ لا يَتِمُّ مَعَ الشُّيُوعِ فِيمَا لَا يَحْتَمِلُ أَيْضًا عِندَ أَبِى يُوسُفَ لِأَنَّ بَقَاءَ الشَّرُكَةِ يَمْنَعُ الْخُلُوصَ لِلَّهِ تَعَالَى وَلَانَّ المُهَايَاةَ فِيهِمَا فِي غَايَةِ الْقُبْح بأن يُقْبَرَفِيهِ الْمَوْتَى سَنَةً وَيُزْرَعَ سَنَةً وَيُصَلَّى فِيهِ فِي وَقْتِ وَيُتَّخَذَ إِصْطَبَلَا فِي وَقتٍ بِخِلَافِ الْوَقْفِ لإمكان الاسْتَغْلالِ وَقِسُمَةِ الْعَلَّةِ وَلَوْوَقَفَ الْكُلَّ ثُمَّ اسْتُحِقَّ جُزءٌ مِّنْهُ بَطَلَ فِي الْبَاقِي عِندَ مُحَمَّدٍ لِأَنَّ الشُّيُوعَ مُقَارَةٌ كَمَا فِي الْهِبَةِ بِخَلافِ مَا إِذَا رَجَعَ الْوَاهِبُ فِي الْبَعْضِ أَوْ رَجَعَ الْوَارِثُ فِي الظُّلْتَيْنِ بَعْدَ مَوْتَ الْمَرِيضَ وَقَدْوَهَبَ أوْ وَقَفَ فِى مَرَضِهِ وَفِى الْمَالِ ضَيْقٌ لِأَنَّ الشَّيُوعَ فِي ذَالِكَ طَارِى وَلَوِ اسْتُحِقَّ جُزء مُمَيَّزَ بِعَيْنِهِ لَمْ يَبْطُلُ فِي الْبَاقِي لِعَدَمِ الشُّيُوعِ وَلِهَذَا جَازَ فِي الْابْتِدَاءِ وَعَلَى هَذَا الْهِبَة وَالصَّدَقَة الْمَمْلُوكَة
He said: Waqf of undivided property (musha‘) is valid according to Abu Yusuf because division is a completion of possession, and possession according to him is not a condition, so likewise its completion. And Muhammad said: It is not valid because the basis of possession according to him is a condition, so likewise what completes it. And this is regarding what admits division. As for what does not admit division, it is valid despite undividedness according to Muhammad as well, because he analogizes it to executed gift and charity. Except for mosque and cemetery, for they are not completed with undividedness even in what does not admit division, according to Abu Yusuf, because the continuation of partnership prevents exclusive dedication to Allah, and because alternate use (muhaya’a) in them is extremely repugnant, such as burying the dead in it one year and planting crops another year, or praying in it at one time and taking it as a stable at another time. This is unlike waqf because exploitation and division of the produce are possible. And if one waqfs the whole and then a part of it is taken by way of istihqaq (claim), it becomes void in the remaining part according to Muhammad because the undividedness is simultaneous (muqarana), as in gift. Unlike the case where the donor takes back part (ruju‘) or the heir takes back the two-thirds after the death of the sick person who made a gift or waqf during his illness and the estate becomes constrained, because the undividedness there is subsequent (tari’). And if a specific, distinguishable part is taken, it does not become void in the remaining part because there is no undividedness, and for this reason it is valid at the outset. The same applies to gift and owned charity.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage is a detailed intra-Hanafi dispute on the validity of waqf of musha‘ (undivided or joint property). The matn states: Abu Yusuf permits waqf of divisible musha‘ because he does not require possession (qabd) for waqf; division of shares is merely a completion. Muhammad prohibits it because he requires possession as a condition, and undivided property cannot be possessed. For property that is not divisible by nature (e.g., a narrow road, small well), both allow it, analogizing to gift and charity. However, for mosques and cemeteries, Abu Yusuf further restricts even for indivisible property because partnership prevents exclusive dedication to Allah, and alternate use (muhaya’a) is repugnant (e.g., using the same land for burial and farming alternately). The passage also discusses partial istihqaq (recovery) after waqf: if a part is claimed and recovered, Muhammad says the waqf becomes void in the remaining part because the undividedness existed from the start (muqarana). But if a specific part is recovered, no voidness. This is compared to gift and charity.

Key Terms
مشاع (musha‘): Undivided property that is shared among co-owners, not yet partitioned into specific shares.
قبض (qabd): Possession or taking delivery of the property; a condition for validity of waqf according to Muhammad, but not according to Abu Yusuf.
مهاياة (muhaya’a): Alternate use of a shared property by the partners, e.g., using land for burial one year and farming the next.
استحقاق (istihqaq): Claim or recovery of part of a property by a third party, e.g., when a previous owner proves ownership.
مقارنة (muqarana): Simultaneous (undividedness from the start), as opposed to ‘tari‘’ (subsequent).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Muhammad al-Shaybani, what is the ruling on waqf of divisible undivided property (musha‘)?
A) Valid without any conditions
B) Invalid because possession (qabd) is a condition
C) Valid only for agricultural land
D) Invalid unless approved by the local qadi

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has a genuine internal difference on musha‘ waqf rooted in the role of qabd; knowing both positions is essential for sound fatwa practice.

Waqf — Endowment
intermediate
6 min
Waqf's Effect on Ownership: Sahibayn vs. Abu Hanifa
Clarifying that al-Quduri's statement about waqf leaving ownership applies to Sahibayn's view

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi positions on whether waqf removes ownership from the waqif and identify which position is the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Waqf's effect on ownership is disputed: Sahibayn say it leaves the waqif's ownership; Abu Hanifa says it remains.

The passage you are about to study is from al-Hidayah's commentary on al-Quduri's matn. It addresses a central intra-Hanafi dispute: does waqf remove the property from the waqif's ownership? The matn states that it does, but the commentator clarifies that this is the view of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), not of Abu Hanifa. Understanding this distinction is crucial for applying the correct ruling in waqf matters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Recognize that Abu Hanifa holds the corpus remains in the ownership of the waqif, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that it leaves his ownership entirely.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
2
Analyze the proof (dalil)
The passage provides a rational proof: if the beneficiary owned the waqf property, it would not be inalienable by the waqif's condition, just like ordinary property. Since the condition does prevent transfer, the beneficiary does not own it, implying the property has left the waqif's ownership.
This proof supports the Sahibayn's view.
3
Understand the commentator's clarification
Al-Marghinani notes that al-Quduri's statement 'it left the ownership of the waqif' must be understood as the view of the Sahibayn, not Abu Hanifa. This prevents misunderstanding the matn.
The matn is general, but the commentary adds specificity.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position for fatwa is that of the Sahibayn: waqf removes ownership. This is recorded in the Zahir al-Riwayah.
Authority weight: zahir riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ينْفُذُ بَيْعُهُ كَسَائِرِ أَمْلاكِهِ وَلِأنَّهُ لَوْ مَلَكَهُ لَمَّا انْتَقَلَ عَنْهُ بِشَرُطِ الْمَالِكِ الْأوَّلِ كَسَائِرِ أَمْلاكِهِ قَالَ وَقَوْلُهُ خَرَجَ عَنْ مِلْكِ الْوَاقِفِ يَجِبُ أَنْ يَكُونَ قَوْلَهُمَا عَلَى الْوَجْهِ الَّذِي سَبَقَ ذِكْرُهُ
His sale is valid like the rest of his properties. And because if he owned it, it would not transfer from him by the condition of the first owner like the rest of his properties. He said: And his statement 'it left the ownership of the waqif' must be their statement (i.e., of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) according to the manner previously mentioned.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage is from the commentary of al-Hidayah on al-Quduri's text. It addresses the nature of waqf's effect on ownership. The matn states that a waqf property, once valid, leaves the ownership of the waqif and does not enter the ownership of the beneficiaries. The proof offered is that if the beneficiary owned it, he could sell it like any other property, but the condition of the first owner prevents transfer. However, the commentator (al-Marghinani) clarifies that this statement of al-Quduri must be understood as the view of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), not that of Imam Abu Hanifa. According to Abu Hanifa, the ownership of the waqif remains on the corpus (raqaba) while the usufruct (manafi') is given to the beneficiaries. Thus, the ruling that waqf removes ownership entirely is specific to the Sahibayn. This is an important intra-Hanafi distinction: the ruling's legal effect differs depending on which Imams' view one follows.

Key Terms
وقف (waqf): The legal act of dedicating property for charitable or pious purposes in perpetuity, removing it from commercial circulation.
مِلْك (milk): Full ownership that allows the owner to dispose of the property as they wish, including sale.
صاحِبين (sahibayn): The two companions of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which Hanafi Imams hold that waqf removes the property from the waqif's ownership?
A) Abu Hanifa only
B) Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn)
C) All three Imams
D) Only Muhammad

Key Takeaway
Waqf's effect on ownership is disputed: the mufta bihi is that it leaves the waqif's ownership (Sahibayn's view), while Abu Hanifa holds the corpus remains in his ownership.
