Waqf — Endowment
intermediate
8 min
Waqf of Undivided Property: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on waqf musha'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding waqf musha', explain the role of possession and divisibility, and apply the distinction to determine the validity of a waqf.

Core Idea
Waqf musha' is valid for indivisible property, but for divisible property it depends on the imam's view on possession.

Waqf (endowment) of an undivided share in jointly owned property (waqf musha‘) presents a classic intra-Hanafi divergence. Imam Abu Yusuf permits it even before division, while Imam Muhammad requires prior division for divisible property. This lesson unpacks their reasoning and clarifies the operative ruling in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
Determine what exactly is disputed: the validity of endowing an undivided share (musha‘) without prior physical division or exclusive possession.
The dispute hinges on whether possession (qabd) is a condition for waqf.
2
State Abu Yusuf's position and reasoning
Abu Yusuf considers waqf musha‘ valid even before division because he does not require actual possession for the validity of waqf; the contract alone suffices.
For Abu Yusuf, division is only a requirement of possession, not a condition of the waqf itself.
3
State Muhammad's position and reasoning
Imam Muhammad requires possession for waqf; since possession of an undivided share is impossible without division, he deems waqf musha‘ invalid for divisible property.
Muhammad analogizes waqf to a gift (hiba), where possession is essential.
4
Apply the exception for non-divisible property
Both imams agree that if the property cannot be divided without losing its utility (e.g., a small room or pathway), waqf musha‘ is valid even according to Muhammad.
The test of divisibility is whether the property still serves its purpose after division.
5
Analyze the special case of mosques and graveyards
Abu Yusuf further rules that even for non-divisible land, waqf for a mosque or graveyard is invalid due to the inherent inappropriateness of shared use of such sacred spaces.
Other types of waqf (e.g., rental income) remain valid for non-divisible musha‘.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوقف
۲۴۸
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد هفتم دوسری جائیداد کے ساتھ ملی ہو اس کو بھی وقف کرنا امام ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک جائز ہے کیونکہ اس خاص حصہ کو دوسرے کے حصہ سے علیحدہ کر دینا یعنی بٹوارہ کر دینا اس پر قبضہ کر لینے کے لوازمات میں سے ہے۔ مگر ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک اس پر قبضہ کرنا ہی شرط نہیں ہے اس لئے قبضہ کے لئے جو تمہ اور لوازمات میں سے ہے وہ بھی شرط نہ ہوگا۔ بلکہ اس پر قبضہ سے پہلے ہی وہ زمین وقف ہو جائے گی۔ لیکن امام محمد رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ وقف مشاع جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ اصل قبضہ ان کے نزدیک شرط ہے اس لئے جس چیز سے قبضہ پورا ہو وہ بھی شرط ہے۔ یہ اختلاف ایسی جائیداد میں ہے جو قابل قسمت ہو( واضح ہو کہ اس سے مراد یہ ہے کہ قابل قسمت ایسی چیز جس کو تقسیم کرنے کے بعد بھی وہ مقصود حاصل ہو جو اس سے مطلوب اور منظور ہو۔ جیسے بڑا گھر بڑا کمرہ اور قابل تقسیم نہ ہونے کے معنی یہ ہوئے کہ تقسیم کر دینے کے بعد وہ چیز ایسی نہ رہے جس سے اس کا مقصود حاصل ہو جائے ۔ مثلاً چھوٹے کمرے، چھوٹے راستے ، چھوٹے پیالے۔ وغیرہ کہ ان کو تقسیم کر دینے کے بعد یہ چیزیں اپنے مقصود پورا کرنے کے قابل نہیں ۔ بلکہ کسی کے بھی کام کی نہیں رہتی ہیں ) اور جو چیز بٹوارے کے قابل نہ ہو تو اسے وقف کرنا امام محمد رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک بھی مشاع ہونے کے باوجود جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ امام محمد رحمتہ اللہ علیہ اس وقف کو ایسے بہ وصدقہ پر قیاس کرتے ہیں جو سپر د کر دیا گیا ہو یعنی جیسے ہمہ وصدقہ جائز ہو جاتا ہے اسی طرح جو چیز تقسیم ہونے کے قابل نہ ہو اس کو بھی وقف کرنا جائز ہے۔ پھر امام ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے مسجد اور مقبرہ کو متنی کیا ہے۔ یعنی اگر کسی ایسی مشترک زمین کو جو تقسیم ہونے کے قابل نہ ہو مسجد یا مقبرہ کے واسطے وقف کیا تو ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک بھی ایسی زمین جائز نہیں ہے جو تقسیم ہونے کے قابل نہ ہو۔ اس لئے کہ اس میں شرکت باقی رہنا خالصہ لوجہ اللہ ہونے سے مانع ہے۔ اور اس لئے بھی کہ مسجد اور قبرستان سے متعلق باری باری سے نفع اٹھانے کا معاہدہ کرنا بہت ہی بری سی بات ہے۔ اس طرح سے کہ مثلاً قبرستان میں ایک سال مردے دفن کئے جائیں اور دوسرے سال اس میں کھیتی کی جائے یا ایک وقت اس میں نماز پڑھی جائے اور دوسرے وقت وہ اصطبل بنا دیا جائے ۔ جبکہ وہ بٹوارے کے قابل نہیں ہے بخلاف مسجد اور مقبرہ کے دوسرے طور پر وقف جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ مکن ہے کہ کرایہ یا اجارہ یا زراعت وغیرہ سے اس کی پیداوار اور منافع لے کر آپس میں تقسیم کر لی جائے ۔ یعنی جو وقف کا حصہ ہو وہ وقف کر دیا جائے۔
Book of Waqf. 248. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary of Hidayah Volume Seven: If a property is mixed with another property, then endowing it is permissible according to Imam Abu Yusuf, because separating that specific portion from the other's portion, i.e., dividing it, is among the requirements of taking possession. But according to Abu Yusuf, taking possession itself is not a condition; therefore, what is a preliminary and requirement for possession will also not be a condition. Rather, that land will become waqf before possession. However, Imam Muhammad said that waqf of musha' (undivided share) is not permissible, because actual possession is a condition according to him; thus, that by which possession is completed is also a condition. This disagreement is regarding property that is divisible (qabil-e qismat). (It is clear that by 'divisible' is meant something which, after division, still fulfills the intended purpose, like a large house or large room; and 'not divisible' means that after division it no longer serves its purpose, e.g., small rooms, small pathways, small bowls, etc., which after division cannot fulfill their purpose and become useless.) And something that is not divisible, its endowment is permissible according to Imam Muhammad even though it is musha', because Imam Muhammad analogizes this waqf to a gift or charity that has been handed over. So just as a gift/charity becomes valid, similarly endowing something not divisible is valid. Then Imam Abu Yusuf excludes mosque and graveyard. That is, if an undivided land that is not divisible is endowed as a mosque or graveyard, then according to Abu Yusuf too it is not permissible, because the persistence of partnership prevents it from being purely for the sake of Allah. Also because making an agreement to benefit alternately from a mosque or graveyard is very bad, e.g., one year burying dead in the graveyard and the next year cultivating it, or one time praying in it and another time making it a stable. Since it is not divisible, unlike other ways of endowing a mosque or graveyard, it is permissible because it is possible to take its produce and profit through rent, lease, or cultivation and divide among themselves – i.e., the share that is waqf is endowed.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of endowing an undivided share (waqf musha'). Imam Abu Yusuf holds that waqf musha' is valid even before division and possession, because he does not consider possession a condition for the validity of waqf. Imam Muhammad requires actual possession, and since possession of an undivided share is not possible without division, he deems waqf musha' invalid for divisible property. However, both agree that if the property is not divisible (such as a small room or pathway), then waqf musha' is valid even according to Imam Muhammad, by analogy to a gift that is handed over. Abu Yusuf further makes an exception for mosques and graveyards: even if the land is not divisible, waqf for these purposes is invalid because the continued partnership prevents pure devotion to Allah and leads to improper alternation of use. For other types of waqf, the income from the undivided share can be collected and used.

Key Terms
وقف مشاع (waqf musha'): Endowment of an undivided share in a property that is owned jointly with others.
قابل قسمت (qabil-e qismat): Property that can be divided without losing its intended utility.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, what kind of undivided property can be validly endowed as waqf?
A) Only property that is divisible
B) Only property that is not divisible
C) Both divisible and non-divisible property
D) Neither divisible nor non-divisible property

Key Takeaway
The validity of waqf musha‘ hinges on divisibility: it is invalid for divisible property (mufta bihi) but valid for non-divisible property, with a special exception from Abu Yusuf for mosques and graveyards.

Waqf — Endowment
intermediate
8 min
Validity of Waqf When a Third-Party Right is Later Proven
Ruling on waqf validity upon later claim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when a waqf remains valid despite a later claim and when it becomes invalid, and apply the same ruling to hiba and sadaqah.

Core Idea
If a claimed portion is specific, the waqf stands; if undivided, the waqf collapses.

A person endows a piece of land, but later it emerges that another person has a right to part of that land. Does this invalidate the entire endowment? The answer hinges on whether the claimed portion is a specific, demarcated piece (mu'ayyan) or an undivided share (musha'). This lesson unpacks Imam Muhammad's ruling, its reasoning, and its extension to gifts and charities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the transaction and the claim
Determine whether the original act was a waqf, hiba, or sadaqah mamlukah. Then identify that a third party has proven ownership of a part of the property.
2
Determine the nature of the claimed portion
Is the claimed portion specific (mu'ayyan), i.e., physically separated and distinct from the rest? Or is it an undivided share (musha'), mixed with the whole?
This distinction is decisive.
3
Apply the ruling based on the nature
If the portion is specific and separate, the claimant takes that portion, and the transaction (waqf, gift, or charity) on the remainder remains valid. If the portion is undivided, the entire transaction becomes invalid (batil).
Imam Muhammad's ruling.
4
Consider the timing of partnership
If there was no partnership at the time of the transaction but partnership arises later (e.g., due to revocation of part, or because the donor was sick and the heirs' share is determined later), the transaction remains valid. Partnership ex post facto does not invalidate.
Exception to the general rule.
5
Analogize to hiba and sadaqah
The same distinction applies to gifts and charities. If a gift is given and later a third party proves ownership of an undivided share, the entire gift is invalid. If the share is specific, only that portion is excluded.
Consistency across similar transactions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسئلہ اگر ایک شخص نے زمین کا پورا ایک ٹکڑا اوقف کیا۔ بعد میں یہ ثابت ہوا کہ اس کی ایک تہائی یا چوتھائی یا کسی جزو کا دوسرا کوئی شخص مستحق ہے تو امام محمد رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک باقی حصہ کا وقف بھی باطل ہو گیا۔ کیونکہ یہ ثابت ہوگیا کہ وقف کرنے کے وقت و ونکڑ امشاع اور مشترک تھا۔ جیسے ہبہ میں ہوتا ہے۔ یعنی ہبہ مشاع ہو کہ اس میں ہبہ کے وقت اشتراک پایا جارہا ہو تو وہ ہبہ باطل ہو جاتا ہے۔ بخلاف اس کے جب بہہ کے وقت شیوع نہ ہو بلکہ بعد میں کسی طرح اشتراک پایا جائے تو وہ ہبہ باطل نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ جیسے کسی نے پوری زمین پہلے جہیہ کر دی مگر بعد میں اس ہبہ کرنے والے نے اس میں سے تھوڑے سے حصہ سے رجوع کر لیا یا مریض نے مرض کی حالت میں ہبہ یا وقف کیا لیکن بعد میں معلوم ہوا کہ اس کے سوا اس کی دوسری کوئی زمین نہیں ہے جو ترکہ ہو سکے اور اس کے لحاظ سے یہ ایک ثلث ہو سکے ۔ جب بھی یہ ہبہ یا وقف باطل نہ ہوگا کیونکہ اس میں ورثہ کی شرکت بعد میں ثابت ہو رہی ہے۔ اور اتنا حصہ جس کا استحقاق اس میں سے ثابت ہوا ہے کوئی معین اور مختار ہو یعنی دوسرے باقی حصہ سے بالکل علیحدہ ہو تو باقی کا وقف باطل نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں حقیقت میں اشتراک اور شیوع نہیں پایا گیا ہے۔ اسی لئے ابتداء میں باقی کا وقف جائز تھا۔ اور یہی حالت ہبہ اور صدقہ مملوکہ کی ہے۔ یعنی اگر اس عہد کے کسی مشترک حصہ میں کسی کا حق ثابت ہوا تو وہ ہبہ اور صدقہ باطل ہوگا۔ اور اگر کوئی معین حصہ ایسا مشترک ثابت ہوا تو وہ باطل نہ ہوگا۔

۲۴۹
كتاب الوقف
اشرف الهدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ہفتم خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے کوئی چیز وقف یا ہبہ کی پھر اس میں سے کسی جزو پر کسی شخص کا دعوی ثابت ہوگیا تو دیکھنا چاہئے کہ وہ حصہ یا جزو دوسرے قبضہ سے علیحدہ اور ممتاز ہے تو وہ حصہ اسی حقدار اور مدعی کا ہو جائے گا اور باقی حصہ کا وقف یا ہبہ ثابت اور قائم رہ جائے گا۔ اور اگر وہ حصہ معین نہ ہو بلکہ سب میں ملا جلا اور مشترک ہو تو وہ وقف اور ہبہ باطل ہو جائے گا اور اگر وقف یا ہبہ کے وقت شرکت بالکل نہ ہو مگر کسی بھی صورت سے اس میں بعد میں شرکت پیدا ہوگئی ہوتو باقی کا وقف اور ہبہ قائم رہے گا۔
Issue: If a person endows an entire piece of land, and later it is proven that one-third or one-fourth or some part of it is claimed by another person, then according to Imam Muhammad, the waqf of the remaining portion also becomes invalid, because it is established that at the time of waqf the piece was undivided and shared. This is like in the case of a gift: if the gift is undivided and sharing exists at the time of gift, then that gift becomes invalid. Conversely, if there was no undividedness at the time of gift but later sharing occurs, then the gift is not invalid. For example, someone gives a whole land as a gift, but later the donor revokes a small portion from it; or a sick person makes a gift or waqf during his illness, and later it is known that he had no other land besides that which could be inheritance, and thus it amounts to one-third of his estate. In such cases, the gift or waqf will not be invalid because the heirs' share is proven later. And if the portion proven to be claimed is specific and distinct, i.e., completely separate from the remaining portion, then the waqf of the remainder is not invalid, because in that case there is no actual undividedness. Therefore, initially the waqf of the remainder was valid. The same rule applies to gift and charity (sadaqah mamlukah). Summary: If someone makes a waqf or gift, then a claim on some part of it is proven, then look: if that part is separate and distinct from the rest, then that part goes to the claimant and the waqf or gift of the remainder stands. If the part is not specific but mixed and common, then the entire waqf or gift becomes invalid. If there was no partnership at the time of waqf or gift, but later partnership arises in any way, then the waqf or gift of the remainder remains valid.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on what happens when a third party's right to a portion of an endowed or gifted property is established after the endowment or gift. The key distinction is whether the claimed portion is specific (mu'ayyan) or undivided (musha'). If it is specific and separate, the claimant takes that portion and the waqf or gift on the rest remains valid. If it is undivided (i.e., a share in the whole), then the entire endowment or gift becomes invalid because the property was partly owned by another at the time of the transaction. The same rule applies to gifts and charities. Additionally, if the partnership arises after the transaction (e.g., due to revocation of part or because of inheritance shares in the case of a sick person's donation), the transaction remains valid.

Key Terms
وقف (waqf): Endowment of property in the way of Allah, removing it from ownership.
ہبہ (hiba): Gift, transfer of ownership without compensation.
مشاع (musha'): Undivided share in a property, not physically demarcated.
معین (mu'ayyan): Specific, distinct portion of property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man endows a building. Later, it is found that his cousin owns a specific apartment in that building at the time of endowment. What happens to the endowment on the remaining apartments?
A) The entire endowment is invalid
B) Only that apartment is excluded; the rest remains valid
C) The endowment is invalid unless the cousin agrees
D) The endowment becomes a trust for both

Key Takeaway
When a third party's right to part of an endowed or gifted property is later proven, the transaction remains valid on the remainder if the claimed portion is specific; the entire transaction becomes invalid if the claimed portion is an undivided share.

Waqf — Endowment
intermediate
12 min
Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Ta'bid in Waqf
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ta'bid in waqf with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf on ta'bid in waqf, explain the dalil of each, and identify the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position.

Core Idea
The word 'waqf' itself implies perpetuity; explicit mention of ta'bid is not required per the relied-upon view.

Waqf is a unique form of charity that removes ownership without transferring it. A key question: must the waqf specify that the benefit continues forever, or is perpetuality inherent? This lesson unpacks the intra-Hanafi dispute between the two disciples and their master, and reveals which view is considered sahih.

Guided Path
1
State the three positions
Identify the positions of Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf on whether explicit mention of perpetuity (ta'bid) is required for a valid waqf.
Be precise: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad require the ultimate channel to be perpetual; Abu Yusuf does not require explicit mention.
2
Analyze Abu Hanifa and Muhammad's dalil
They analogize waqf to emancipation (itq): both remove ownership without transfer and are inherently perpetual. A temporary channel or time limit defeats the purpose, like a time-bound sale.
Note the qiyas to itq and to bay' (sale).
3
Analyze Abu Yusuf's dalil
Abu Yusuf argues the purpose is taqarrub (nearness to Allah), which can be achieved even with a temporary channel. The word 'waqf' itself implies perpetuity, so explicit mention is unnecessary.
He also adds that if the named channel ceases, the proceeds go to the poor by default.
4
Evaluate the tarjih
The text declares that the correct (sahih) view is that of Abu Yusuf. Understand why later scholars preferred his view: it aligns with the broader objectives of waqf and avoids invalidating many endowments.
This tarjih is from a later commentary, not the Zahir al-Riwayah.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The operative position for fatwa today is Abu Yusuf's: explicit ta'bid is not a condition; waqf is valid even if the initial beneficiary is temporary, and after extinction it goes to the poor.
Be aware that Muhammad's stricter view still appears in some texts, but it is not relied upon.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقف تام کب ہوتا ہے
قَالَ وَ لَا يَتِمُ الْوَقْفُ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ حَتَّى يَجْعَلَ اخِرَهُ بِجِهَةٍ لَا تَنْقَطِعُ أَبَداَوَ قَالَ أَبُويُوسفَ إِذَا سَمَّى فِيهِ جهَةً تَنْقَطِعُ جَازَ وَ صَارَ بَعْدَهَا لِلْفُقَرَاءِ وَإِنْ لَمْ يُسَمِهِمْ لَهُمَا أَنَّ مُوْجَبَ الْوَقْفِ زَوَالُ الْمِلْكِ بِدُونِ التَمليك وَأَنَّهُ يَتَأَبَّدُ كَالْعِتْقِ فَإِذَا كَانَتِ الْجِهَةُ يَتَوَهَّمُ اِنْقِطَاعُهَا لَا يَتَوَ فَرْعَلَيْهِ مُقْتَضَاهُ فَلِهَذَا كَانَ التَّوقِيتُ مُبْطِلًا لَهُ كَالتَّوْقِيتِ فِي الْبَيْعِ وَلِأَبِى يُوسُفَ أَنَّ الْمُقْصُودَ هُوَ التَقَرُّبُ إِلَى اللهِ تَعَالَى وَهُوَ مُوَقَرْ عَلَيْهِ لأَنَّ التَّقَرُّبُ تَارَةً يَكُونُ فِى الصَّرِف إِلى جِهَةِ تَنْقَطِعُ وَمَرَةَ بِالصَّرْفِ إِلى جِهَةٍ تَتَابَدُ فَيَصِحُ فِى الْوَجْهَيْن وَقِيلَ إِنَّ التَّابِيْدِ شَرْط بِالْإِجْمَاعِ إِلَّا أَنَّ عِنْدَ أَبِى يُوسُفَ لَا يُشْتَرَطُ ذَكَرُ التَّابِيْدِ لا نَ لَفَظَةَ الْوَقفِ وَالصَّدَقَةِ مُنَيَةٌ عَنْهُ لَمَا بَيَّنَا أَنَّهُ إِزَالَهُ اَلْمُلْكِ يَدُونَ السَّمْلِيْكِ كَالْعِتْقِ وَلِهَذَا قَالَ فِي الْكِتَابِ فِي بَيَانِ قَوْلِهِ وَصَارَ بَعْدَهَا لِلْفُقَرَاءِ وَإِن لَّمْ يُسَمِهـ وهذا هو الصَّحِيحُ وَعِندَ مُحَمَّدٍ ذكرُ التَّابِيْدِ شَرْطَ لِأَنَّ هَذَا صَدَقَةٌ بِالْمَنْفَعَةِ أو بالغَلَةِ وَذَالِکَ قَدْيَكُور فَدْيَكُونُ مُؤقتاً وَقَدْيَكُونُ مُوَبَّدَ افَمُطْلَقَهُ لَا يَنْصَرِفُ إِلَى التَّابِي فَلَا بُدَّ مِنَ التَّنْصِيصِ
ترجمہ قدوری رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ امام ابو حنیفہ ومحمد رحمتہ اللہ علیہا کے نزدیک وقف کا کام اس وقت پورا ہوگا کہ اس کے آخر میں یہ بتا دیا جائے کہ اس کا مصرف ایسا کام ہو گا جو بھی ختم ہونے والا نہ ہو۔ (اور وہ ایسا مصرف نہ ہو جو ایک وقت میں اس طرح ہو جائے کہ اس میں خرچ کرنے کا موقع باقی نہ رہے مثلا یہ کہ دینا کہ یہ مال فقراء اور مساکین اور دینی طلبہ کی تعلیم میں خرچ کیا جائے کہ یہ سلسلہ کبھی بھی ختم ہونے والا نہ ہو گا ۔ اور ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے کہا ہے کہ اس کے برخلاف ہونے سے بھی (مثلا یہ مال میرے بیٹوں میرے بھائیوں پر یا صرف فلاں مد میں خرچ کیا جائے جو کچھ دنوں بعد بند اور ختم ہو سکتا ہے اور رشتہ داری کا سلسلہ بھی منقطع بھی ہو سکتا ہے۔ تو ایسا ہونے سے بھی وقف جائز ہو جائے گا۔ البتہ اگر وہ مخصوص رشتہ دار یا مدرسہ کسی وقت نا پید ہو جائے تو اس کے بعد عام فقراء و مساکین و مدارس میں خرچ کیا جاسکے گا۔ اگر چہ اس نے کھل کر فقراء کا نام نہ لیا ہو ۔ امام ابوحنیفہ محمد رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ وقف کا کام تو صرف یہ لازم کرنا ہوتا ہے کہ اب وقف کرنے والے کی ملکیت اس پر باقی نہیں رہے گی بلکہ ختم ہو جائے گی۔ اس کے بغیر کہ وہ دوسرے شخص کی ملکیت میں جائے ۔ اور یہ ہمیشہ رہنے والی بات ہے جیسے غلام کی آزادی ہمیشہ کے لئے ہو جاتی ہے۔ پس جب واقف نے اپنے وقف کے لئے ایسا مصرف مقرر کر دیا جس کے ختم ہو جانے کا وہم ہو تو وقف کا اصل مقصد اس سے پورا نہ ہوگا ۔ اسی واسطے اگر وقف کو کسی مخصوص یا متعین وقت تک کے لئے کیا ہو مثلاً دس یا پندرہ برس تو یہ وقت مقرر کرنا اس کو باطل کر دیتا ہے۔ جیسے کہ دس دنوں تک کے لئے کسی چیز کو فروخت کرنا باطل ہوتا ہے۔ اور امام ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ وقف کا مقصود صرف یہ ہوتا ہے کہ بارگاہ انہی میں تقرب حاصل ہو۔ اور یہ بات وقف کرنے سے پورے طور پر صادق آتی ہے ۔ کیونکہ تقرب کا حصول کبھی اس طرح سے ہوتا
When does waqf become complete? He (al-Quduri) said: Waqf does not become complete according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad until he makes its ultimate destination a channel that never ceases. And Abu Yusuf said: If he mentions a channel that ceases, it is valid, and after it becomes for the poor, even if he did not name them. For them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), the requirement of waqf is the removal of ownership without transfer of ownership, and it is perpetual like emancipation. So if the channel is likely to cease, its requirement is not fulfilled; therefore, specifying a time invalidates it, like specifying a time in sale. And for Abu Yusuf, the purpose is drawing near to Allah Almighty, and that is achieved, because drawing near sometimes occurs by spending to a channel that ceases and sometimes to a channel that is perpetual; thus it is valid in both cases. It is said that perpetuity (ta'bid) is a condition by consensus, except that according to Abu Yusuf, the explicit mention of perpetuity is not required because the word 'waqf' and 'sadaqah' suffice for it, as we explained that it is removal of ownership without transfer, like emancipation. Therefore, the author said in the book clarifying his statement: 'And it becomes after that for the poor, even if he did not name them.' This is the correct view. And according to Muhammad, the mention of perpetuity is a condition, because this is a charity of benefit or produce, and that may be temporary or perpetual; its absolute form does not imply perpetuity, so specification is necessary.
Translation: Al-Quduri said: According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, the act of waqf is complete only when at its end he specifies a channel that will never cease. (And it should not be such that after some time there is no scope to spend, e.g., saying 'this wealth is to be spent on the poor, the needy, and the education of religious students' because this series will never end.) And Abu Yusuf said that even if it is the opposite (e.g., 'this wealth is to be spent on my sons, my brothers, or only on such-and-such project' which may cease after some time and the relationship may end), then also the waqf becomes valid. However, if those specified relatives or school become extinct, then after that it can be spent on the general poor and needy and schools, even if he did not explicitly name the poor. The proof of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: The effect of waqf is that the ownership of the waqf-giver ceases forever without transfer to someone else, and it is perpetual like emancipation. So when the waqf-giver specifies a channel that is likely to cease, the essential requirement is not fulfilled. Therefore, specifying a time invalidates it, just as specifying a time in a sale invalidates it. And the proof of Abu Yusuf: The purpose of waqf is only to attain closeness to Allah, and that is completely achieved by making waqf, because closeness can be attained sometimes by spending to a channel that ceases and sometimes to a perpetual channel. So it is valid in both cases.
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage presents a fundamental intra-Hanafi dispute on whether waqf requires the specification of a perpetual (permanent) beneficiary. Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad hold that for waqf to be complete, the ultimate destination (jiha) must be one that never ends, such as the poor, mosques, or public utilities. If the waqf is made for a limited time or for a group that may die out, it is invalid. They analogize waqf to emancipation (itq), which is inherently perpetual. Specifying a time would be like a time-bound sale, which is void. Abu Yusuf argues that the essence of waqf is to seek nearness to Allah, and that can be achieved even if the initial beneficiary is temporary. Once that beneficiary ceases, the proceeds go to the poor by default. He does not require explicit mention of perpetuity because the very word 'waqf' implies perpetuity. Imam Muhammad, however, requires explicit mention of ta'bid because he considers waqf as a charity of usufruct, which can be temporary; hence absolute wording does not imply perpetuity. The relied-upon (sahih) position according to the text is that of Abu Yusuf.

Key Terms
تأبید (ta'bid): Perpetuity; the condition that the benefit of the waqf continues indefinitely.
جہة (jiha): Channel or destination for the proceeds of the waqf; the ultimate beneficiary.
وقت (waqt): Time limit; specifying a duration for the waqf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (sahih) position in the Hanafi school, if someone endows a property for his children, and upon their extinction for the poor, but he does not explicitly say 'for the poor', what is the ruling?
A) The waqf is invalid because the ultimate channel is not perpetual
B) The waqf is valid, and after the children die out, it goes to the poor even without explicit mention
C) The waqf is valid only if he explicitly mentions the poor
D) The waqf becomes invalid because the children are not a perpetual channel

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the relied-upon position is that waqf does not require explicit mention of perpetuity; the word 'waqf' itself suffices to make it perpetual, and a temporary channel defaults to the poor.

10 min
Effect of a Claim on Part of Waqf or Hiba Property
States the ruling when part of waqf/hiba is claimed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule regarding claims on part of waqf or hiba property by distinguishing between separable and inseparable portions.

Core Idea
A claim on part of waqf voids the whole only if the part is inseparable; otherwise only that part is removed.

When a person makes a waqf or gives a hiba, their ownership ends and the property transfers. But what if someone later proves ownership of a part of that property? Does the entire endowment collapse? The Hanafi school provides a nuanced answer based on whether the claimed part is physically distinct and separable. This lesson unpacks that ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claimed part
First, determine if the part that is claimed is physically separate and distinct from the rest of the property or if it is intermixed and inseparable.
For example, a specific room in a building vs. an undivided share of land.
2
If separate: apply the rule of removal
If the claimed part is distinct, it is given to the claimant, and the remaining property continues as waqf or hiba. The transfer was valid on the portion that the transferor actually owned at the time.
3
If mixed: apply the rule of invalidity
If the claimed part is not separable (mixed with the whole), the entire waqf or hiba becomes void because the property was not fully owned and the contract cannot be executed partially without confusion.
4
Consider timing of mixing
If there was no mixing at the time of waqf/hiba but it occurred later (e.g., after the transfer), the original waqf/hiba remains valid on the portion not claimed. Later events do not retroactively invalidate it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے کوئی چیز وقف یا ہبہ کی پھر اس میں سے کسی جزو پر کسی شخص کا دعوی ثابت ہوگیا تو دیکھنا چاہئے کہ وہ حصہ یا جزو دوسرے قبضہ سے علیحدہ اور ممتاز ہے تو وہ حصہ اسی حقدار اور مدعی کا ہو جائے گا اور باقی حصہ کا وقف یا ہبہ ثابت اور قائم رہ جائے گا۔ اور اگر وہ حصہ معین نہ ہو بلکہ سب میں ملا جلا اور مشترک ہو تو وہ وقف اور ہبہ باطل ہو جائے گا اور اگر وقف یا ہبہ کے وقت شرکت بالکل نہ ہو مگر کسی بھی صورت سے اس میں بعد میں شرکت پیدا ہوگئی ہوتو باقی کا وقف اور ہبہ قائم رہے گا۔
The summary is that if someone made a waqf or hiba of something, then a claim of someone is proven on a part of it, then it should be seen: if that part or portion is separate and distinct from the other possession, then that part will belong to that rightful claimant, and the waqf or hiba of the remaining part will remain established and valid. And if that part is not specified but rather mixed and common in everything, then that waqf and hiba will become void. And if at the time of waqf or hiba there was no sharing at all, but later sharing occurs in some way, then the waqf and hiba of the rest will remain valid.
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This is a ruling statement explaining the effect of a proven claim on a part of waqf or hiba property. The key distinction is whether the claimed part is physically distinct and separable. If it is separate, only that part is taken by the claimant, and the rest remains as waqf or hiba. If the claimed part is mixed and inseparable from the whole, the entire waqf or hiba becomes void because the owner's property has been usurped and the waqf cannot be completed. Finally, if there was no mixing at the time of the transfer but mixing occurred later (e.g., after the waqf was made), the original waqf remains valid on the portion that was not claimed, as the mixing is a later event that does not retroactively invalidate the waqf.

Key Terms
وقف (waqf): The act of dedicating property for charitable purposes, removing it from one's ownership.
ہبہ (hiba): A gift made by one person to another, transferring ownership.
شرکت (shirkah): Partnership or mixing of property, here referring to the claimed part being mixed with the rest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone makes a waqf of a piece of land, and later a person proves ownership of a portion that is distinct and separable, what happens to the waqf?
A) The entire waqf becomes void.
B) The claimed portion is given to the claimant and the rest remains waqf.
C) The waqf is void unless the claimant is a relative.
D) The waqf remains valid but the original owner must compensate the beneficiary.

Key Takeaway
The validity of a waqf or hiba when part is claimed depends on physical separability: if distinct, only that part is removed; if mixed, the whole is void.

The Condition of Perpetuity in Waqf: Abu Hanifa vs Abu Yusuf vs Muhammad
Explains the ikhtilaf among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad on ta'bid in waqf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on ta'bid in waqf, apply the proofs from qiyas and purpose, and identify the mufta bihi position on the dispute.

Core Idea
Perpetuity is essential for waqf, but Abu Yusuf allows temporary beneficiaries—after they end, the property goes to the poor.

This passage from al-Hidayah presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a waqf must be explicitly perpetual (mu'abbad) to be valid. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad require that the beneficiary class never terminate, while Abu Yusuf accepts temporary beneficiaries, with the property eventually reverting to the poor. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to apply Hanafi principles of qiyas and maqasid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its hukm
The act is waqf (endowment). The dispute is whether a waqf that does not explicitly designate a perpetual beneficiary is valid (sahih) or invalid (batil).
The default ruling for waqf is that it is a binding charitable act; the question is its validity with temporary beneficiaries.
2
State the three Hanafi positions
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: Waqf is invalid if the beneficiary may terminate (e.g., children who might die out). Abu Yusuf: Waqf is valid even with a temporary beneficiary; after termination it goes to the poor.
Muhammad also requires explicit mention of perpetuity; Abu Yusuf says the word 'waqf' itself implies perpetuity.
3
Analyze the proof for Abu Hanifa and Muhammad
They argue by qiyas: waqf is like 'itq (manumission) – ownership is removed without transfer, and both require perpetuity. Also like a timed sale (bay' mu'aqqat), which is invalid.
The illa is: removal of ownership without tamlik necessitates perpetuity; timing contradicts that.
4
Analyze the proof for Abu Yusuf
Abu Yusuf focuses on the purpose (qurbah): nearness to Allah can be achieved by spending on either a temporary or perpetual cause. The word 'waqf' itself denotes perpetuity, so explicit mention is not needed.
He uses istihsan? Not explicitly, but he prioritizes the objective over the qiyas of 'itq.
5
Determine the tarjih and thamarah al-khilaf
The text declares Abu Yusuf's view as correct (al-sahih) regarding the validity of the waqf when the beneficiary ends. The practical difference: a waqf for one's children without stating perpetuity is valid according to Abu Yusuf and becomes for the poor after the children; according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, it is invalid unless perpetuity is specified.
Muhammad's additional requirement (explicit ta'bid) is also noted, but the relied-upon fatwa follows Abu Yusuf on this point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَ لَا يَتِمُ الْوَقْفُ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ حَتَّى يَجْعَلَ اخِرَهُ بِجِهَةٍ لَا تَنْقَطِعُ أَبَداَوَ قَالَ أَبُويُوسفَ إِذَا سَمَّى فِيهِ جهَةً تَنْقَطِعُ جَازَ وَ صَارَ بَعْدَهَا لِلْفُقَرَاءِ وَإِنْ لَمْ يُسَمِهِمْ لَهُمَا أَنَّ مُوْجَبَ الْوَقْفِ زَوَالُ الْمِلْكِ بِدُونِ التَمليك وَأَنَّهُ يَتَأَبَّدُ كَالْعِتْقِ فَإِذَا كَانَتِ الْجِهَةُ يَتَوَهَّمُ اِنْقِطَاعُهَا لَا يَتَوَ فَرْعَلَيْهِ مُقْتَضَاهُ فَلِهَذَا كَانَ التَّوقِيتُ مُبْطِلًا لَهُ كَالتَّوْقِيتِ فِي الْبَيْعِ وَلِأَبِى يُوسُفَ أَنَّ الْمُقْصُودَ هُوَ التَقَرُّبُ إِلَى اللهِ تَعَالَى وَهُوَ مُوَقَرْ عَلَيْهِ لأَنَّ التَّقَرُّبُ تَارَةً يَكُونُ فِى الصَّرِف إِلى جِهَةِ تَنْقَطِعُ وَمَرَةَ بِالصَّرْفِ إِلى جِهَةٍ تَتَابَدُ فَيَصِحُ فِى الْوَجْهَيْن وَقِيلَ إِنَّ التَّابِيْدِ شَرْط بِالْإِجْمَاعِ إِلَّا أَنَّ عِنْدَ أَبِى يُوسُفَ لَا يُشْتَرَطُ ذَكَرُ التَّابِيْدِ لا نَ لَفَظَةَ الْوَقفِ وَالصَّدَقَةِ مُنَيَةٌ عَنْهُ لَمَا بَيَّنَا أَنَّهُ إِزَالَهُ اَلْمُلْكِ يَدُونَ السَّمْلِيْكِ كَالْعِتْقِ وَلِهَذَا قَالَ فِي الْكِتَابِ فِي بَيَانِ قَوْلِهِ وَصَارَ بَعْدَهَا لِلْفُقَرَاءِ وَإِن لَّمْ يُسَمِهـ وهذا هو الصَّحِيحُ وَعِندَ مُحَمَّدٍ ذكرُ التَّابِيْدِ شَرْطَ لِأَنَّ هَذَا صَدَقَةٌ بِالْمَنْفَعَةِ أو بالغَلَةِ وَذَالِکَ قَدْيَكُور فَدْيَكُونُ مُؤقتاً وَقَدْيَكُونُ مُوَبَّدَ افَمُطْلَقَهُ لَا يَنْصَرِفُ إِلَى التَّابِي فَلَا بُدَّ مِنَ التَّنْصِيصِ
He said: Waqf is not completed according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad until he makes its end a channel that does not terminate forever. And Abu Yusuf said: If he names in it a channel that terminates, it is permissible and after that it becomes for the poor even if he did not name them. For them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that the requirement of waqf is removal of ownership without transfer, and it is perpetual like manumission. So when the channel is such that its termination is imagined, its requirement is not fulfilled. Therefore timing it invalidates it, like timing in a sale. For Abu Yusuf is that the purpose is seeking nearness to Allah, and it is achieved [by that] because nearness sometimes is by spending to a channel that terminates and sometimes by spending to a channel that is perpetual, so it is valid in both ways. And it is said that perpetuity is a condition by consensus, except that according to Abu Yusuf it is not required to mention perpetuity because the word waqf and sadaqah are sufficient for it, as we explained that it is removal of ownership without transfer like manumission. Therefore he said in the book in explanation of his statement: 'And after that it becomes for the poor even if he did not name them.' And this is the correct view. And according to Muhammad, mentioning perpetuity is a condition because this is a charity of usufruct or produce, and that sometimes occurs as temporary and sometimes as perpetual, so its absolute form does not refer to perpetuity, so specification is necessary.
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of a waqf that is not explicitly perpetual (mu'abbad). The source text presents the positions of the three major Hanafi imams. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that for a waqf to be complete (tam), the donee must specify a beneficiary category that will not end (e.g., the poor, mosques) because waqf inherently requires perpetuity like 'itq (manumission). If the beneficiary is such that it could terminate (e.g., one's children who may die out), the waqf is invalid unless the surplus goes to the poor. Abu Yusuf holds that even if the beneficiary is temporary, the waqf is valid because the purpose is qurbah (nearness to Allah), which can be achieved even by a temporary benefit. However, he agrees that once the temporary line ends, the property goes to the poor. The text then resolves that the correct view (al-sahih) is that of Abu Yusuf on this point. It also mentions a second layer: Muhammad requires explicit mention of perpetuity because waqf of usufruct can be temporary, while Abu Yusuf holds the word 'waqf' itself implies perpetuity. This is a classic example of usul ikhtilaf regarding whether the term 'waqf' is unambiguous in denoting perpetuity.

Key Terms
تأبيد (ta'bid): Making something eternal or perpetual; here it refers to the condition that a waqf must be for a perpetual benefit.
جهة (jihah): The direction or purpose for which waqf is made; the beneficiary class or cause.
توقيت (tawqit): Limiting something to a fixed time; here it is the act of making a waqf for a limited duration (e.g., 10 years).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in al-Hidayah, what happens to a waqf made for a temporary beneficiary (e.g., 'for my children') without stating the reversion?
A) The waqf is void and property returns to the donor.
B) The waqf is valid and it continues for the children perpetually.
C) The waqf is valid and after the children the property goes to the poor.
D) The waqf is valid and the children own the property after the donor's death.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the mufta bihi is that a waqf is valid even if the designated beneficiary is temporary, and it automatically reverts to the poor upon the beneficiary's extinction.

The Proof of Waqf of Immovable Property from the Sahaba
Ruling with proof from Sahaba practice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on waqf of real estate and identify the proof from the practice of the Companions.

Core Idea
Waqf of land and buildings is valid and recommended, proven by the unanimous practice of the Sahaba.

This lesson explores a foundational ruling in Hanafi waqf law: the permissibility of endowing immovable property ('aqar). The source text, from Al-Hidayah commentary on Al-Quduri, presents a concise ruling backed by one of the strongest proofs in Hanafi fiqh—the collective practice of the Companions of the Prophet ﷺ. We will examine this proof, its authority, and the examples that solidify it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and the Act
What is the act being ruled upon (waqf of 'aqar), and what is the hukm (permissible, recommended)? Note that the text says 'yajuzu' (it is permissible).
The ruling is permissibility, but the commentary indicates it is sunnah muakkadah.
2
Locate the Dalil
What proof does the author cite? The phrase 'because a group of the Companions made waqf of it'.
This is a dalil naqli (transmitted evidence) from the practice of the Sahaba.
3
Understand the Type of Dalil
Why is the action of the Sahaba considered a valid proof in Hanafi usul? Hanafis accept 'Qawl al-Sahabi' as a source of law under certain conditions, especially when there is no known opposition.
The Sahaba's practice, when widespread and not denounced, indicates ijma' or sunnah.
4
Explore the Examples
The commentary provides specific instances: the house of Arqam, the well of Rumah (Uthman), and endowments by Abu Bakr, Umar, Ali, Zubayr. These show the practical application.
These examples reinforce that waqf of real estate was common among the Sahaba.
5
Assess the Authority
What is the weight of this proof? The Hanafi school considers this a strong proof, close to ijma'. The ruling is 'muttafaq alayh' across schools.
This permissibility is unanimously accepted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَيَجُوزُ وَقْفُ العَقَارِ لأَنَّ جَمَاعَةً مِّنَ الصَّحَابَةِ رِضْوَانُ اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِمْ وَقَفُوهُ
He said: Waqf of real estate is permissible because a group of the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them, made waqf of it.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This is a ruling statement with proof (dalil naqli). The author states the ruling that waqf of 'aqar (immovable property such as land and buildings) is permissible. The proof is the practice of a group of Sahaba, implying ijma' or at least established precedent. The Urdu commentary then elaborates with examples: the house of Arqam ibn Abi al-Arqam, which was used by the Prophet for da'wah and later made waqf; the well of Rumah (Bi'r Rumah) purchased and made waqf by Uthman; waqf of Zubayr; and others like Abu Bakr, Umar, Ali. These examples support the permissibility and desirability of waqf of real estate. The authority of this proof is the consensus (or near-consensus) of the Sahaba, which serves as a strong precedent in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
عقار ('aqar): Immovable property, real estate such as land, houses, and buildings.
صحابہ (Sahabah): The Companions of the Prophet Muhammad ﷺ; their actions are a source of legislation (sunnah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary proof given for the permissibility of waqf of real estate in this passage?
A) A verse from the Quran.
B) A hadith from the Prophet.
C) The practice of a group of Sahaba.
D) Logical deduction (qiyas).

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates waqf of immovable property ('aqar) based on the established practice of the Companions, making it a sunnah muakkadah.

8 min
The Condition of Perpetuity in Waqf: Abu Yusuf vs. Muhammad
Defining waqf and discussing whether permanence is a condition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on whether perpetuity must be explicitly mentioned in a waqf and explain the reasoning behind each view.

Core Idea
The word 'waqf' itself implies permanence according to Abu Yusuf, so explicit mention of perpetuity is not required.

Waqf is a central institution of Islamic charity, but what makes a waqf valid? One key issue is whether the endower must explicitly state that the endowment is perpetual. The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement on this point. In this lesson, we will explore the arguments of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani and understand which view became the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the two positions within the Hanafi school: Abu Yusuf holds that explicit mention of perpetuity is not required; Muhammad holds that it is a condition.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
2
Identify the opponent and their proof
For each position, understand the proof. Abu Yusuf argues that the term 'waqf' itself implies permanence, like freeing a slave. Muhammad argues that waqf can be temporary or permanent, so permanence must be stated explicitly.
Muhammad's view is the opposing school in this dispute.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine Muhammad's reasoning: waqf is the endowment of usufruct, which can be for a limited time or forever. Without explicit mention, the default is not necessarily perpetuity.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Abu Yusuf's response is that the very definition of waqf (removing ownership without transferring) inherently means permanence, as it is not a temporary transfer.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if a person says 'I make this property waqf' without saying 'forever', the waqf is valid according to Abu Yusuf, but invalid according to Muhammad.
The later school follows Abu Yusuf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوقف
۲۵۰
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ہفتم
ہے کہ وہ ہو کر ختم ہو جائے۔ اور کبھی اس طرح سے بھی ہوتا ہے کہ اس راہ میں خرچ کر دینے کے بعد وہ ہمیشہ کے لئے باقی رہ جائے ۔ اور وقف ان دونوں ہی صورتوں سے صحیح ہوتا ہے۔ اور بعض مشائخ نے کہا ہے کہ وقف کا ہمیشہ کے لئے ہونا بالاتفاق شرط ہے لیکن اختلاف یہ ہے کہ ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک بیان میں ہمیشہ کے لئے ذکر ہونا شرط نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ لفظ وقف اور صدقہ سے ہی یہ مفہوم ظاہر ہوتا ہے۔ کیونکہ پہلے یہ بیان کر دیا گیا ہے کہ وقف کے معنی یہ ہیکہ کوئی چیز کسی کے ملک میں دیئے بغیر اپنی ملکیت سے نکال دینا۔ پھر ایسا کرنا محدود مدت کے لئے نہیں بلکہ ہمیشہ کے لئے ہونا ۔ جیسا کہ غلام کو آزاد کر دینے میں ہوتا ہے ۔ اسی بناء پر کتاب میں ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کا قول بیان کرنے کے بعد کہا ہے کہ اس طرح کرنے کے بعد بالآخر وہ چیز فقیروں کے واسطے ہو جائے گی ۔ اگر چہ اس وقت فقراء کا نام نہ لیا گیا ہواور یہی قول صحیح ہے۔ اور امام محمد رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزد یک وقف میں ہمیشہ کے لئے بیان کرنا شرط ہے کیونکہ وقف تو کسی چیز کی پیداوار یا منافع کے وقف کرنے کا نام ہے۔ اور یہ بات کبھی مخصوص اور محدود وقت کے لئے ہوتی ہے اور کبھی ہمیشہ کے لئے ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے ہمیشگی کا ذکر کئے بغیر کلام کو مطلق رکھنے سے ہمیشگی مراد نہیں ہو سکتی ہے بلکہ ہمیشگی کو ظاہر کرنے کے لئے اس کو صراحت کے ساتھ بیان کرنا ضروری ہے۔
The Book of Waqf. 250. Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu commentary of Hidaya, Volume Seven. ... (continues) ... And some scholars have said that the perpetuity of waqf is a condition by consensus, but the difference is that according to Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, mentioning perpetuity in the expression is not a condition because the words 'waqf' and 'sadaqah' themselves indicate this meaning. ... And Imam Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, holds that mentioning perpetuity is a condition in waqf because waqf is the name for endowing the produce or benefits of something, and this can be for a specific limited time or forever. Therefore, without mentioning perpetuity, the absolute expression cannot mean perpetuity; rather, to indicate perpetuity, it must be stated explicitly.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether the condition of perpetuity (ta'bid) must be explicitly stated in a waqf. The author defines waqf as removing ownership without transferring it to another's ownership, which inherently implies permanence. Abu Yusuf holds that the terms 'waqf' and 'sadaqah' themselves imply perpetuity, so explicit mention is unnecessary. Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that waqf is essentially about endowing usufruct, which can be temporary or permanent, so permanence must be stated explicitly. The text notes that the relied-upon position is Abu Yusuf's view, as indicated by the phrase 'this is the correct opinion.'

Key Terms
وقف (waqf): Endowment: removing ownership of a property while retaining its corpus and dedicating its usufruct for charitable purposes.
تأبيد (ta'bid): Perpetuity: the condition that waqf must be established forever, not for a limited time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi), is explicit mention of perpetuity necessary for a valid waqf?
A) Yes, it is necessary.
B) No, the word 'waqf' itself implies perpetuity.
C) It depends on the type of property.
D) Only if the endower intends temporary use.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a waqf is valid even without explicit mention of perpetuity because the word 'waqf' itself implies permanence, according to the relied-upon view of Abu Yusuf.

The Permissibility of Waqf of Real Estate
Ruling with proof from Companions' practice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the permissibility of waqf of real estate in the Hanafi school and cite the proof of the Companions' practice as the primary evidence.

Core Idea
Waqf of real estate is permissible and recommended, proven by the continuous practice of the Companions.

Waqf (endowment) is a highly meritorious act in Islam, often associated with mosques and public utilities. However, many students are surprised to learn that waqf of immovable property (real estate) like houses and land is not only permissible but was practiced by the Prophet's Companions for both public and private benefit. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling and its proof from the actions of the Sahaba.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what is being ruled upon and the legal category: waqf of real estate is declared permissible (ja'iz) and recommended (mustahabb).
The text explicitly states 'yajuzu waqf al-'aqar'.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is the practice of a group of Companions who performed waqf of real estate. This is a form of ijma' fi'li (consensus by action).
The author lists specific examples: Arqam, Uthman, Zubayr, Abu Bakr, Umar, Ali.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof establishes the ruling)
The Companions would not perform an act that is impermissible, especially in matters of charity and worship. Their constant practice (tawatur 'amali) indicates the legitimacy of the act.
This reasoning is strong enough to override any potential doubt about the absence of a direct Quranic verse.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (scholarly difference)
There is no significant disagreement among Hanafis on this issue; all consider it permissible and recommended. Some other schools may have minor conditions, but the core is agreed upon.
The passage indicates unanimous approval by the cited Companions.
5
Evaluate the tarjih and modern applicability
The ruling is mufta bihi (operative for fatwa) in the Hanafi school. Today, this allows endowing real estate for educational, medical, or charitable purposes.
The practice of waqf continues globally as a vital Islamic financial institution.

Source Text

قَالَ وَيَجُوزُ وَقْفُ العَقَارِ لأَنَّ جَمَاعَةً مِّنَ الصَّحَابَةِ رِضْوَانُ اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِمْ وَقَفُوهُ
ترجمہ اور عقار (غیر منقولہ جائیداد ) کا وقف جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ صحابہ کرام کی ایک جماعت نے یہ وقف کیا ہے۔ تشریح قال ويجوز .... الخ غير منقولہ جائید اور مین و مکان کا وقف جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ متعد دصحابہ کرام نے وقف کیا ہے۔ ان میں سے ارقم بن ابی الا رقم میں چنانچہ ان کے بیٹے عثمان نے روایت کی کہ میرا باپ چھ آدمیوں کے بعد ساتواں مسلمان ہوا۔ ان کا ایک گھر صفا پر تھا۔ یہ وہی گھر تھا جس میں رسول اللہ رہتے اور لوگوں کو اسلام کی دعوت فرماتے تھے ۔ چنانچہ اس میں کئی آدمیوں کی ایک جماعت اسلام لائی جن میں عمر بن الخطاب بھی تھے ۔ اس وجہ سے اس گھر کا نام دار الاسلام رکھا گیا۔ بعد میں ارتقم نے اسے اپنی اولاد پر وقف کر دیا۔ (الحديث)

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof (dalil) for the permissibility of waqf of real estate ('aqar). The primary evidence is the practice of the Companions (ijma' fi'li). The author lists several notable examples: Arqam's house on Safa (used as a da'wah center), Uthman's purchase of the well of Rumah for public use, Zubayr's waqf, and others. The Prophet's own action of giving a piece of land in charity is also cited. This establishes that waqf of immovable property is a established practice and therefore valid.

Key Terms
عقار ('aqar): Real estate; immovable property such as land and buildings.
حبس (habs): Another term for waqf, especially used for horses and weapons in the path of Allah.

B) The consensus of the Companions who performed waqf of real estate.
C) Qiyas on the waqf of movable property.
D) The Prophet's statement that waqf is only for land.

Key Takeaway
Waqf of real estate is permissible and recommended in the Hanafi school, proven by the established practice of the Companions.

Waqf of Movable Property: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Stating the general rule and introducing an intra-Hanafi exception based on accessoriness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on waqf of movable property, explain the legal reasoning based on accessory (tab'iyyah), and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Movable property cannot be waqf alone, but can be included as an accessory to land.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi disagreement that shaped the school's approach to endowing movable assets. While Abu Hanifa held that only immovable property can be the subject of a valid waqf, his two leading students—Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani—recognized an important exception: when movables are necessary as accessories to land, they may be included in the waqf. Understanding this dispute clarifies the Hanafi concept of tab'iyyah (accessoriness) and its limits.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule
The text opens with Abu Hanifa's absolute ruling: waqf of movable property (manqul) is invalid. Note that 'movable' here means anything that can be transported or relocated.
Abu Hanifa's positions are always a baseline; exceptions come from the Sahibayn.
2
Locate the Exception Introduced by Abu Yusuf
Abu Yusuf states that if a farm is endowed along with its cows and ploughmen (who are slaves of the endower), the waqf of these movables is permissible. The same applies to all farming tools.
The exception is not arbitrary; it is tied to the land's function.
3
Extract the Legal Reasoning (Illah)
The reason (illah) for the exception is 'tab'iyyah' (accessoriness): these movables are subordinate to the land in achieving the intended purpose of cultivation. Just as water is included in the sale of land (even though water alone cannot be sold), and buildings are included in the waqf of land, movables essential to the land's use acquire the same legal status.
This is a qiyas (analogy) based on custom and necessity.
4
Note Muhammad's Reinforcement
Muhammad al-Shaybani agrees with Abu Yusuf, adding a priority argument (awla): since he permits independent waqf of some movables (like horses and weapons, as will be discussed), the inclusion of movables as accessories is even more justified.
Muhammad's comment shows that the exception is not a concession but a logical extension.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi (Operative Ruling)
Although Abu Hanifa's position is the apparent general rule, later Hanafi practice and fatwa have adopted the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. The mufta bihi today is that waqf of movables is permissible when they are customary accessories to the endowed immovable property, and even independently for certain items like horses and weapons.
The tarjih (preference) is based on the majority of later scholars and practical necessity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يَجُوزُ وَقْفُ مَا يُنْقَلُ وَيُحَوَّلُ قَالَ وَهُدًا عَلَى الْإِرْسَالِ قَوْل أَبِي حَنِيفَةً وَقَالَ أَبُويُوسُفَ إِذَا وَقَفَ ضَيْعَةً بِبَقَرِهَا وَأُكَرَتِهَا وَهُمْ عَبِيدُهُ جَازَوَ كَذا سَائِرُ الآتِ الْحِرَاثَةِ لأنَّه تَبعُ الْأَرْضِ فِي تَحْصِيلِ مَا هُوَ الْمَقْصُودُ وَقَدَيَتْبَتُ مِنَ الْحُكْمِ تَبْعَ مَا لَا يَشْتُ مَقْصُودًا كَالشَّرْبِ فِى البَيْعَ وَالْبَنَاءِ فِى الْوَقْفِ وَمُحَمَّدٌ مَعَهُ فِيهِ لِأَنَّه لَمَّا جَازَافَرَادُ بَعْضِ الْمَنْقُولِ بِالوَقفِ عِندَهُ فَلان يَجُوزُ الْوَقْفُ فِيهِ تَبْعا أولى
ترجمہ اور ایسی چیز جو ادھر سے ادھر لے جانے کے قابل ہو یعنی مال منقولہ کو وقف کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ مصنف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے کہا ہے کہ مطلقا نا جائز ہونے کا یہ قول امام ابوحنیفہ رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کا ہے۔ اور ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے کہا ہے کہ اگر کوئی شخص اپنا کھیت اس کے جو تنے والے بیلوں اور ان کا شتکاروں کے جو وقف کرنے والے کے غلام ہیں وقف کیا تو جائز ہے۔ اسی طرح کا شتکاری کے دوسرے سامان بل وغیرہ کا بھی اس کے ساتھ وقف کر دینا جائز ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اصل مقصود یعنی نملہ کے حصول میں یہ چیزیں زمین کے تابع ہوتی ہیں ۔ اور کبھی ایک چیز اس کے مستقل ارادہ سے ثابت نہیں ہوتی ہے مگر وہی چیز دوسرے وقت تابع ہو کر ثابت ہو جاتی ہے۔ جیسے زمین کو فروخت کرنے سے اس کا پانی اس میں داخل ہو جاتا ہے ۔ یعنی جس پانی سے وہ زمین سیراب کیجاتی ہوا گر کوئی صرف اسی پانی کو فروخت کرنا چاہے تو وہ فروخت کے قابل نہیں ہوگا۔ مگر زمین کے ساتھ وہ پانی فروخت ہو جاتا ہے)۔ اور جیسے صرف عمارت کو اس کی زمین کے بغیر وقف کرنا صحیح نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ لیکن زمین کے ساتھ وقف ہو جاتی ہے اور امام محمد رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کا قول بھی اس مسئلہ میں ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے موافق ہے۔ کیونکہ امام محمد رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک جب بعض منقول اشیاء کا وقف تنہا مستقل طور پر جائز ہے تو غیر منقول کے تابع ہو کر بدرجہ اولی وقف جائز ہو گا۔ اسی لئے آگے بیان فرما دیا ہے)
And waqf of what is movable and transportable is not permissible. He said: 'And this, in absolute terms, is the statement of Abu Hanifa.' Abu Yusuf said: 'If a person endows a farm with its cows and its ploughmen, who are his slaves, it is permissible, and likewise the rest of the farming tools, because they are accessory to the land in achieving the intended purpose. And sometimes a ruling can be established as an accessory of what is not independently intended, like the water in a sale and the building in a waqf.' Muhammad agrees with him in this, because when the independent waqf of some movables is permissible according to him, then it is more appropriate that waqf as an accessory is permissible. Therefore he will explain later.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the permissibility of waqf of movable property (manqul). Imam Abu Hanifa's general ruling is that waqf of movables is invalid (la yajuz). However, Abu Yusuf introduces an exception: if the movables are accessories (taba') to a piece of real estate (e.g., cows and tools for farming), then their waqf along with the land is valid. The reasoning is that these items are subordinate to the land in achieving the goal of cultivation. Muhammad al-Shaybani agrees with Abu Yusuf, applying a priority argument (awla): since he permits waqf of some movables independently (such as horses and weapons, as will be discussed), then as accessories it is even more permissible. The text uses the analogy of water included in the sale of land (even though water alone cannot be sold) and a building being included in the waqf of land.

Key Terms
منقول (manqul): Movable property: items that can be transported from place to place.
تبع (taba'): Accessory: something that is legally attached to a principal item, such as tools to land.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi Hanafi position, when is waqf of movable property valid?
A) Only when the movable is attached to the land permanently.
B) When the movable is an accessory to immovable property and customarily included.
C) Always, because all property can be endowed.
D) Only for farming equipment, not for household items.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the general rule is that waqf of movables is invalid, but an exception established by Abu Yusuf and Muhammad allows it when the movables are customary accessories to immovable property.

Waqf of Movables: Custom vs Text in Hanafi and Shafi'i Thought
Inter-madhhab dispute on waqf of movables with intra-Hanafi divergence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on waqf of movable property, distinguish the views of Muhammad al-Shaybani and Abu Yusuf, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the principle of custom (ta'amul).

Core Idea
Waqf of movables is permissible only where custom supports it; the Hanafi school rejects unrestricted analogy to real estate.

This passage from Al-Hidayah examines the permissibility of endowing movable property beyond the well-known case of horses and weapons for jihad. The Hanafi school, represented by Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf, bases permissibility on prophetic precedent and established custom, while Imam al-Shafi'i extends the ruling to any durable movable through analogy. You will explore the istihsan-based reasoning, the intra-Hanafi difference, and the practical consequences of each approach.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on waqf of horses and weapons
Identify the basic ruling: waqf of kurra' (horses) and silah (weapons) is valid based on istihsan due to prophetic practice (Khalid and Talhah). Note that Abu Yusuf agrees on this point.
The term 'kurra' includes camels if used for fighting.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Muhammad extends waqf to any movable item that is customarily endowed (like tools, books, cooking pots). Abu Yusuf restricts to the items with explicit textual proof (horses and weapons). Understand each scholar's reasoning.
Muhammad uses the analogy of istisna' where custom overrides qiyas.
3
Examine the Shafi'i position and its dalil
Al-Shafi'i argues that any durable movable that can be benefited from while the corpus remains can be waqf, by analogy (qiyas) to real estate and to the permitted horses/weapons.
This is the general Shafi'i principle for waqf of movables.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response to Shafi'i
The Hanafi response: waqf of such items is not established from the Prophet's practice, so they remain under the original prohibition of waqf of movables (like dirhams and dinars). Custom (ta'amul) is the only basis for exception, not unrestrained qiyas.
This preserves the default ruling that movables cannot be waqf unless proven otherwise.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Shafi'i school allows waqf of books, tools, and similar items freely. The Hanafi school (following Muhammad) allows only those movable items for which custom has developed, or for which there is a textual basis. This restricts the scope of movable waqf in practice.
Most later Hanafi jurists follow Muhammad's opinion, as stated in the text.

وَ قَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ يَجُوزُ حُبَسُ الكُرّاعِ وَالسّلاح مَعْنَاهُ وَقَفَهُ فِي سَبِيلِ اللهِ وَأَبُو يُوسُفَ مَعَهُ فِيهِ عَلَى مَا قَالُوا وَهُوَ " راستِحْسَانُ وَالْقِيَاسُ أَنْ لَا يَجُوزُ لِمَا بَيَّنَا مِنْ قَبْلُ وَجُهُ الْاِسْتِحْسَانِ الْأَثَارُ الْمَشْهُورَةٌ فِيهِ مِنْهَا قَولُهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ وَ أمَّا خَالِدٌ فَقَدْ حَبِسَ ادْرُعًا وَ أَفْرَا سَالَهُ فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى وَ طَلْحَةُ حَبِسَ دُرُوعَهُ فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى وَيُرْوَى وَأكْرَاعَة وَالْكُرَاحَ الْخَيلُ وَيَدْخُل فِي حُكْمِهِ الْإِبِلُ لِأَنَّ الْعَرَب يُجَاهِدُ ونَ عَلَيْهَا وَكَذَا السَّلَاحُ يُحْمَلُ عَلَيْهَا وَعَن مُحَمَّدٌ أَنَّهُ يَجُوزُوقَفُ مَا فِيهِ تَعَامَل مِنَ الْمُفَوَلَاتِ كَالْفَاسِ وَالْمَرَ وَ القَدُومِ وَالْمَشَارَوَ الجِنَازَةِ وَثِيَابِهَا وَالقُدُورِ وَالْمَرَاحِلَ وَالْمَصَاحِفِ وَعِندَ أَبِى يُوسُفَ لَا يَجُوزُ لأنَّ القِيَاسَ إِنَّمَا يُتَرَكُ بِالنَّصِ وَالنَّص وَرَدَ فِى الْكُرَاعَ وَالسّلَاحِ فَيُقْتَصَرُ عَلَيْهِ وَمُحَمَّدَ يَقُولُ الْقِيَاسُ قَديتَرَكَ بِالتَّعَامِل كَمَا فِي الْإِسْتِصْنَاعِ وَقَدُوحِدَ التَعَامُلُ فِى هَذهِ الأَشْيَاءِ وَعَنْ نَصِيرِ بْنِ يَحْيى إِنَّهُ وَقَفَ كُتُبَهُ الْحَاقَّ بِالْمُصْحَفِ وَهَذا صَحِيحُ لِأَنَّ كُلَّ وَاحِدٍ يُمْسَك لِلدِّينِ تَعْلِيمًا وَتَعَلَمَا وَقِرَاءَةَ وَأكْثَرُ فَقَهَاءِ الْأمْصَارِ عَلى قَوْلِ مُحَمَّدٌ وَمَا لَا تَعَامُل فِيْهِ لَا يَجُوزُ عِنْدَنَا وَفَفَهُ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِى كُلُّ مَا يُمْكِنُ الْإِنْتِفَاعُ بِهِ مَعَ بَقَاءِ أَصْلِهِ وَيَجُوزُ بَيْعَهُ يَجُوزُ وَقَفَهُ لأَنَّهُ يُمْكِنُ الانتفاع به فَأَشْبَهَ الْعَقَارَ وَالْكُرَاعَ وَالسّلَاحَ وَلَنَا أَنَّ الْوَقْفَ فِيهِ لَا يَتَابَ مِنْهُ عَلَى مَا بَيِّنَاهُ فَصَارَ كَالدَّرَاهِم وَالدَّنَا بَيْرِ بِخِلَافِ
And Muhammad said: 'The waqf of horses and weapons is permissible.' Its meaning is: endowing them in the way of Allah. And Abu Yusuf agrees with him in this, as they said. And it is istihsan; the qiyas is that it is not permissible, as we explained earlier. The basis of istihsan is the well-known traditions on this, including his statement (peace be upon him): 'As for Khalid, he endowed his armor and his horses in the way of Allah, the Exalted.' And Talhah endowed his armor in the way of Allah, the Exalted. And it is narrated: 'and his horses' - 'kurra' is horses. And camels enter into this ruling because the Arabs fight on them, and similarly weapons are carried on them. And from Muhammad: he says that the waqf of whatever movable items are customary (like the spade, hoe, adze, saws, bier and its garments, cooking pots, cauldrons, and copies of the Qur'an) is permissible. And according to Abu Yusuf, it is not permissible because qiyas is only abandoned by a text (nas), and the text came only for horses and weapons, so it is limited to them. Muhammad says: qiyas has been abandoned by custom ('amal), just as in the case of istisna'. And custom exists for these items. And from Nasir ibn Yahya: he endowed his books, which are analogous to the copy of the Qur'an, and this is sound because each one is held for religion, teaching, learning, and recitation. And most jurists of the cities follow Muhammad's opinion. And what has no custom, it is not permissible with us. And al-Shafi'i said: 'Everything that can be benefited from while its essence remains, and its sale is permissible, its waqf is permissible, because benefit is possible, so it is analogous to real estate, horses, and weapons.' And we (Hanafis) say: waqf of such items is not established from the Prophet based on what we have explained, so it becomes like dirhams and dinars (which cannot be waqf).
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage covers the permissibility of waqf of horses (kurra') and weapons (silah) for jihad. Imam Muhammad considers it valid based on istihsan (juristic preference) supported by traditions: the Prophet reported that Khalid and Talhah endowed their armor and horses. Abu Yusuf agrees. The qiyas (analogy) would suggest it is not permissible (because movables cannot be waqf), but the text from the Prophet overrides qiyas. Muhammad extends this to all movable items that are customarily used as waqf, like tools, biers, cooking pots, and Qur'ans. Abu Yusuf limits it to the narrated items. Most later scholars follow Muhammad. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that any durable movable that can be used while the corpus remains can be waqf, based on analogy with real estate. The Hanafi response is that waqf of such items is not established from the Prophet's practice, so they remain like dirhams and dinars which cannot be waqf. However, items for which custom has developed are an exception.

Key Terms
كراع (kurra'): Horses (specifically used for warfare).
سلاح (silah): Weapons, such as armor, swords, etc.
تعامل (ta'amul): Customary practice; the established usage among people.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis for Imam Muhammad's permission to waqf movable items like tools and books?
A) Direct Quranic verse.
B) Consensus of the Companions.
C) Customary practice (ta'amul) of the people.
D) Analogy to the waqf of dirhams.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits waqf of movables only where there is textual precedent (horses/weapons) or established custom; unqualified analogy to real estate is rejected.

Waqf of Movable Property: The Accessory Principle
Intra-Hanafi dispute on waqf of movables

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on waqf of movable property and apply the principle of taba'iyya to determine validity when the movable is an accessory to land.

Core Idea
Movable property cannot be endowed alone, but can be as an accessory to land.

This passage addresses a foundational intra-Hanafi dispute on whether movable property (manqul) can be subject to waqf. While Abu Hanifa holds an absolute prohibition, his two disciples Abu Yusuf and Muhammad allow it when the movable is an accessory to land. Understanding this distinction and the principle of taba'iyya (accessoriness) is crucial for correctly applying waqf rulings in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is waqf of movable property (manqul). Abu Hanifa rules it is absolutely invalid. Your task is to note that this is the general principle.
Movable property includes anything that can be transported, like animals, tools, or vehicles.
2
Distinguish the positions of the Sahibayn
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad allow waqf of movables when they are accessories to land. Identify the condition: the movable must be an appurtenance to real estate.
E.g., oxen and ploughs for a farm.
3
Follow Abu Yusuf's analogy
Abu Yusuf likens this to water in a sale and buildings in a waqf: they are valid as accessories despite not being valid independently. Understand the legal reasoning (qiyas).
Al-tābiʿ tābiʿ: the accessory follows the principal.
4
Analyze Muhammad's a fortiori argument
Muhammad argues that since some movables (e.g., horses, weapons) can be endowed independently in his view, allowing them as accessories is even more appropriate. Trace the logic: mā lā yathbutu maqsūdan yathbutu tabaʿan.
This argument strengthens the permissibility as accessory.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position for fatwa is that of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad for accessories. For independent waqf of movables, later Hanafi jurists follow Muhammad's broader view based on custom (taʿāmul).
In practice, many movables like cars or machinery may be validly endowed if customarily used for charitable purposes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يَجُوزُ وَقْفُ مَا يُنْقَلُ وَيُحَوَّلُ قَالَ وَهَذَا عَلَى الْإِرْسَالِ قَوْلُ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ إِذَا وَقَفَ ضَيْعَةً بِبَقَرِهَا وَأَكَرَتِهَا وَهُمْ عَبِيدُهُ جَازَ كَذَا سَائِرُ آلاتِ الْحِرَاثَةِ لِأَنَّهُ تَبَعٌ لِلْأَرْضِ فِي تَحْصِيلِ مَا هُوَ الْمَقْصُودُ وَقَدْ يَثْبُتُ مِنَ الْحُكْمِ تَبَعًا مَا لَا يَثْبُتُ مَقْصُودًا كَالشَّرْبِ فِي الْبَيْعِ وَالْبِنَاءِ فِي الْوَقْفِ وَمُحَمَّدٌ مَعَهُ فِيهِ لِأَنَّهُ لَمَّا جَازَ إِفْرَادُ بَعْضِ الْمَنْقُولِ بِالْوَقْفِ عِنْدَهُ فَلَأَنْ يَجُوزَ الْوَقْفُ فِيهِ تَبَعًا أَوْلَى
And the waqf of what is moved and transferred is not permissible. He said: And this is, unrestrictedly, the statement of Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf said: If one endows a farm with its oxen and its ploughmen, who are his slaves, it is permissible. Likewise, the rest of the ploughing tools, because they are appurtenances to the land in achieving the intended objective. And sometimes a ruling is established as accessory what is not established as an independent object, like water in a sale and a building in a waqf. And Muhammad agrees with him in this, because when it is permissible to make some movable property independently subject to waqf in his view, then it is even more appropriate that waqf should be permissible in it as an accessory.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the validity of waqf of movable property. According to Abu Hanifa, waqf of anything that can be moved (manqul) is absolutely invalid. However, Abu Yusuf allows it when the movable item is accessory to real estate, such as oxen and tools for a farm, because they are necessary for achieving the purpose of the land. He draws an analogy to water being included in the sale of land even though water cannot be sold independently, and to buildings being included in waqf of land even though a building cannot be endowed alone. Muhammad al-Shaybani agrees with Abu Yusuf, arguing that since in his view some movables can be endowed independently (e.g., horses and weapons, as will be discussed), it is even more appropriate that they be valid as accessories. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that waqf of movables as accessories to land is valid, and for independent movables, the permissibility is limited to specific items such as horses and weapons, and by extension items customarily used.

Key Terms
مَنْقُول (manqūl): Movable property that can be transported from one place to another, as opposed to real estate (ʿaqār).
تَبَع (tabaʿ): Accessory or appurtenance; something that follows the main object in legal rulings.
وَقْف (waqf): The permanent dedication of property for charitable purposes, with the corpus preserved and usufruct given to beneficiaries.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Yusuf, when is waqf of oxen and ploughing tools permissible?
A) When they are endowed independently without land.
B) When they are endowed as accessories to a farm or land.
C) When they are endowed for the benefit of horses.
D) They are never permissible.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, waqf of movable property is invalid independently but valid as an accessory to land, following the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.

Waqf — Endowment
