The Waqif's Reserved Benefit and Administration: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute about waqif's self-benefiting condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on a waqif stipulating ghulla or wilaya for himself, identify the evidence for each, and apply the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
A waqif may benefit from his own waqf if he stipulates it—Abu Yusuf's view is the relied-upon position.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a waqif can reserve the produce (ghulla) or administration (wilaya) of his endowment for himself. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani differ fundamentally on the nature of waqf and the validity of such conditions. Understanding their arguments and the school's final tarjih is essential for correctly applying waqf law.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the two views: what does Abu Yusuf rule? What does Muhammad rule? Note that Hilal al-Razi and al-Shafi'i agree with Muhammad.
The mufta bihi is Abu Yusuf's view: condition is valid.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The opposing position within the Hanafi school is Muhammad's. He argues that the condition invalidates the waqf. Understand the basis: waqf as tamlik to Allah.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine Muhammad's dalil: waqf is a donation (tabarru‘) transferring ownership to Allah; stipulating benefit for oneself is contradictory, like reserving a part of a mosque. This is a qiyas argument.
Also mentioned: the difference may stem from the condition of qabd and ifraz.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Abu Yusuf's response: he cites a hadith that the Prophet ate from his own sadaqa (endowed property). This proves that a waqif can benefit by condition. Also, waqf is removal of ownership to Allah, so a condition of benefit does not contradict the essence.
The hadith is the core evidence; the commentator says it supports validity.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Abu Yusuf, a waqif can stipulate to receive income during his life; the waqf is valid. Under Muhammad, such a waqf is null. The school adopts Abu Yusuf's view for fatwa.
Similar rule applies when stipulating for umm walad or mudabbar servants.

قَالَ وَإِذَا جَعَلَ الْوَاقِفُ عُلَّةَ الْوَقْفِ لِنَفْسِهِ أَوْ جَعَلَ الْوِلَايَةَ إِلَيْهِ جَازَ عِنْدَ أَبِي يُوسُفَ قَالَ ذَكَرَ فَضْلَيْنِ شَرْطُ الْعَلَّةِ لِنَفْسِهِ وَجَعْلُ الْوِلَايَةِ إِلَيْهِ أَمَّا الْأَوَّلُ فَهُوَ جَائِزٌ عِنْدَ أَبِي يُوسُفَ وَلَا يَجُوزُ عَلَى قِيَاسِ قَوْلِ مُحَمَّدٍ وَهُوَ قَوْلُ هِلَالٍ الرَّازِي وَبِهِ قَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ وَقِيلَ إِنَّ الِاخْتِلَافَ بَيْنَهُمَا بِنَاء عَلَى الِاخْتِلَافِ فِي اشْتِرَاطِ الْقَبْضِ وَالْإِفْرَازِ وَقِيلَ هِيَ مَسْأَلَةٌ مُبْتَدَأَةُ وَالْخِلَافُ فِيمَا إِذَا شَرَطَ الْبَعْضَ لِنَفْسِهِ فِي حَيَاتِهِ وَبَعْدَ مَوْتِهِ لِلْفُقَرَاءِ وَفِيمَا إِذَا شَرَطَ الْكُلَّ لِنَفْسِهِ فِي حَيَاتِهِ وَبَعْدَ مَوْتِهِ لِلْفُقَرَاءِ سَوَاءٌ وَلَوْ وَقَفَ وَشَرَطَ الْبَعْضَ أَوِ الْكُلَّ لِأُمَّهَاتِ أَوْلَادِهِ وَمُدَبَّرِيهِ مَا دَامُوا أَحْيَاءَ فَإِذَا مَاتُوا فَهُوَ لِلْفُقَرَاءِ وَالْمَسَاكِينِ فَقَدْ قِيلَ يَجُوزُ بِالِاتِّفَاقِ وَقَدْ قِيلَ هُوَ عَلَى الْخِلَافِ أَيْضًا وَهُوَ الصَّحِيحُ لِأَنَّ اشْتِرَاطَهُ لَهُمْ فِي حَيَاتِهِ كَاشْتِرَاطِهِ لِنَفْسِهِ وَجْهُ قَوْلِ مُحَمَّدٍ أَنَّ الْوَقْفَ تَبَرُّعٌ عَلَى وَجْهِ التَّمْلِيكِ بِالطَّرِيقِ الَّذِي قَدَّمْنَاهُ فَاشْتِرَاطُ الْبَعْضِ أَوِ الْكُلِّ لِنَفْسِهِ يُبْطِلُهُ لِأَنَّ التَّمْلِيكَ مِنْ نَفْسِهِ لَا يَتَحَقَّقُ فَصَارَ كَالصَّدَقَةِ الْمُنْفِذَةِ وَشَرَطَ بَعْضَ بُقْعَةِ الْمَسْجِدِ لِنَفْسِهِ وَلِأَبِي يُوسُفَ مَا رُوِيَ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ كَانَ يَأْكُلُ مِنْ صَدَقَتِهِ وَالْمُرَادُ مِنْهَا صَدَقَةُ الْمَوْقُوفَةِ وَلَا يَحِلُّ الْأَكْلُ مِنْهَا إِلَّا بِالشَّرْطِ فَدَلَّ عَلَى صِحَّتِهِ وَلِأَنَّ الْوَقْفَ إِزَالَةُ الْمِلْكِ إِلَى اللَّهِ تَعَالَى عَلَى وَجْهِ الْقُرْبَةِ عَلَى مَا بَيَّنَّاهُ فَإِذَا شَرَطَ الْبَعْضَ أَوِ الْكُلَّ لِنَفْسِهِ فَقَدْ جَعَلَ مَا صَارَ مَمْلُوكًا لِلَّهِ تَعَالَى لِنَفْسِهِ
He said: When the waqif makes the produce (or benefit) of the waqf for himself, or makes the administration to himself, it is permissible according to Abu Yusuf. He said: He mentioned two sections: stipulating the produce for himself and making the administration to himself. As for the first, it is permissible according to Abu Yusuf, and it is not permissible on the basis of the saying of Muhammad, and it is the saying of Hilal al-Razi, and al-Shafi'i said the same. And it is said that the difference between them is based on the difference regarding the condition of delivery (qabd) and separation (ifraz). And it is said that it is an original issue. The disagreement is whether he stipulates part for himself during his life and after his death for the poor, and also whether he stipulates all for himself during his life and after his death for the poor, both are the same. And if he endows and stipulates part or all for his female slaves who are mothers of his children (ummahat awlad) and his mudabbars as long as they are alive, then when they die it is for the poor and needy, it has been said it is permissible by agreement, and it has been said it is also based on disagreement, and that is correct because stipulating for them during his life is like stipulating for himself. The basis of Muhammad's saying is that waqf is a donation in the form of ownership as we have presented, so stipulating part or all for himself invalidates it because ownership from himself is not realized, so it becomes like a sadaqa that is executed, and stipulating part of a mosque for himself. And for Abu Yusuf there is the narration that the Prophet, peace be upon him, used to eat from his sadaqa, and by that is meant the endowed sadaqa, and eating from it is not permissible except by condition, so this indicates its validity. And also because waqf is the removal of ownership to Allah Almighty in the form of a pious act as we have explained, so when he stipulates part or all for himself, he has made what became owned by Allah Almighty for himself.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of a waqf in which the founder (waqif) stipulates that the produce (ghulla) or the administration (wilaya) of the waqf remain for himself, either during his lifetime or permanently. The passage presents the views of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Abu Yusuf permits such a condition, citing a hadith that the Prophet (peace be upon him) would eat from his own sadaqa (referring to an endowed property), which implies that such a stipulation is valid. Muhammad al-Shaybani disallows it, arguing that waqf is a transfer of ownership to Allah (tamlik to Allah), so stipulating benefit for oneself is contradictory—one cannot own something that belongs to Allah. He analogizes it to stipulating part of a mosque for oneself, which is invalid. The difference is sometimes attributed to a disagreement about whether delivery (qabd) and separation (ifraz) are necessary conditions for waqf. The passage also discusses similar cases, such as stipulating for one's umm walad (slave mother) or mudabbar slaves during their lifetime; some say this is agreed upon, but the correct view is that it follows the same disagreement, because stipulating for them during his life is like stipulating for himself. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is Abu Yusuf's view: a waqif may stipulate the produce or administration for himself during his lifetime, as long as after his death it goes to the poor. This is the operative ruling in the school.

Key Terms
الْغُلَّةُ (al-ghullah): The produce, revenue, or benefit generated by the waqf property (e.g., rent, fruits).
الْوِلَايَةُ (al-wilāyah): The administrative authority or trusteeship over the waqf property, including the power to manage and supervise.
الْقَبْضُ وَالْإِفْرَازُ (al-qabḍ wa al-ifrāz): Delivery (taking possession) and separation (segregation of the waqf property from other assets). Some Hanafi scholars consider these conditions for the validity of waqf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi), what is the ruling on a waqif stipulating the produce (ghulla) of the waqf for himself during his lifetime?
A) Invalid, because waqf transfers ownership to Allah
B) Valid, based on a hadith of the Prophet
C) Invalid, unless the waqf is for a mosque
D) Valid only if the waqif is poor

Key Takeaway
A waqif may validly stipulate the produce or administration of his waqf for himself during his lifetime, as per the relied-upon Hanafi position of Abu Yusuf.

Using Broken Parts of Waqf for Repair
Ruling on using broken parts of waqf buildings for repair

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on using broken parts of a waqf for repair and explain why distribution to beneficiaries is prohibited.

Core Idea
Broken parts of a waqf building remain part of the corpus and must be used for repair, not given to beneficiaries.

This lesson examines a key rule in Hanafi waqf law concerning the management of broken or dismantled materials from an endowed building. The passage from al-Hidayah clarifies the obligation to use these materials for the waqf's own repair and the prohibition on distributing them to beneficiaries. Understanding this rule preserves the perpetuity of the endowment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is being ruled upon? The use of broken parts (al-naqd) from a waqf building. The ruling: it is obligatory (wajib) to use them for repair of the waqf if needed.
The hukm level is wajib, not fard, because it is based on the necessity of preserving the waqf.
2
Understand the rationale
Why must the broken parts be used for repair? Because repair is necessary for the waqf to remain perpetually, fulfilling the waqif's purpose.
The ta'lil (reasoning) is that the waqf is intended to last forever (ta'bīd).
3
Apply the exceptions
If immediate repair is not needed, the broken parts must be kept for future use. If they cannot be reused in their original place, they are sold and the price spent on repair.
This is a substitute (badal) for the original object.
4
Note the prohibition and its basis
It is not permissible to distribute the broken parts among the beneficiaries because they are part of the corpus (ʿayn), and beneficiaries only have right to usufruct (manāfiʿ). The corpus belongs to Allah.
This is a key principle: the ʿayn is owned by Allah and cannot be alienated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حَتَّى يَحْتَاجَ إِلى عِمَارَتِهِ فَيَصْرِفُهُ فِيهَا لِأَنَّهُ لَا بُدَّ مِنَ الْعِمَارَةِ لِيَبْقَى عَلَى التَّابِيْدِ فَيَحْصُل مَقْصُودُ الْوَاقِفِ فَإِنَّ مَسَّتِ الْحَاجَةُ إِلَيْهِ فِى الْحَالِ صَرَفَهَا فِيهَا وَإِلَّا أَمْسَكَهَا حَتَّى لَا يَتَعَدَّرُ عَلَيْهِ ذَالِكَ أَوَانِ الْحَاجَةِ فَيَسْطُلُ الْمَقْصُودُ وَإِنْ تَعَدَّرَ إِعَادَةُ عَيْنِهِ إِلى مَوْضِعِهِ بِيْعَ وَصَرَفَ ثَمَنَهُ إِلَى الْمَرَمَّةِ صَرِفًا لِلبَدَل إِلى مَصْرِفِ المُدل وَلَا يَجُوزُ ان تُقَيِّمَهُ يَعْنِي النَّقْضَ بَيْنَ مُسْتَحِقَّى الْوَقْفِ لِأَنَّهُ جُزْء مِنَ الْعَيْنِ وَلا حق الموقوفِ عَلَيْهِمْ فِيهِ وَإنما قُهُمْ فِى الْمَنَافِعِ وَالْعَيْنُ حَقٌّ اللَّهِ تَعَالى فَلَا يُصْرَفُ إِلَيْهِمْ غَيْرَ حَقِهم
Until he is in need of its repair, so he spends it on it, because repair is necessary for it to remain perpetually, so the purpose of the waqif is achieved. If immediate need arises, he spends it on it; otherwise he keeps it so that it is not difficult for him at the time of need and the purpose is thwarted. If returning the exact object to its place is impossible, it is sold and its price is spent on repair, as a substitute for the thing replaced. And it is not permissible to distribute it, meaning the broken parts, among the beneficiaries of the waqf, because it is a part of the corpus, and the beneficiaries have no right in it; rather their right is only in the usufruct, and the corpus is the right of Allah the Exalted, so nothing besides their right should be given to them.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This is a ruling from the matn of al-Quduri or al-Hidayah regarding the management of a waqf when parts of its building become broken or useless. The ruling states that the judge or supervisor must use these broken parts for repair of the waqf itself. If repair is not needed immediately, they should be preserved for future use. Only if it is impossible to reuse the parts in their original place (e.g., they are too damaged) may they be sold and the proceeds used for repair. The key principle is that broken parts remain part of the corpus (ʿayn) of the waqf, not property of the beneficiaries. Beneficiaries only have right to usufruct (manāfiʿ), so they cannot be given the broken parts or their value as distribution. The corpus belongs to Allah, so it cannot be diverted to beneficiaries beyond their entitled benefit.

Key Terms
النَّقْض (al-naqd): The broken materials or debris from a waqf building.
الْعَيْن (al-ʿayn): The physical corpus of the waqf property, as opposed to its usufruct.
الْمَنَافِع (al-manāfiʿ): The usufructs or benefits derived from the waqf property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, what should be done with broken parts of a waqf building if they cannot be reused in their original place?
A) Distribute them among the beneficiaries.
B) Sell them and use the proceeds for waqf repair.
C) Discard them as waste.
D) Keep them for the supervisor's personal use.

Key Takeaway
Broken parts of a waqf (al-naqd) remain part of the waqf corpus and must be used for its repair; they cannot be distributed to beneficiaries.

Waqif Stipulating Benefit or Supervision for Himself
Intra-Hanafi dispute on waqif stipulating benefit or supervision

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on a waqif stipulating benefit or supervision for himself, identify the proofs, and apply the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
A waqif may stipulate to benefit from or supervise his own endowment; this is the relied-upon Hanafi view.

When a person endows property, does he lose all connection to it, or can he retain some rights? This passage from Al-Hidayah presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani on two specific stipulations: taking the benefits (manafi') of the waqf for oneself, and keeping supervisory authority (wilayah). Although Muhammad rejects both as incompatible with the transfer of ownership, Abu Yusuf permits them, and his view is the apparent madhhab. The passage lays out the evidence, including a hadith of the Prophet (ﷺ) and analogies to caravanserais and cemeteries.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two stipulations
Recognize that the passage discusses two distinct issues: (1) the waqif stipulating the benefits of the waqf for himself, and (2) the waqif stipulating the supervisory authority (wilayah) for himself.
Both are treated separately, but the ruling for each is the same per Abu Yusuf.
2
State each imam's position
Note that Abu Yusuf permits both stipulations, while Muhammad al-Shaybani considers them invalid. Hilal al-Razi and al-Shafi'i agree with Muhammad.
The disagreement is internal to the Hanafi school.
3
Grasp the underlying basis
Understand that some link this dispute to the earlier disagreement on whether qabd (possession) and ifraz (segregation) are conditions for waqf validity. Others treat it as an independent issue.
Muhammad requires delivery to an administrator; Abu Yusuf does not.
4
Analyze the proofs
Examine Muhammad's argument: waqf is a transfer of ownership, so stipulating benefit for oneself is like giving to oneself, which invalidates. Then examine Abu Yusuf's response: the hadith of the Prophet eating from his sadaqah, and the analogy of building a caravanserai and lodging there.
Abu Yusuf emphasizes that the waqf becomes Allah's property, so taking from it is not self-transfer.
5
Identify the mufta bihi and practical implications
The passage states that Abu Yusuf's view is the apparent madhhab (zahir al-madhhab) and thus the relied-upon position. The practical difference: per Abu Yusuf, the waqif may take income and manage the waqf; per Muhammad, such stipulations would void the waqf.
The judge may still remove an untrustworthy waqif from supervision.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَإِذَا جَعَلَ الْوَاقِفُ مَنَافِعَ الْوَقْفِ لِنَفْسِهِ أَوْ جَعَلَ الْوِلَايَةَ إِلَيْهِ جَازَ عِنْدَ أَبِي يُوسُفَ. قَالَ: ذَكَرَ فَصْلَيْنِ: شَرْطَ الْمَنَافِعِ لِنَفْسِهِ، وَجَعْلَ الْوِلَايَةِ إِلَيْهِ. أَمَّا الْأَوَّلُ فَهُوَ جَائِزٌ عِنْدَ أَبِي يُوسُفَ، وَلَا يَجُوزُ عَلَى قِيَاسِ قَوْلِ مُحَمَّدٍ، وَهُوَ قَوْلُ هِلَالٍ الرَّازِي، وَبِهِ قَالَ الشَّافِعِي. وَقِيلَ: إِنَّ الِاخْتِلَافَ بَيْنَهُمَا بِنَاءٌ عَلَى الِاخْتِلَافِ فِي اشْتِرَاطِ الْقَبْضِ وَالْإِفْرَازِ. وَقِيلَ: هِيَ مَسْأَلَةٌ مُبْتَدَأَةٌ. وَالْخِلَافُ فِيمَا إِذَا شَرَطَ الْبَعْضَ لِنَفْسِهِ فِي حَيَاتِهِ وَبَعْدَ مَوْتِهِ لِلْفُقَرَاءِ، وَفِيمَا إِذَا شَرَطَ الْكُلَّ لِنَفْسِهِ فِي حَيَاتِهِ وَبَعْدَ مَوْتِهِ لِلْفُقَرَاءِ سَوَاءٌ. وَلَوْ وَقَفَ وَشَرَطَ الْبَعْضَ أَوِ الْكُلَّ لِأُمَّهَاتِ أَوْلَادِهِ وَمُدَبَّرِيهِ مَا دَامُوا أَحْيَاءَ، فَإِذَا مَاتُوا فَهُوَ لِلْفُقَرَاءِ وَالْمَسَاكِينِ، فَقَدْ قِيلَ: يَجُوزُ بِالِاتِّفَاقِ، وَقَدْ قِيلَ: هُوَ عَلَى الْخِلَافِ أَيْضًا، وَهُوَ الصَّحِيحُ لِأَنَّ اشْتِرَاطَهُ لَهُمْ فِي حَيَاتِهِ كَاشْتِرَاطِهِ لِنَفْسِهِ. وَجْهُ قَوْلِ مُحَمَّدٍ: أَنَّ الْوَقْفَ تَبَرُّعٌ عَلَى وَجْهِ التَّمْلِيكِ بِالطَّرِيقِ الَّذِي قَدَّمْنَاهُ، فَاشْتِرَاطُ الْبَعْضِ أَوِ الْكُلِّ لِنَفْسِهِ يُبْطِلُهُ لِأَنَّ التَّمْلِيكَ مِنْ نَفْسِهِ لَا يَتَحَقَّقُ، فَصَارَ كَالصَّدَقَةِ الْمُنْجِزَةِ وَشَرْطِ بَعْضِ بُقْعَةِ الْمَسْجِدِ لِنَفْسِهِ. وَلِأَبِي يُوسُفَ: مَا رُوِيَ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ ﷺ كَانَ يَأْكُلُ مِنْ صَدَقَتِهِ، وَالْمُرَادُ مِنْهَا صَدَقَةُ الْمَوْقُوفَةِ، وَلَا يَحِلُّ الْأَكْلُ مِنْهَا إِلَّا بِالشَّرْطِ، فَدَلَّ عَلَى صِحَّتِهِ. وَلِأَنَّ الْوَقْفَ إِزَالَةُ الْمِلْكِ إِلَى اللهِ تَعَالَى عَلَى وَجْهِ الْقُرْبَةِ عَلَى مَا بَيَّنَّاهُ، فَإِذَا شَرَطَ الْبَعْضَ أَوِ الْكُلَّ لِنَفْسِهِ فَقَدْ جَعَلَ مَا صَارَ مَمْلُوكًا لِلَّهِ تَعَالَى لِنَفْسِهِ، لَا أَنْ جَعَلَ مِلْكَ نَفْسِهِ لِنَفْسِهِ، وَهَذَا جَائِزٌ كَمَا إِذَا بَنَى حَانًا أَوْ سِقَايَةً أَوْ جَعَلَ أَرْضَهُ مَقْبَرَةً وَشَرَطَ أَنْ يَنْزِلَهُ أَوْ يَشْرَبَ مِنْهُ أَوْ يَدْفَنَ فِيهِ. وَلِأَنَّ مَقْصُودَهُ الْقُرْبَةُ، وَفِي التَّصَرُّفِ إِلَى نَفْسِهِ ذَلِكَ. قَالَ ﷺ: نَفَقَةُ الرَّجُلِ عَلَى نَفْسِهِ صَدَقَةٌ. وَلَوْ شَرَطَ الْوَاقِفُ أَنْ يَسْتَبْدِلَ بِهِ أَرْضًا أَخْرَى إِذَا شَاءَ ذَلِكَ فَهُوَ جَائِزٌ عِنْدَ أَبِي يُوسُفَ، وَعِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ الْوَقْفُ جَائِزٌ وَالشَّرْطُ بَاطِلٌ. وَلَوْ شَرَطَ الْخِيَارَ لِنَفْسِهِ فِي الْوَقْفِ ثَلَاثَةَ أَيَّامٍ جَازَ الْوَقْفُ وَالشَّرْطُ عِنْدَ أَبِي يُوسُفَ، وَعِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ الْوَقْفُ بَاطِلٌ، وَهَذَا بِنَاءٌ عَلَى مَا ذَكَرْنَا. وَأَمَّا فَصْلُ الْوِلَايَةِ فَقَدْ نَصَّ فِيهِ عَلَى قَوْلِ أَبِي يُوسُفَ، وَهُوَ قَوْلُ هِلَالٍ أَيْضًا، وَهُوَ ظَاهِرُ الْمَذْهَبِ. وَذَكَرَ هِلَالٌ فِي وَقْفِهِ وَقَالَ: أَقْوَامٌ—إِنْ شَرَطَ الْوَاقِفُ الْوِلَايَةَ لِنَفْسِهِ كَانَتْ لَهُ، وَإِنْ لَمْ يَشْتَرِطْ لَمْ تَكُنْ لَهُ وِلَايَةٌ. قَالَ مَشَايِخُنَا: الْأَشْبَهُ أَنْ يَكُونَ هَذَا قَوْلَ مُحَمَّدٍ، لِأَنَّ مِنْ أَصْلِهِ أَنَّ التَّسْلِيمَ إِلَى الْقَيِّمِ شَرْطٌ لِصِحَّةِ الْوَقْفِ، فَإِذَا سَلَّمَ لَمْ يَبْقَ لَهُ وِلَايَةٌ فِيهِ. وَلَنَا: أَنَّ الْمُتَوَلِّيَ إِنَّمَا يَسْتَفِيدُ الْوِلَايَةَ مِنْ جِهَتِهِ بِشَرْطِهِ، فَيَسْتَحِيلُ أَنْ لَا يَكُونَ لَهُ الْوِلَايَةُ وَغَيْرُهُ يَسْتَفِيدُ الْوِلَايَةَ مِنْهُ. وَلِأَنَّهُ أَقْرَبُ النَّاسِ إِلَى هَذَا الْوَقْفِ فَيَكُونُ أَوْلَى بِوِلَايَتِهِ، كَمَنِ اتَّخَذَ مَسْجِدًا يَكُونُ أَوْلَى بِعِمَارَتِهِ وَنَصْبِ الْمُؤَذِّنِ فِيهِ، وَكَمَنْ أَعْتَقَ عَبْدًا كَانَ الْوَلَاءُ لَهُ لِأَنَّهُ أَقْرَبُ النَّاسِ إِلَيْهِ. وَلَوْ أَنَّ الْوَاقِفَ شَرَطَ وِلَايَتَهُ لِنَفْسِهِ وَكَانَ الْوَاقِفُ غَيْرَ مَأْمُونٍ عَلَى الْوَقْفِ فَلِلْقَاضِي أَنْ يَنْزِعَهَا مِنْ يَدِهِ نَظَرًا لِلْفُقَرَاءِ، كَمَا لَهُ أَنْ يَخْرُجَ الْوَصِيَّ نَظَرًا لِلصِّغَارِ. وَكَذَا إِذَا شَرَطَ أَنْ لَيْسَ لِسُلْطَانٍ وَلَا لِقَاضٍ أَنْ يَخْرُجَهَا مِنْ يَدِهِ وَيُوَلِّيَهَا غَيْرَهُ، لِأَنَّهُ شَرْطٌ مُخَالِفٌ لِحُكْمِ الشَّرْعِ فَبَطَلَ.
He said: And if the waqif makes the benefits of the waqf for himself or makes the supervision to himself, it is permissible according to Abu Yusuf. He said: He mentioned two matters: stipulating the benefits for himself and making the supervision to himself. As for the first, it is permissible according to Abu Yusuf, but not permissible by analogy to the saying of Muhammad, and it is the saying of Hilal al-Razi, and al-Shafi'i also said it. And it was said: The disagreement between them is based on the disagreement regarding the stipulation of possession and segregation. And it was said: It is an original issue. And the disagreement is whether he stipulates part for himself during his life and after his death for the poor, or he stipulates all for himself during his life and after his death for the poor, both are the same. And if he endows and stipulates part or all for his ummahat awlad (slave mothers of his children) and his mudabbars (slaves whose emancipation is delayed) as long as they are alive, then when they die it is for the poor and needy, then it has been said it is permissible by agreement, and it has been said it is also subject to disagreement, and that is the correct view because his stipulation for them during his life is like his stipulation for himself. The reasoning of Muhammad's saying is that waqf is a donation on the basis of transfer of ownership in the manner we have mentioned, so stipulating part or all for himself invalidates it because transfer of ownership from oneself to oneself is not realized, so it becomes like an immediate sadaqah and stipulating part of a mosque's area for himself. And for Abu Yusuf: what is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to eat from his sadaqah, and what is meant is the endowed sadaqah, and eating from it is not lawful except by stipulation, so this indicates its validity. And because waqf is the removal of ownership to Allah the Exalted for the purpose of seeking closeness (qurbah) as we have explained, so if he stipulates part or all for himself, he has made what has become owned by Allah the Exalted for himself, not that he made his own ownership for himself, and this is permissible just as if he built a caravanserai or a drinking place or made his land a cemetery and stipulated that he would lodge there or drink from it or be buried in it. And because his purpose is qurbah, and in the disposal towards himself that is also present. He (peace be upon him) said: The spending of a man on himself is charity. And if the waqif stipulates that he may exchange it for another land whenever he wishes, then it is permissible according to Abu Yusuf, but according to Muhammad the waqf is valid and the condition is void. And if he stipulates an option for himself in the waqf for three days, the waqf and condition are valid according to Abu Yusuf, but according to Muhammad the waqf is void, and this is based on what we mentioned. As for the matter of supervision, he has stated in it the opinion of Abu Yusuf, and it is also the opinion of Hilal, and it is the apparent madhhab. And Hilal mentioned in his waqf and said: Some people said: If the waqif stipulates supervision for himself, it is his; if he does not stipulate, he has no supervision. Our mashayikh said: The more likely is that this is the opinion of Muhammad, because from his principle is that delivery to the administrator is a condition for the validity of the waqf, so if he has delivered, he retains no supervision over it. And for us: The trustee (mutawalli) derives supervision from his side [the waqif] by his stipulation, so it is impossible that he himself has no supervision while someone else derives supervision from him. And because he is the closest person to this waqf, so he is more entitled to its supervision, like one who builds a mosque is more entitled to its maintenance and appointment of the mu'adhdhin in it, and like one who manumits a slave has the wala' (patronage) because he is the closest person to him. And if the waqif stipulates his supervision for himself and the waqif is not trustworthy over the waqf, then the judge may remove it from his hand for the sake of the poor, just as he may dismiss an executor for the sake of minors. Likewise, if he stipulates that no sultan or judge may remove it from his hand and appoint another, that condition is contrary to the ruling of the Sharia, so it is void.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani regarding two issues: (1) whether a waqif (endower) can stipulate that the benefits (manafi') of the waqf go to himself during his lifetime, and (2) whether he can stipulate that he retains the supervision (wilayah) of the waqf. Abu Yusuf permits both, while Muhammad considers them invalid. The passage discusses the basis of their disagreement. Some say it hinges on their differing views on whether possession (qabd) and segregation (ifraz) are conditions for the validity of waqf. Others say it is an independent issue. The text also extends the dispute to stipulations for one's own slave-mothers and mudabbars. Abu Yusuf's proof includes the hadith that the Prophet (ﷺ) used to eat from his sadaqah, indicating that such a stipulation is valid. Muhammad's reasoning is that waqf involves transferring ownership to Allah, so one cannot own something that has become Allah's property. The passage further states that the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Yusuf, and it is the apparent madhhab (zahir al-madhhab). However, the judge may remove an untrustworthy waqif from supervision, and any condition that contradicts Sharia (like preventing the judge from removal) is void.

Key Terms
مَنَافِع الْوَقْف (manāfiʿ al-waqf): The income, usufructs, or benefits generated by an endowment.
الْوِلَايَة (al-wilāyah): The supervisory authority over the waqf, including management and administration.
الْقَبْض وَالْإِفْرَاز (al-qabd wa al-ifrāz): Possession and segregation of the waqf property from the waqif's other assets.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab's relied-upon position, if a waqif stipulates that he will retain supervision (wilayah) of his endowment, what is the ruling?
A) The stipulation is invalid and the waqf is void.
B) The stipulation is valid and he retains supervision.
C) The supervision automatically goes to the judge regardless of stipulation.
D) The stipulation is valid only if the waqif is trustworthy.

Key Takeaway
A waqif may validly stipulate to take benefits from his own endowment or to supervise it, and this is the relied-upon Hanafi view.

Waqf — Endowment
intermediate
8 min
Stipulating Benefit for Oneself in Waqf
Ruling and proof for waqif retaining benefit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on a waqif stipulating benefit for himself, explain the proofs of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, and identify the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
A waqif may stipulate benefit for himself; Abu Yusuf permits, Muhammad prohibits.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether a person who establishes a waqf (endowment) can legally stipulate that he himself will enjoy its usufruct or income. The two leading disciples, Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad, hold opposing views. Understanding their proofs and the ultimately preferred opinion is essential for correctly applying waqf law.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi positions
Identify what Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say regarding a waqif stipulating benefit for himself. Abu Yusuf says it is permissible (jā'iz); Muhammad says it is invalid (bātil).
Remember, this is an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.
2
Identify the point of disagreement
Determine the underlying basis for the difference. It stems from whether delivery (qabd) to a trustee is a condition for the validity of waqf. Muhammad requires it; Abu Yusuf does not.
Some scholars treat this as an independent issue.
3
Analyze each proof
Examine the dalīl for each position. Abu Yusuf cites the hadith that spending on oneself is charity (sadaqah) and analogy with using a public inn one built. Muhammad analogizes to conditional charity, which is invalid.
Note the Hanafi use of qiyas and istihsan.
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: If the waqif stipulates income for himself, according to Abu Yusuf the waqf is valid and he may take the income. According to Muhammad, the waqf is invalid.
This affects actual fatwa and court rulings.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The scholars of Balkh and Sadr al-Shahid preferred Abu Yusuf's view, and it is the relied-upon position for fatwa.
Tarjīh is based on strength of dalīl and practical necessity.

طریقہ سے وقف کرنا بھی باطل ہے۔ اور امام ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کی دلیل وہ حدیث ہے جس میں روایت ہے کہ رسول اللہ اپنے صدقہ میں سے کھاتے تھے ۔ تو اس صدقہ سے مراد وقف ہے۔ حالانکہ وقف کے مال سے کھانا حلال نہیں ہے ، مگر شرط کے ساتھ ۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ وقف میں شرط کر لینا صحیح ہے۔ لیکن یہ حدیث کہیں نہیں ملی ہے۔ بلکہ روایت یہ ہے کہ رسول اللہ کے صدقہ یعنی وقف میں سے آپ کے اہل و عیال عام دستور کے مطابق کھاتے تھے ) ۔ ( رواه ابن ابی شيبه ) اس دلیل سے کہ وقف کے معنی ہیں کسی چیز سے اپنی ملکیت زائل کر کے تقرب کے طور پر اللہ تعالیٰ کی ملک میں دینا جیسا کہ ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں ۔ پس اگر واقف نے وقف کی آمدنی سے اس کی کچھ یا کل آمدنی اپنی ذات کے لئے شرط کی تو جو چیز اللہ تعالیٰ کی مملوک ہو چکی تھی اس کی اپنی ذات کے لئے شرط کی۔ اور ایسی بات نہیں ہے کہ اپنی ملک کو اپنے واسطے مخصوص کر لیا ہے۔ اور اللہ تعالیٰ کی مملوک چیز کو اپنے لئے شرط کر لینا جائز ہے۔ جیسے کوئی خان ( سرائے خانہ ( یا سقایہ ( سبیل ) بنائے یا کسی زمین کو قبرستان بنادے اور اس میں یہ شرط لگائے کہ اس سرائے میں خود بھی ٹھہرے گا یا اس سبیل اور سقایہ سے خود بھی پانی پئے گا یا اس قبرستان میں اپنا مردہ بھی دفن کرے گا تو یہ جائز ہوتا ہے اور اس دلیل سے کہ اس کا مقصود اس وقف سے تقرب الہی ہے۔ اور یہی بات اپنی ذات پر خرچ کرنے سے بھی حاصل ہوتی ہے۔ چنانچہ رسول اللہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ آدمی کا اپنی ذات پر خرچ کرنا اس کے حق میں صدقہ ہے ( اور اپنی بیوی و اولا دو خادم پر خرچ کرنا بھی اس کے واسطے صدقہ ہے۔ ابن ماجہ اور نسائی نے اس کی روایت کی ہے۔ اور اس کی اسناد عمدہ وجید ہے)۔ (ابن حجر اور حضرت ابو سعید خدری نے مرفوع روایت کی ہے کہ جس نے حلال طریقہ سے کوئی مال کمایا اور اس سے اپنی ذات کے لئے کھانا یا کپڑا بنایا ی مخلوق الہی کو دیا تو یہ اس کے لئے زکوۃ ہے۔ جیسا کہ صحیح ابن حبان اور حاکم میں ہے ۔ اس باب میں اور بھی بہت کی حدیثیں ہیں ۔
Except that he makes his own property for himself, and this is permissible, just as if he builds an inn or a water station, or makes his land a cemetery, and stipulates that he will stay in it, or drink from it, or be buried in it, because his purpose is closeness (to Allah), and in spending on himself that is the same. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'A man's spending on himself is charity.' Translation of Quduri (may Allah have mercy on him): He said that if the endower kept the usufruct and produce of the endowment for himself, or reserved the guardianship of the endowment for himself, then according to Imam Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him) it is permissible. The scholars of Balkh (may Allah have mercy on them) adopted this opinion, and Sadr al-Shahid (may Allah have mercy on him) used to give fatwa accordingly. The author (may Allah have mercy on him) said that Shaykh Quduri (may Allah have mercy on him) mentioned two things in this: first, stipulating usufruct and produce for oneself; second, stipulating becoming trustee for oneself. The detail of the first condition is that it is permissible according to Imam Abu Yusuf. And by analogy to the statement of Imam Muhammad, it appears that it is not permissible, which is the statement of Bilal al-Razi (may Allah have mercy on him). (Correctly, he is Hilal ibn Yahya al-Ra'i, may Allah have mercy on him). And Imam Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) also has this opinion. Some scholars said that this difference between the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is based on their disagreement regarding the condition of possession and delivery. Some others said that it is an independent and new issue. Then this difference exists in both scenarios: whether he stipulates part of the income for himself for life and after his death for the poor, or the entire income for himself for life and then after his death for the poor; there is no difference. And if he stipulates that part or all of the income will be for his umm walad or mudabbar slaves as long as they live, and after their death for the poor and needy, it is said that this condition is unanimously permissible. And it is said that there is also disagreement between the two companions in this. And this is correct, because stipulating income for umm walad and mudabbar slaves for their lives is like stipulating for oneself, so the previous disagreement applies. The reason for Imam Muhammad’s statement is that the meaning of waqf is to make someone the owner of a portion in the aforementioned manner with benevolence, i.e., to seek closeness to Allah Almighty. Therefore, stipulating to reserve a little or all of the income for oneself would nullify it, because making oneself the owner is not realized. So this issue becomes like conditional charity – giving some wealth to a poor person as charity on condition that part of it is for the giver, or making part of land a mosque on condition that part of it remains for the maker (these are invalid). For this reason, waqf in the mentioned manner is invalid. The proof of Imam Abu Yusuf is the hadith that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to eat from his charity. By that charity, waqf is meant. Even though eating from waqf property is not lawful except with a condition. This shows that stipulating a condition in waqf is correct. But this hadith is not found; rather, the narration is that the Prophet’s family used to eat from his charity (i.e., waqf) according to common practice. (Reported by Ibn Abi Shaybah). And from this proof: the meaning of waqf is to divest ownership of something and give it to Allah’s ownership for closeness, as we have explained. So if the endower stipulates part or all of the income for himself, he stipulates for himself something that has become Allah’s property. It is not that he reserved his own property. And stipulating Allah’s property for oneself is permissible, just as if someone builds a inn or a water station or makes a piece of land a graveyard and stipulates that he himself will stay in that inn, or drink from that water station, or bury his dead in that graveyard, then it is permissible. And from the proof that his purpose is closeness to Allah through this waqf, and that same purpose is also achieved by spending on himself. Indeed, the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'A man's spending on himself is charity.' (And spending on his wife, children, and servant is also charity. Ibn Majah and Nasa'i reported it, and its chain is excellent and good). (Ibn Hajar and Abu Sa'id al-Khudri reported in marfu' form: 'Whoever earns lawful wealth and from it makes food or clothing for himself or gives it to Allah's creation, it is zakat for him.' As in Sahih Ibn Hibban and Hakim. There are many other hadiths on this topic.)
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute with proofs on whether a waqif (endower) can stipulate benefit from the waqf for himself. The matn (from Quduri) states that it is permissible, comparing it to building a public inn or water station where the builder uses it. The proof is the hadith that spending on oneself is charity. The Urdu commentary clarifies that there are two distinct issues: (1) stipulating usufruct for oneself, and (2) stipulating guardianship (wilaya) for oneself. For the first, Abu Yusuf holds it permissible; Muhammad's view, by qiyas, makes it invalid because waqf requires complete transfer of ownership to Allah. The difference is traced to whether delivery (qabd) to a trustee is a condition for validity of waqf. Abu Yusuf says no, so stipulation is valid; Muhammad says yes, so it is invalid. The commentary also notes that some scholars treat this as an independent issue. If a waqif stipulates for his umm walad or mudabbar slaves, the same disagreement applies. Abu Yusuf's strongest proof is that the Prophet used to eat from his own waqf, but the hadith is weak; the author prefers the analogy of building a mosque and using part for oneself. The lesson emphasizes that the intention of qurba (closeness) is the basis, and spending on oneself can also be qurba.

Key Terms
وقف (waqf): An endowment dedicated to Allah by removing ownership of the property and dedicating its usufruct for charitable purposes.
واقف (waqif): The person who establishes the waqf (endower).
قرابت (qurbah): An act of drawing near to Allah, i.e., a pious deed intended to attain His pleasure.
نفقة (nafaqah): Spending on maintenance, including food, clothing, and shelter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position in this passage, what is the ruling if a waqif stipulates that he will keep the income of his waqf for himself during his lifetime?
A) The waqf is invalid and the income must go to charity.
B) The waqf is valid and the income belongs to the waqif as stipulated.
C) The waqf is valid but the stipulation is void.
D) The waqf is suspended until the waqif's death.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a waqif may validly stipulate benefit for himself from his waqf; Abu Yusuf's view is the mufta bihi.

Stipulating Substitution in Waqf: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on condition to exchange waqf land

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad on istibdal in waqf and identify the practical consequence of their disagreement.

Core Idea
Abu Yusuf allows the waqif to stipulate substitution by istihsan; Muhammad voids the condition but preserves the waqf.

This passage presents a disagreement between two leading Hanafi imams regarding a condition in waqf that allows the endower to exchange the property. Understanding this dispute illuminates the role of istihsan in Hanafi jurisprudence and the tension between strict legal principles and practical flexibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the condition
Recognize that the waqif is stipulating a right to exchange the waqf land for another property whenever he wishes. The act is the stipulation itself, not the waqf.
The condition is an additional term attached to the waqf deed.
2
State Abu Yusuf's position and its basis
According to Abu Yusuf, this condition is permissible (ja'iz) by istihsan (juristic preference). Istihsan allows departure from strict qiyas (analogy) to avoid hardship or achieve a better outcome.
The text does not give a specific proof, but Abu Yusuf relies on the general principle of istihsan.
3
State Imam Muhammad's position
Imam Muhammad holds that the waqf itself is valid (ja'iz) but the condition to substitute is void (batil). He argues that waqf is perpetual and inalienable; a condition allowing substitution contradicts this nature.
Muhammad treats the condition as null, leaving the original waqf property unchanged.
4
Analyze the underlying principles
Abu Yusuf's view prioritizes the waqif's need and flexibility (istihsan), while Muhammad's view prioritizes the classical principle of waqf perpetuity. This shows how different usul lead to different furu'.
Both positions derive from valid Hanafi methodologies.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Abu Yusuf, the waqif may exercise the condition and exchange the property; under Muhammad, the condition is ignored, so the original waqf remains. A mufti must know which view is operative in practice.
Later Hanafi practice often adopts Abu Yusuf's view in cases of genuine need.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ شَرَطَ الْوَاقِفُ أَنْ يَسْتَبْدِلَ بِهِ أَرْضًا أَخْرَى إِذَاشَاء ذَالِكَ فَهُوَ جَائِرٌ عِنْدَ أَبِي يُوْسُفَ وَعِندَ مُحَمَّدِ الْوَقْفُ جَائِرُ وَالشَّرطُ بَاطِلُّ إذا وقف کرنے والے نے یہ شرط کی ہو کہ جب چاہے گا اس زمین کے عوض دوسری زمین بدل لے گا۔ تو امام ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک استحسانا جائز ہے۔ اور امام محمد رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک وقف جائز ہے۔ اور یہ شرط باطل ہے۔
And if the endower stipulates that he may substitute it with another land whenever he wishes, then it is permissible according to Abu Yusuf, and according to Muhammad the waqf is valid and the condition is void. If the endower stipulates that whenever he wishes he will exchange this land for another land, then according to Imam Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him) it is permissible by istihsan. And according to Imam Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) the waqf is valid and the condition is void.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the condition of istibdal (substitution) in waqf. Imam Abu Yusuf, by istihsan (juristic preference), holds that such a condition is valid, meaning the waqif can exchange the waqf property for another. Imam Muhammad holds that the waqf itself is valid, but the condition to substitute is void, so the waqf remains with the original property and the condition is ineffective. The difference may stem from their views on whether a condition that contradicts the nature of waqf (perpetuity) can be valid. Abu Yusuf allows it based on practical need (istihsan), while Muhammad adheres strictly to the principle that waqf property is inalienable.

Key Terms
استبدال (istibdal): The act of substituting or exchanging waqf property for another property.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that allows departing from strict qiyas for a more equitable ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is Imam Muhammad's ruling if a waqif stipulates the right to substitute the waqf land?
A) The waqf is invalid.
B) The waqf is valid but the condition is void.
C) Both the waqf and condition are valid.
D) The waqf is suspended until the substitution is made.

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of stipulating substitution in waqf depends on which Hanafi imam's view is adopted; the condition does not necessarily void the waqf.

Condition Allowing Exchange of Waqf Land
Ruling on condition allowing exchange of waqf land.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on the condition of istibdal in waqf and explain the basis of their difference.

Core Idea
In waqf, a condition allowing exchange is valid by istihsan (Abu Yusuf) but void per Zahir al-Riwayah (Muhammad).

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a waqif can stipulate the right to exchange the waqf property. While Imam Muhammad holds that such a condition is void because waqf is perpetual, Imam Abu Yusuf permits it based on istihsan, prioritizing benefit over strict analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
The issue is the validity of a condition in a waqf deed that allows the waqif to exchange the endowed land for another at his discretion.
This condition is known as istibdal.
2
State Abu Yusuf's position
Imam Abu Yusuf rules that both the waqf and the condition are valid, relying on istihsan (juristic preference).
Istihsan here overrides strict qiyas to avoid hardship and allow benefit.
3
State Muhammad's position
Imam Muhammad rules that the waqf is valid but the condition is void, adhering to the principle that waqf is perpetual and cannot be rescinded by the waqif.
This is the position recorded in Zahir al-Riwayah.
4
Understand the basis of difference
The difference stems from conflicting priorities: preserving the perpetuity of waqf (Muhammad) versus allowing flexibility for the waqif's benefit (Abu Yusuf).
Both rely on valid Hanafi sources: text (Zahir al-Riwayah) and istihsan.
5
Note the practical consequence
According to Abu Yusuf, the waqif may later exchange the property; according to Muhammad, he cannot, and the condition is null.
The waqf remains binding in both views.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اگر وقف کرنے والے نے یہ شرط کی ہو کہ جب چاہے گا اس زمین کے عوض دوسری زمین بدل لے گا۔ تو امام ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک استحسانا جائز ہے۔ اور امام محمد رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک وقف جائز ہے۔ اور یہ شرط باطل ہے۔
If the waqif (endower) has made a condition that whenever he wishes he will exchange this land for another land. Then according to Imam Abu Yusuf, it is permissible by istihsan (juristic preference). And according to Imam Muhammad, the waqf is valid, and this condition is void.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of a condition in a waqf (endowment) that allows the waqif to exchange the waqf property (istibdal) for another piece of land at his discretion. Imam Abu Yusuf considers both the waqf and the condition valid, based on istihsan (juristic preference), meaning he gives priority to the benefit that may come from allowing exchange. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, however, holds that the waqf itself is valid but the condition of exchange is void, meaning the waqf is binding and cannot be undone by exchange at the will of the waqif. The text does not elaborate on the reasoning here, but the general Hanafi principle is that once a waqf is perfected, the property is transferred to Allah's ownership and cannot be exchanged except for a valid reason (like the land becoming useless) with judicial permission. Abu Yusuf's view allows greater flexibility for the waqif to change the property to something more beneficial.

Key Terms
استبدال (istibdal): Exchange of waqf property for another property.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; deviating from a strict analogy for a stronger reason.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, what is the status of a waqf where the waqif has stipulated that he may exchange the land for another?
A) The waqf is void.
B) The waqf is valid and the condition is also valid.
C) The waqf is valid but the condition is void.
D) The waqf is valid only if the qadi approves the exchange.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a condition allowing exchange in waqf is valid according to Abu Yusuf (by istihsan) but void according to Muhammad (strict adherence to waqf perpetuity).

Allocating Waqf Income to Umm Walad and Mudabbar: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on waqf condition validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the disagreement between Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf regarding the validity of reserving waqf income for one's umm walad or mudabbar, and evaluate the evidence each imam uses.

Core Idea
Conditioning waqf benefit for one's own dependents is disputed: Abu Yusuf permits it; Muhammad invalidates it as self-benefit.

This passage delves into a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute: can a waqif (founder) stipulate that the income of his waqf (endowment) be given to his umm walad (slave mother of his child) or mudabbar (slave with deferred freedom) during their lifetimes, and only thereafter to the poor? The two great disciples of Abu Hanifa, Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, differ on this point. Understanding their arguments sharpens our grasp of the legal nature of waqf and the scope of valid conditions within it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
What is the exact condition being debated? The waqif stipulates that the income goes to his umm walad/mudabbar while they live, then to the poor. The disagreement is whether this condition is valid.
2
State Imam Muhammad's position and proof
Imam Muhammad holds the condition invalid, analogizing it to conditioning benefit for oneself, which would void the waqf. Identify his analogies (conditional charity, conditional mosque) and his reasoning that waqf means transferring ownership to Allah.
3
State Imam Abu Yusuf's position and proof
Imam Abu Yusuf holds the condition valid. Identify his evidences: a hadith about the Prophet eating from his sadaqah (interpreted as waqf), analogy to public utilities (inns, water stations) where the founder may benefit, and hadiths on spending on oneself being charity.
4
Analyze the textual critique of Abu Yusuf's hadith
The passage notes that the hadith about the Prophet himself eating from his waqf is not found; the authentic narration is that his family ate from it. How does this affect the strength of Abu Yusuf's proof?
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If the condition is valid (Abu Yusuf), the waqf is valid and the income is given to the umm walad/mudabbar during their lives. If invalid (Muhammad), the waqf is void or the condition is void and the income goes directly to the poor. This shows how the dispute impacts real-world application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فرق نہیں ہوگا۔ اور اگر وقف میں یہ شرط کی ہو کہ آمدنی سے کچھ یا سب کی سب اپنی ام ولد یا مدبروں کے واسطے ہو گی جب تک کہ وہ زندہ رہیں لیکن ان کے مرجانے کے بعد وہ آمدنی فقراء اور مساکین کے لئے ہو جائے گی۔ تو کہا گیا ہے کہ یہ شرط بالاتفاق جائز ہے۔ اور کہا گیا ہے کہ اس میں بھی صاحبین کا اختلاف ہے۔ اور یہی صحیح ہے ۔ کیونکہ ام ولد اور مدبروں کی زندگی تک کے لئے آمدنی اور پیداوار کو مخصوص کرنے کی شرط کرنا ایسا ہے ۔ جیسے اپنی ذات کے لئے شرط کرنا ہے ( تو گزشتہ اختلاف جاری ہو گیا۔ اور امام محمد رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے قول کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ وقف کے معنی ہیں کسی پر احسان کرتے ہوئے مذکورہ بالا طریقہ سے کسی جز کا مالک بنا دینا۔ یعنی اللہ تعالیٰ عزوجل کی جناب میں تقرب حاصل کرنے کے لئے ۔ لہذا اس میں تھوڑی سی آمدنی یا پوری کی پوری آمدنی کو اپنی ذات کے لئے مخصوص کر لینے کی شرط کرنا اس کو باطل کر دے گا۔ کیونکہ خود اپنی ذات کو مالک بنا دینا متحقق نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ تو یہ مسئلہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے صدقہ منفذ و۔ یعنی کسی فقیر کو بطور صدقہ کچھ مال اس شرط پر دینا کہ اس میں سے کچھ اسی دینے والے کے لئے ہے۔ جیسے زمین کے کچھ حصہ کو مسجد بنا دینا اس شرط کے ساتھ کہ اس کا کچھ حصہ خود اسی بنا دینے والے کے لئے ہے (حالانکہ یہ دونوں صورتیں باطل ہیں ) اس لئے مذکور طریقہ سے وقف کرنا بھی باطل ہے۔ اور امام ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کی دلیل وہ حدیث ہے جس میں روایت ہے کہ رسول اللہ اپنے صدقہ میں سے کھاتے تھے ۔ تو اس صدقہ سے مراد وقف ہے۔ حالانکہ وقف کے مال سے کھانا حلال نہیں ہے ، مگر شرط کے ساتھ ۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ وقف میں شرط کر لینا صحیح ہے۔ لیکن یہ حدیث کہیں نہیں ملی ہے۔ بلکہ روایت یہ ہے کہ رسول اللہ کے صدقہ یعنی وقف میں سے آپ کے اہل و عیال عام دستور کے مطابق کھاتے تھے ) ۔ ( رواه ابن ابی شیبه ) اس دلیل سے کہ وقف کے معنی ہیں کسی چیز سے اپنی ملکیت زائل کر کے تقرب کے طور پر اللہ تعالیٰ کی ملک میں دینا جیسا کہ ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں ۔ پس اگر واقف نے وقف کی آمدنی سے اس کی کچھ یا کل آمدنی اپنی ذات کے لئے شرط کی تو جو چیز اللہ تعالیٰ کی مملوک ہو چکی تھی اس کی اپنی ذات کے لئے شرط کی۔ اور ایسی بات نہیں ہے کہ اپنی ملک کو اپنے واسطے مخصوص کر لیا ہے۔ اور اللہ تعالیٰ کی مملوک چیز کو اپنے لئے شرط کر لینا جائز ہے۔ جیسے کوئی خان ( سرائے خانہ ( یا سقایہ ( سبیل ) بنائے یا کسی زمین کو قبرستان بنادے اور اس میں یہ شرط لگائے کہ اس سرائے میں خود بھی ٹھہرے گا یا اس سبیل اور سقایہ سے خود بھی پانی پئے گا یا اس قبرستان میں اپنا مردہ بھی دفن کرے گا تو یہ جائز ہوتا ہے اور اس دلیل سے کہ اس کا مقصود اس وقف سے تقرب الہی ہے۔ اور یہی بات اپنی ذات پر خرچ کرنے سے بھی حاصل ہوتی ہے۔ چنانچہ رسول اللہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ آدمی کا اپنی ذات پر خرچ کرنا اس کے حق میں صدقہ ہے ( اور اپنی بیوی و اولا دو خادم پر خرچ کرنا بھی اس کے واسطے صدقہ ہے۔ ابن ماجہ اور نسائی نے اس کی روایت کی ہے۔ اور اس کی اسناد عمدہ وجید ہے)۔ (ابن حجر اور حضرت ابو سعید خدری نے مرفوع روایت کی ہے کہ جس نے حلال طریقہ سے کوئی مال کمایا اور اس سے اپنی ذات کے لئے کھانا یا کپڑا بنایا ي مخلوق الہی کو دیا تو یہ اس کے لئے زکوۃ ہے۔ جیسا کہ صحیح ابن حبان اور حاکم میں ہے ۔ اس باب میں اور بھی بہت کی حدیثیں ہیں ۔
There will be no difference. And if in the waqf this condition is made that some or all of the income will be for his umm walad or mudabbar as long as they are alive, but after their death the income will be for the poor and needy. So it has been said that this condition is unanimously permissible. And it has been said that in this too there is disagreement among the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). And this is correct. Because making a condition to allocate the income and produce specifically for the umm walad and mudabbar during their lifetime is like making a condition for one's own self (so the previous disagreement applies). And the reason for Imam Muhammad's statement is that the meaning of waqf is to make someone the owner of a part through the mentioned method while doing a favor, i.e., to seek closeness to Allah Almighty. Therefore, making a condition to specify a little or all of the income for one's own self would invalidate it, because making one's own self the owner is not realized. So this issue becomes like a 'sadaqah munaffadh' (a charity with strings attached): i.e., giving some money to a poor person as charity on the condition that some of it is for the giver himself, like making part of a land a mosque on the condition that part of it is for the one who made it (both these forms are void). Therefore, making a waqf in the mentioned way is also void. And the proof of Imam Abu Yusuf is the hadith in which it is narrated that the Messenger of Allah used to eat from his sadaqah. By sadaqah here is meant waqf. Although eating from waqf property is not permissible except with a condition. From this it is understood that making a condition in waqf is valid. But this hadith is not found anywhere. Rather, the narration is that the family of the Messenger of Allah used to eat from his sadaqah, i.e., waqf, according to the common practice. (Narrated by Ibn Abi Shaybah). With this proof: because the meaning of waqf is to remove one's ownership from something and give it into the ownership of Allah as a means of closeness, as we have explained. So if the waqif conditions some or all of the income for his own self, then he has conditioned for himself something that has already become owned by Allah. And it is not the case that he has reserved his own property for himself. And conditioning something that belongs to Allah for oneself is permissible. Like if someone builds a khan (inn) or saqaya (water station) or makes a piece of land a cemetery and stipulates that he himself will stay in that inn, or drink water from that water station, or bury his dead in that cemetery, this is permissible. And with this proof: that his purpose in this waqf is closeness to Allah, and this same purpose is also achieved by spending on himself. Thus the Messenger of Allah said: 'A man's spending on himself is charity for him, and spending on his wife, children, and servant is also charity for him.' (Ibn Majah and Nasa'i narrated it, and its chain is excellent and good). (Ibn Hajar and Abu Sa'id al-Khudri narrated it marfu'an: 'Whoever earns wealth in a lawful manner and spends it on food or clothing for himself, or gives it to Allah's creatures, it is zakat for him.' As in Sahih Ibn Hibban and al-Hakim. There are many other hadiths in this chapter.)
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the validity of a condition in a waqf (endowment) that its income be allocated first to the waqif's umm walad (slave mother of his child) or mudabbar (slave whose freedom is deferred) during their lifetimes, then to the poor after their death. The text first notes that some say this condition is unanimously permissible, but then clarifies that the correct view is that there is a disagreement between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. Imam Muhammad argues that such a condition is like conditioning the income for oneself, which is invalid because waqf means transferring ownership to Allah for His sake, and reserving benefit for oneself contradicts that. He analogizes it to a charity with strings attached (sadaqah munaffadh) or making a mosque with a condition that part of it remains for oneself—both are void. Imam Abu Yusuf, on the other hand, relies on a hadith that the Prophet ate from his sadaqah (interpreted as waqf), and analogizes it to permissible conditions in public utilities like inns, water stations, or cemeteries where the founder may benefit himself. He also cites hadiths on the virtue of spending on oneself and family. The text indicates that the hadith cited by Abu Yusuf is not actually found, and the authentic narration is that the Prophet's family ate from his waqf, not the Prophet himself. The Hanafi position is that the condition is valid according to Abu Yusuf and invalid according to Muhammad, with the mufta bihi (relied-upon position) not explicitly stated but the text leans towards acknowledging the difference.

Key Terms
وقف (waqf): Endowment: removing ownership from property and dedicating it to Allah's causes with the corpus preserved.
ام ولد (umm walad): A female slave who has borne a child to her master; she becomes free upon his death.
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave whose freedom is deferred until the master's death (by tadbir).
صدقہ منفذ (sadaqah munaffadh): A charity with strings attached, where the donor retains some benefit. Hanafi law considers such a charity void.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, why is it invalid to condition waqf income for one's umm walad or mudabbar during their lives?
A) Because they are not eligible to receive waqf benefits.
B) Because it is analogous to conditioning the income for oneself, which contradicts the nature of waqf as transfer of ownership to Allah.
C) Because the hadith cited by Abu Yusuf is weak.
D) Because umm walad and mudabbar are already entitled to maintenance from the waqif.

Key Takeaway
The validity of a condition in waqf benefitting the waqif's dependents is disputed between Imam Muhammad (invalid) and Imam Abu Yusuf (valid), with both positions rooted in sound Hanafi methodology.

The Three-Day Option in Waqf: Abu Yusuf vs. Muhammad
Intra-Hanafi ruling on conditional option in waqf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding a conditional option in waqf and explain the underlying principle that leads to their disagreement.

Core Idea
A conditional option in waqf is either permissible (Abu Yusuf) or invalidates the waqf (Muhammad), based on the nature of waqf as immediate and irrevocable.

This lesson examines a specific intra-Hanafi disagreement: when a person makes a waqf but reserves a three-day option to revoke it. Is the waqf valid with the condition, or does the condition render it void? The answer depends on how each imam views the inherent nature of waqf as an act of devotion that must be immediate and binding.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and the condition
The waqif stipulates a three-day period during which he can decide whether to finalize the waqf or cancel it. This is a conditional option (khiyar) attached to the endowment.
2
State Imam Abu Yusuf's ruling and reasoning
Imam Abu Yusuf holds that both the waqf and the condition are permissible. He analogizes it to his earlier position that a waqif may condition the produce/income for himself during his lifetime. Since waqf is like a sadaqah, conditions should be honored.
3
State Imam Muhammad's ruling and reasoning
Imam Muhammad holds that the condition is invalid because it contradicts the perpetual and irrevocable nature of waqf. Since the condition is integral, the entire waqf becomes void. He does not permit self-benefiting conditions in waqf.
4
Trace the ikhtilaf to the foundational principle
The disagreement stems from a broader principle: Abu Yusuf permits conditions that benefit the waqif as long as they do not contradict the essence of waqf, while Muhammad insists that waqf must be immediately binding without any self-interest.
This is the same disagreement mentioned in the previous lesson on conditioning produce for oneself.
5
Determine the thamarah (practical consequence)
Under Abu Yusuf's view, the waqf is valid and the option can be exercised; under Muhammad's view, the waqf is void from the start, so no property is transferred. The mufta bihi in later Hanafi practice is often Muhammad's position, making the waqf void.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اگر وقف میں اپنے لئے تین دن کی شرط کی۔ یعنی اس زمین کے وقف کرنے یا نہ کرنے کے بارے میں ابھی تین دنوں تک مجھے اختیار ہے ۔ تو امام ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک وقف اور شرط دونوں جائز ہیں۔ لیکن امام محمد رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزد یک وقف باطل ہے۔ ان کا یہ اختلاف اسی بناء پر ہے جو ہم پہلے بیان کر چکے ہیں ( یعنی وقف کرتے وقت اس کی پیداوار اور آمدنی کو اپنی زندگی تک کے لئے شرط رکھنا امام ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک جائز ہے اس لئے تین دن کے اختیار رکھنے کی شرط بھی جائز ہوگی ۔ اور امام محمد رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک وہ جائز نہیں ہے تو یہ بھی جائز نہیں ہے )۔
If in the waqf a condition of three days is made for himself, i.e., regarding the waqf of this land or not, I have an option for three days. Then according to Imam Abu Yusuf, both the waqf and the condition are permissible. But according to Imam Muhammad, the waqf is void. This difference of theirs is based on what we have previously explained (i.e., conditioning the produce and income for oneself during lifetime is permissible according to Imam Abu Yusuf, therefore the condition of a three-day option will also be permissible. And according to Imam Muhammad, that is not permissible, so this is also not permissible).
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage addresses the validity of a condition in a waqf that reserves a three-day period for the waqif to decide whether to finalize the endowment or not (an option to revoke). Once again, we see the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad. Imam Abu Yusuf permits both the waqf and the condition, analogizing it to the previous case of conditioning income for oneself during one's life, which he also permits. Imam Muhammad, who disallows the previous condition, therefore also declares the option condition invalid; and since the condition is integral to the waqf in this case, the waqf itself becomes void. The text explicitly ties this ruling to the foundational difference between the two imams regarding whether a waqf can include any self-benefiting condition. Abu Yusuf views such conditions as permissible because waqf is akin to sadaqah where conditions are honored; Muhammad views them as inconsistent with the nature of waqf as perpetual and irrevocable.

Key Terms
خيار (khiyar): Option, right to rescind a contract within a specified period.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the practical consequence of Imam Muhammad's view on a three-day option in waqf?
A) The waqf is valid but the option is void.
B) The waqf is valid only if the option is exercised within three days.
C) The waqf is void because the condition of option invalidates it.
D) The option is valid but only for land waqf.

Key Takeaway
The validity of a conditional option in waqf depends on the imam: Abu Yusuf permits both waqf and condition; Muhammad declares the waqf void due to the condition's inconsistency with waqf's irrevocability.

The Waqif's Right to Appoint Himself as Mutawalli: Intra-Hanafi Dispute and Qadi's Override
Intra-Hanafi dispute on self-trusteeship in waqf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two main Hanafi positions on whether a waqif can condition his own trusteeship, identify the mufta bihi view, and explain the qadi's authority to remove an unfit mutawalli.

Core Idea
A waqif loses all authority over his waqf; conditioning his own trusteeship is invalid per the preferred Hanafi view.

This passage addresses a key intra-Hanafi dispute: can the founder of a waqf appoint himself as the trustee (mutawalli)? The text presents the permissive view of Imam Abu Yusuf and Hilal al-Ra'y, then shows that the later mashayikh prefer Imam Muhammad's restrictive position. It further clarifies that even if the condition were valid, the qadi has the overriding authority to remove an unfit mutawalli, ensuring the beneficiaries' welfare.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core legal question
What exactly is being disputed? Is it permissible for a waqif to make a condition (shart) that he himself become the mutawalli of his own waqf?
The waqif's ownership ceases upon waqf; the question is whether he can reserve management authority.
2
Map the intra-Hanafi positions
State the views of Abu Yusuf/Hilal (permissive) and Imam Muhammad (restrictive). Note that al-Quduri records the permissive view as 'zahir al-madhhab'.
The permissive view is also supported by Hilal al-Ra'y in his book al-Waqf.
3
Examine the proofs for each side
Identify the analogies (qiyas) used for the permissive view: the mosque builder and the manumitter. Then identify Imam Muhammad's principle: waqf requires handover to a manager, severing the waqif's connection.
The permissive view argues from the waqif's greater care; the restrictive view from the nature of waqf as permanent transfer.
4
Understand the tarjih (preference)
The mashayikh prefer Imam Muhammad's view. Explain that they consider it 'more likely' (شبہ زیادہ بہتر) and thus the mufta bihi.
This tarjih is based on the principle that waqf must be complete and irrevocable.
5
Apply the qadi's supervisory role
Even if one follows the permissive view, the qadi can remove an unfit waqif-mutawalli. Conditions conflicting with Shari'ah (like preventing removal) are void.
The qadi's authority is analogous to removing an unfit guardian of orphans.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اب دوسرے مسئلہ (ولایت کی بحث ) یعنی اپنے آپ کے لئے متولی بننے کی شرط کرنے کا بیان ہوگا۔ تو اس مسئلہ میں قدوری رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے اس بات کی تصریح کردی ہے کہ امام ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک یہ جائز ہے۔ اور ہلال الرائی رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کا بھی یہی قول ہے۔ اور ظاہر المذہب بھی یہی ہے۔ ہلال رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے اپنی کتاب الوقف میں لکھا ہے کہ علماء کی ایک جماعت نے کہا ہے کہ اگر وقف کرنے والے نے اپنی بھلائی کے خیال سے قاضی کو اختیار ہوگا کہ اس وقف کو اس کے قبضہ سے نکال دے۔ جیسے کسی نے اپنے بعد اپنی یتیم اولاد کے لئے کسی کو وصی بنادیا جو اس کی پوری دیکھ بھال کرے حالانکہ وہ دیندار قابل اعتماد نہیں ہے تو اس کے بارے میں بھی قاضی کو اختیار ہوتا ہے کہ ان یتیم بچوں کا خیال کر کے اس وصی کو بے اختیار کر دے اور کسی دوسرے دیانتدار ذمہ دار کو ان کا ذمہ دار بنادے۔ اسی طرح اگر وقف کرنے والے نے یہ شرط کی ہو کہ کسی بادشاہ یا قاضی کو یہ اختیار نہیں ہو گا اس وقف کو میرے قبضہ سے نکال کر اس پر کسی دوسرے شخص کو متولی بنادے ۔ حالانکہ اس وقف کرنے والے کے ظاہری حالات کی بناء پر اس وقف پر اس کی طرف سے اطمینان نہیں ہو تو بھی قاضی کو اختیار ہو گا کہ اس کے قبضہ سے نکال کر کسی دوسرے کو متولی مقرر کر دے کیونکہ وقف کرنے والے کی یہ شرط . شرعی حکم اور مصلحت کے مخالف ہے۔ اس بناء پر خود وہ شرط ہی باطل ہوگئی۔
Now the second issue (discussion of wilayah), i.e., the ruling on making a condition for oneself to become mutawalli (trustee). So in this issue, al-Quduri has clarified that according to Imam Abu Yusuf, this is permissible. And Hilal al-Ra'y also has this same statement. And the apparent madhhab (zahir al-madhhab) is also this. Hilal wrote in his book al-Waqf that a group of scholars said that if the waqif made a condition to remain mutawalli for himself, then he will remain mutawalli and will have wilayah. And if he did not make such a condition, then he will not have wilayah, i.e., he will not remain mutawalli. Our mashayikh said that it seems more likely (شبہ زیادہ بہتر) that it should be according to the statement of Imam Muhammad. Because according to Imam Muhammad, as a principle, for the validity of waqf it is a condition that it be handed over to a manager (munazzim) and a trustee (qayyim). So when the waqif handed it over to the trustee and mutawalli, then his wilayah in the waqf ceased to remain. And our proof is that the trustee gained wilayah from the waqif through a condition; it is impossible that the waqif himself does not have wilayah and yet another person gains wilayah from him. And also with this proof: that the waqif has more connection and sympathy with this waqf than all other people. Therefore, his wilayah to become the mutawalli of this waqf is better. Just like if someone built a mosque, he is more entitled (awla) in its maintenance, construction, and appointing its mu'adhdhin. And just like if someone freed a slave, the wala' of that slave belongs to the manumitter, because the manumitter has the most connection and closeness. And if the waqif reserved for himself the right to be mutawalli of his waqf and made a condition, while he is not trustworthy in terms of trusteeship, i.e., he is not religious, to the extent that there is no confidence from his side in the matter of this waqf, then the qadi has the authority, considering the welfare of the poor, to remove this waqf from his possession. Just like if someone appointed a guardian after him for his orphan children to take full care, but that guardian is not religious and trustworthy, then the qadi also has the authority, considering the orphans, to remove that guardian and appoint another trustworthy person. Similarly, if the waqif made the condition that no king or qadi will have the authority to remove this waqf from my possession and appoint another person as mutawalli, even though based on the apparent circumstances of the waqif there is no confidence from his side, then also the qadi has the authority to remove him from his possession and appoint another as mutawalli, because this condition of the waqif contradicts the Shari'ah ruling and public interest. On this basis, the condition itself becomes void.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage discusses the second issue regarding wilayah (authority/trusteeship) in waqf: whether the waqif (endower) can condition that he himself be the mutawalli (trustee/manager) of his own waqf. The text begins by stating that according to Imam Abu Yusuf and Hilal al-Ra'y, and the apparent madhhab (zahir al-madhhab), this is permissible. Hilal al-Ra'y in his al-Waqf states that a group of scholars said if the waqif conditions his own trusteeship, he gets it; otherwise, he does not. However, the mashayikh (later scholars) of the Hanafi school have expressed that the more likely (شبہ زیادہ بہتر) position is that of Imam Muhammad, i.e., the waqif loses all authority once he completes the waqf. This is because for a valid waqf, the property must be transferred to a manager (qayyim) or trustee, and upon such transfer the waqif's connection is severed. The text then presents the proof for the contrary view (supporting the waqif's capability) using arguments: (1) Since the mutawalli derives his authority from the waqif, it is impossible that the waqif himself lacks that authority. (2) The waqif has more concern and care for the waqf than anyone else, so he is most suitable, analogous to a builder of a mosque being most entitled to maintain it, or the manumitter having closest relationship (wala') to the freed slave. The passage then addresses the scenario where the waqif is dishonest or not religious: even if he conditions his own trusteeship, the qadi has the authority to remove him and appoint another, because the condition contradicts the Shari'ah's concern for the welfare of the beneficiaries. The qadi's authority overrides even a condition that no one else can remove him. The qadi's power is compared to that over a guardian of orphans who is unfit; the qadi can remove him. This passage combines an intra-Hanafi dispute with a ruling on the qadi's overriding authority.

Key Terms
ولایت (wilayah): Authority or trusteeship over the waqf property and its management.
متولی (mutawalli): Trustee or manager appointed to administer the waqf according to the waqif's conditions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view of the Hanafi mashayikh, what happens to the waqif's authority (wilayah) after he completes the waqf?
A) He retains full authority as mutawalli if he conditions it.
B) He loses all authority regardless of any condition.
C) He retains authority only if the qadi approves.
D) He retains authority for three days, then loses it.

Key Takeaway
The waqif cannot retain trusteeship after establishing a valid waqf; the qadi may remove an unfit mutawalli even if the deed states otherwise.

Waqif Appointing Himself as Mutawalli: The Hanafi Debate
Intra-Hanafi dispute on validity of waqif's condition to be mutawalli

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on waqif self-appointment as mutawalli and explain the reasoning behind each using the proofs cited in the text.

Core Idea
A waqif can stipulate to be his own mutawalli? Abu Yusuf says yes, Muhammad says no—authority cannot transfer from one who has none.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether a waqif (endower) can validly stipulate that he himself will be the mutawalli (administrator) of the waqf. The difference turns on the nature of authority in waqf: can the waqif retain control after transferring the property? We follow the debate between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, with the proofs each side uses, and see how the later school evaluates the positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
Determine exactly what is being contested: the validity of the waqif's condition to serve as mutawalli of his own waqf.
This is not about the waqf itself but about a condition attached to it.
2
State Abu Yusuf's position and his proof
Recount Abu Yusuf's view that both the waqf and the condition are valid. Identify his proofs: logical necessity (the mutawalli derives authority from the waqif, so the waqif must have authority) and analogy (mosque builder, manumitter).
Abu Yusuf's view is supported by al-Quduri and Hilal al-Ra'y and is the zahir al-madhhab.
3
State Muhammad al-Shaybani's position and his proof
Recount Muhammad's view that the waqf is invalid if such a condition is stipulated. Identify his proof: waqf requires handing over control to an administrator; after handover, the waqif's authority ceases.
Muhammad's view is considered more likely (ashbah) by the mashayikh.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response and rebuttal
Examine how Abu Yusuf's supporters rebut Muhammad's argument: it is impossible for the mutawalli to derive authority from someone who lacks it; also the waqif has the strongest connection to the waqf.
Both sides use qiyas and logical reasoning.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
Identify the practical difference: if the condition is valid, the waqif remains mutawalli; if invalid, the waqf may be void. Then note which view is the mufta bihi (operative for fatwa) according to the text.
The text indicates the mashayikh preferred Muhammad's view, but the zahir al-madhhab is Abu Yusuf's.

اختیار ہے ۔ تو امام ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک وقف اور شرط دونوں جائز ہیں۔ لیکن امام محمد رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزد یک وقف باطل ہے۔ ان کا یہ اختلاف اسی بناء پر ہے جو ہم پہلے بیان کر چکے ہیں ( یعنی وقف کرتے وقت اس کی پیداوار اور آمدنی کو اپنی زندگی تک کے لئے شرط رکھنا امام ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک جائز ہے اس لئے تین دن کے اختیار رکھنے کی شرط بھی جائز ہوگی ۔ اور امام محمد رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک وہ جائز نہیں ہے تو یہ بھی جائز نہیں ہے )۔

اب دوسرے مسئلہ (ولایت کی بحث ) یعنی اپنے آپ کے لئے متولی بننے کی شرط کرنے کا بیان ہوگا۔ تو اس مسئلہ میں قدوری رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے اس بات کی تصریح کردی ہے کہ امام ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک یہ
